Talaq — Divorce
advanced
15 min
Advanced Maintenance as a Gift: The Hanafi Dispute and Its Ruling
Intra-Hanafi dispute on advanced maintenance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on recovery of advanced maintenance, explain the analogy to gifts (hiba), and apply the mufta bihi ruling to cases of death or irrevocable divorce.

Core Idea
Advanced maintenance is a gift (silah), not a wage — once received, it cannot be reclaimed.

The Hanafi school faced a critical question: if a husband pays his wife's maintenance in advance, and the marriage ends before the period expires, may he recover the unused portion? This lesson unpacks the intra-madhhab disagreement, the reasoning that led to the relied-upon fatwa, and its application when the father makes the payment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed ruling
What is advanced maintenance (nafaqah mu'ajjal)? When does the husband seek recovery? The core dispute is whether it is a wage (iwad) for availability or a gift (silah).
The ruling affects both death and divorce scenarios.
2
Trace the positions within the Hanafi school
Abu Hanifa held it is a wage recoverable proportionally; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) held it is a gift not recoverable. Identify the basis for each.
The fatwa is on the Sahibayn's view.
3
Analyse the Hanafi proof for the Sahibayn's position
The analogy to hiba (gift): once delivered and received, ownership transfers irrevocably. Similarly, advanced maintenance is a silah, not an iwad.
This is a qiyas-based reasoning.
4
Apply the ruling when the father pays
If the husband's father pays the wife's maintenance, the same rule applies: the father cannot reclaim after divorce or death, following Abu Yusuf's view.
The father is in the same position as the son.
5
Note the later controversy on revocable divorce
Some later scholars (e.g., al-Ramli) argued for recovery in revocable divorce to prevent abuse, but the relied-upon view is non-recovery.
The text advises caution (tahammul) at the time of fatwa.

ولهما أنها صلة وقد اتصل بها القبض ولا رجوع في الصلات بعد الموت لانتهاء حكمها كما في الهبة وفتح القدير، والفتوى على قولهما، وجعله الولوالجي وأصحاب الفتاوى قول أبي يوسف قالوا والفتوى عليه. وشمل ما إذا كان المعجل الزوج أو أباه لما في الولوالجية وغيرها : أبو الزوج إذا دفع نفقة امرأة ابنه صرح بالموت اتفاقاً يكفينا مؤنة رده فيقال له لو كان يسقط بالموت لما صح التكفيل به فنقول : كان القياس ذلك لكن استحسن صحة التكفيل شفقة عليهن وامتثالاً لوصية الشارع بهن فذا مما خرج عن الأصل ضرورة، وجعله الموت من العوارض دون الطلاق تحكم بلا ريب . وفي الثالث بأن قوله «أنه في البدائع بأنه يبطل سائر الحقوق مردود لأن سائر» يجيء بمعنى جميع فتكون القضية جزئية قصد بها سلب العموم لا عموم السلب ويكفي فيه تعلقه بالمهر فقط، وأيضاً يمكن حمل الحقوق التي لا تسقط بالطلاق على المهر ونفقة ما دون الشهر ونفقة استدين عليها بأمر فلا يبعد إطلاق جميع الحقوق عليها ثم قال : ثم إن نسبته الخصاف إلى زاد الطلاق من عنده أن أراد أنه لم يستنبطه من كلام المشايخ المتقدمين وأصولهم المعتمدة فهو جراءة عظيمة على هذا الإمام الذي قال عنه الإمام الحلواني إنه كبير في العلم يليق الاقتداء به والذي يتعين المصير إليه أن يقال يتأمل عند الفتوى كما يقع وجرت به عادة المشايخ رحمهم الله تعالى في هذا المقام فإن هذه الرواية لم يظهر ضعفها، كيف وقد أفتى بها الشيخان الصدر الشهيد والمرغيناني وذكرت في المتون كالوقاية والنقاية والإصلاح والغرر وغيرها، وظهر ضعف الوجوه التي قوى بها خلاف تلك الرواية ولهذا توقفت كثيراً في الفتوى بالسقوط مع ما ظهر لي من الأبحاث المذكورة وظفرت بنقل صريح في تصحيح عدم السقوط في خزانة المفتين فليتأمل عند الفتوى وفي الجواهر : إنه لا ينبغي أن يفتي بسقوطها بالطلاق الرجعي لئلا يتخذها الناس وسيلة لقطع حق النساء .اهـ. كلام المقدسي رحمه الله تعالى. فقد رجع إلى ما قاله المؤلف رحمه الله وإن قال أخوه في النهر فيه نظر وبين وجهه الرسلي ببعض ما مر وقال: إن المؤلف قد أفتى في فتاويه بالسقوط .اهـ. والذي اعتمده في منح الغفار ما في جواهر الفتاوى . من أن الفتوى السقوط بالرجعي واقتصر عليه القهستاني. وقال الشيخ علاء الدين: واستحسنه محشي الأشباه. وبالسقوط مطلقاً أفتى شيخنا الرملي لكن صحح الشرنبلالي في شرحه للوهبانية ما بحثه في البحر قال : وهو الأصح . ورد ما ذكره ابن الشحنة فتأمل عند الفتوى .اهـ. وهو يشعر بميله إلى ما بحثه المؤلف، وقد علمت تصحيحه وعبارة الزيلعي محتملة لأن يكون المراد بما صححه هو. هذا كما فهمه الشرنبلالي فاستدل بها وليست صريحة فيما حمله عليها المؤلف بل المتبادر منها الأول لما يعلم من مراجعتها. والحاصل أنه قد اختلف الإفتاء والتصحيح في هذه المسألة فينبغي كما قال بعض الفضلاء أن يتأمل عند الفتوى بأن ينظر في حال الرجل هل فعل ذلك تخلصاً من النفقة أو لسوء اخلاقها على عدم مثلاً.
ثم طلقها الزوج ليس للأب أن يسترد ما دفع لأنه لو أعطاها الزوج والمسألة بحالها لم يكن له ذلك عند أبي يوسف وعليه الفتوى، فكذا إذا أعطاها أبو الزوج اهـ. وشمل الموت والطلاق لما ذكرناه، وكذا في الخانية: ولو عجل لها ثم طلقها لم يكن له أن يسترد، وفي فتح القدير : والموت والطلاق قبل الدخول سواء، وفي نفقة المطلقة إذا مات زوجها اختلفوا؛ قيل ترد، وقيل لا تسترد بالاتفاق لأن العدة قائمة في موته ؛ كذا في الأقضية. فعلى هذا لا ينبغي أن يقيد كلام المصنف بموت أحدهما كما فعله الزيلعي بل تجعل مستقلة، ووجهه أنها صلة لزوجته ولا رجوع فيما يهبه لزوجته والعبرة لوقت الهبة لا لوقت الرجوع فالزوجية من الموانع من الرجوع كالموت ودفع الأب كدفع ابنه فلا إشكال .
قوله : (ويباع القن في نفقة زوجته) يعني إذا كان تزوجه بإذن المولى لأنه دين وجب في ذمته لوجود سببه وقد ظهر وجوبه في حق المولى فيتعلق برقبته كدين التجارة في العبد التاجر ومراده عند عدم الفداء فإن للمولى أن يفديه لأن حقها في النفقة لا في عين الرقبة فلو مات العبد سقطت، وكذا إذا قتل في الصحيح لأنه صلة، وكذا المهر، ولم أرهم صرحوا هنا بأن المرأة إذا اختارت استسعاءه في النفقة دون بيعه أن لها ذلك أم لا، لكن صرحوا في المأذون له للتجارة إذا لحقه دين واختار الغرماء استسعاءه دون بيعه أن لهم ذلك؛ ذكره الزيعلي في المأذون فينبغي أن يكون هنا كذلك. وينبغي أن المرأة إذا اختارت استسعاءه لنفقتها كل يوم يكون لها ذلك أيضاً. قيدنا بإذن المولى لأنه لو تزوج بغير إذن المولى لا يباع في النفقة لعدم وجوبها لعدم صحة النكاح ولذا لم يقيد المصنف بالإذن لأن عند عدمه لم تكن زوجة لتجب لها النفقة، وكذا المهر لا يباع فيه ولو دخل بها لعدم ظهوره في حق المولى، وإنما يطالب به بعد عتقه . وقيد بالقن وهو العبد الذي لا حرية فيه بوجه عند الفقهاء. وفي اللغة العبد إذا هو وأبواه يستوي فيه الاثنان والجمع والمذكر والمؤنث كما في شرح النقاية، لأن المكاتب والمدير وأم الولد لا يباعون فيها لعدم جواز البيع وإنما عليهم السعاية إلا إذا عجز المكاتب فإنه يباع لزوال المانع . وقيد بنفقة زوجته لأن نفقة أولاده لا تجب عليه، سواء كانت الزوجة حرة أو أمة، أما إذا كانت حرة فلأن الأولاد أحراراً تبعاً لها والحر لا يستوجب النفقة على العبد إلا الزوجة، وإن كانت المرأة أمة فنفقة الأولاد على مولى الأمة وإن كانت نفقة الأم على العبد لأن الأولاد تبع للأم في الملك فتكون نفقة الأولاد على المالك لا على الزوج؛ كذا في ملك
قوله : (وفي نفقة المطلقة الخ قال الرملي : استفيد منه ومما في الذخيرة من قوله «لو عجل الزوج لها نفقة مدة ثم مات أحدهما قبل مضي المدة لم يرجع عليها ولا في تركتها في قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف : وقال محمد: يرفع عنها بحصته ما مضى ويجب رد الباقي إن كان قائماً، وقيمته إن كان مستهلكاً الخ». جواب حادثة الفتوى طلقها بائناً وعجل لها نفقة تسعة أشهر فأسقطت سقطاً بعد
And for them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is a gift, and the receipt has been connected to it, and there is no return of gifts after death because their ruling ends, as in a gift. And in Fath al-Qadir, the fatwa is on their statement. Al-Walwaliji and the authors of fatawa made it the statement of Abu Yusuf, saying the fatwa is upon it. And it includes whether the one who advanced payment is the husband or his father, as in al-Walwalijiyya and others: The father of the husband if he pays the maintenance of his son's wife... (continues with the text).
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether advanced maintenance can be recovered if the marriage ends by death or divorce. The core issue: is advanced maintenance a wage for being available (as Abu Hanifa held) or a gift (silah) as Abu Yusuf and Muhammad held? The latter view, that it is a gift and thus non-recoverable once received, is the basis of the fatwa. The author then extends this to the case of the father paying his son's wife's maintenance, ruling that the father also cannot reclaim it after divorce, following Abu Yusuf's view. The passage then delves into a later controversy: does this non-recovery apply to revocable divorce (talaq raj'i) as well? Some later scholars, like al-Ramli, opined that it does not, to prevent abuse. The author advises caution (yata'ammal 'inda al-fatwa). Next, the ruling on selling a slave for his wife's maintenance is explained: the slave can be sold only if he married with his master's permission, as the obligation of maintenance then becomes a debt attached to his person. Finally, the passage discusses the maintenance of a divorced woman if the husband dies, noting a difference of opinion on whether advanced maintenance is recoverable from her estate. The relied-upon view is that it is not recoverable because the iddah period continues after death, and the payment is a gift to the wife.

Key Terms
الصلة (al-silah): A gift or donation, as opposed to a wage or compensation. Advanced maintenance is considered a silah, not an iwad.
الرجوع (al-ruju'): Recovery or return of property; here, the husband's claim to get back the advanced maintenance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon fatwa in the Hanafi school, can a husband reclaim advanced maintenance paid to his wife if she dies before the period ends?
A) Yes, he can reclaim the full amount.
B) Yes, he can reclaim the portion for the remaining period.
C) No, he cannot reclaim any of it because the payment was a gift (silah).
D) It depends on whether the marriage was consummated.

Key Takeaway
Advanced maintenance is a gift (silah) and, once received, is non-recoverable upon death or irrevocable divorce, following the majority Sahibayn position.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
12 min
Selling a Slave for Maintenance and the Divorced Woman's Maintenance
Rulings on slave sale for maintenance and divorced woman's maintenance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a slave can be sold for his wife's maintenance, and apply the ruling on advanced maintenance to the case of a divorced woman when her husband dies.

Core Idea
A slave is sold for his wife's maintenance only if he married with permission; advanced maintenance for a divorced woman is not recoverable upon the husband's death.

The passage continues with two practical applications. First, if a married slave fails to pay his wife's maintenance, may he be sold to satisfy her claim? This lesson details the conditions. Second, if a husband advances maintenance and then dies during the wife's iddah, can her heirs keep the payment? The ruling again turns on the nature of silah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule for selling a slave for maintenance
The basic rule: a qinn (full slave) who married with his master's permission may be sold to pay his wife's overdue maintenance.
The permission is crucial; without it, the marriage is invalid, and no maintenance is owed.
2
Examine the conditions and limits
Only a qinn (not a mudabbar, mukatib, or umm walad) can be sold. The master may pay to avoid sale. If the slave dies, the debt lapses because it was a silah, not a business debt.
Compare to a trading slave: his business debt attaches to his person even after death.
3
Apply the advanced maintenance ruling to a divorced woman's case after husband's death
If a husband advances maintenance and then dies, and the wife was divorced (or in iddah), the majority view (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that her heirs do not return the payment. Muhammad's view differs.
The iddah period continues after the husband's death, so the maintenance is deemed earned.
4
Analyse the reasoning
The advanced payment is a gift (silah) to the wife; the husband's death does not revoke the gift. The wife's iddah is a period of obligation, so even if the husband dies early, the entire advanced sum remains hers.
This is consistent with the core dispute lesson.

Source Text

فعل ذلك تخلصاً من النفقة أو لسوء اخلاقها على عدم مثلاً.
ثم طلقها الزوج ليس للأب أن يسترد ما دفع لأنه لو أعطاها الزوج والمسألة بحالها لم يكن له ذلك عند أبي يوسف وعليه الفتوى، فكذا إذا أعطاها أبو الزوج اهـ. وشمل الموت والطلاق لما ذكرناه، وكذا في الخانية: ولو عجل لها ثم طلقها لم يكن له أن يسترد، وفي فتح القدير : والموت والطلاق قبل الدخول سواء، وفي نفقة المطلقة إذا مات زوجها اختلفوا؛ قيل ترد، وقيل لا تسترد بالاتفاق لأن العدة قائمة في موته ؛ كذا في الأقضية. فعلى هذا لا ينبغي أن يقيد كلام المصنف بموت أحدهما كما فعله الزيلعي بل تجعل مستقلة، ووجهه أنها صلة لزوجته ولا رجوع فيما يهبه لزوجته والعبرة لوقت الهبة لا لوقت الرجوع فالزوجية من الموانع من الرجوع كالموت ودفع الأب كدفع ابنه فلا إشكال .
قوله : (ويباع القن في نفقة زوجته) يعني إذا كان تزوجه بإذن المولى لأنه دين وجب في ذمته لوجود سببه وقد ظهر وجوبه في حق المولى فيتعلق برقبته كدين التجارة في العبد التاجر ومراده عند عدم الفداء فإن للمولى أن يفديه لأن حقها في النفقة لا في عين الرقبة فلو مات العبد سقطت، وكذا إذا قتل في الصحيح لأنه صلة، وكذا المهر، ولم أرهم صرحوا هنا بأن المرأة إذا اختارت استسعاءه في النفقة دون بيعه أن لها ذلك أم لا، لكن صرحوا في المأذون له للتجارة إذا لحقه دين واختار الغرماء استسعاءه دون بيعه أن لهم ذلك؛ ذكره الزيعلي في المأذون فينبغي أن يكون هنا كذلك. وينبغي أن المرأة إذا اختارت استسعاءه لنفقتها كل يوم يكون لها ذلك أيضاً. قيدنا بإذن المولى لأنه لو تزوج بغير إذن المولى لا يباع في النفقة لعدم وجوبها لعدم صحة النكاح ولذا لم يقيد المصنف بالإذن لأن عند عدمه لم تكن زوجة لتجب لها النفقة، وكذا المهر لا يباع فيه ولو دخل بها لعدم ظهوره في حق المولى، وإنما يطالب به بعد عتقه . وقيد بالقن وهو العبد الذي لا حرية فيه بوجه عند الفقهاء. وفي اللغة العبد إذا هو وأبواه يستوي فيه الاثنان والجمع والمذكر والمؤنث كما في شرح النقاية، لأن المكاتب والمدير وأم الولد لا يباعون فيها لعدم جواز البيع وإنما عليهم السعاية إلا إذا عجز المكاتب فإنه يباع لزوال المانع . وقيد بنفقة زوجته لأن نفقة أولاده لا تجب عليه، سواء كانت الزوجة حرة أو أمة، أما إذا كانت حرة فلأن الأولاد أحراراً تبعاً لها والحر لا يستوجب النفقة على العبد إلا الزوجة، وإن كانت المرأة أمة فنفقة الأولاد على مولى الأمة وإن كانت نفقة الأم على العبد لأن الأولاد تبع للأم في الملك فتكون نفقة الأولاد على المالك لا على الزوج؛ كذا في ملك
قوله : (وفي نفقة المطلقة الخ قال الرملي : استفيد منه ومما في الذخيرة من قوله «لو عجل الزوج لها نفقة مدة ثم مات أحدهما قبل مضي المدة لم يرجع عليها ولا في تركتها في قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف : وقال محمد: يرفع عنها بحصته ما مضى ويجب رد الباقي إن كان قائماً، وقيمته إن كان مستهلكاً الخ». جواب حادثة الفتوى طلقها بائناً وعجل لها نفقة تسعة أشهر فأسقطت سقطاً بعد
And for them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is a gift, and the receipt has been connected to it, and there is no return of gifts after death because their ruling ends, as in a gift. And in Fath al-Qadir, the fatwa is on their statement. Al-Walwaliji and the authors of fatawa made it the statement of Abu Yusuf, saying the fatwa is upon it. And it includes whether the one who advanced payment is the husband or his father, as in al-Walwalijiyya and others: The father of the husband if he pays the maintenance of his son's wife... (continues with the text).
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether advanced maintenance can be recovered if the marriage ends by death or divorce. The core issue: is advanced maintenance a wage for being available (as Abu Hanifa held) or a gift (silah) as Abu Yusuf and Muhammad held? The latter view, that it is a gift and thus non-recoverable once received, is the basis of the fatwa. The author then extends this to the case of the father paying his son's wife's maintenance, ruling that the father also cannot reclaim it after divorce, following Abu Yusuf's view. The passage then delves into a later controversy: does this non-recovery apply to revocable divorce (talaq raj'i) as well? Some later scholars, like al-Ramli, opined that it does not, to prevent abuse. The author advises caution (yata'ammal 'inda al-fatwa). Next, the ruling on selling a slave for his wife's maintenance is explained: the slave can be sold only if he married with his master's permission, as the obligation of maintenance then becomes a debt attached to his person. Finally, the passage discusses the maintenance of a divorced woman if the husband dies, noting a difference of opinion on whether advanced maintenance is recoverable from her estate. The relied-upon view is that it is not recoverable because the iddah period continues after death, and the payment is a gift to the wife.

Key Terms
القن (al-qinn): A full slave without any partial freedom; only such slave can be sold for maintenance.
السعاية (al-sa'ayah): Working to pay a debt; here, the slave may work to earn the maintenance instead of being sold.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A slave (mukatib) fails to pay his wife's maintenance. Can he be sold to satisfy the debt?
A) Yes, because maintenance is a debt.
B) No, a mukatib cannot be sold; he must be made to work (saya).
C) Yes, but only if his wife agrees.
D) No, because the woman can only claim from the master.

Key Takeaway
A slave is sold for his wife's maintenance only if he is a qinn and married with permission; advanced maintenance for a divorced woman is not recoverable upon the husband's death.

Reclaiming Advance Nafaqah After Talaq or Death
Ruling on whether advance nafaqah can be reclaimed if divorce or death occurs before the period ends.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the operative Hanafi ruling on reclaiming advance nafaqah after divorce or death, and explain the reasoning based on it being a gift.

Core Idea
Advance nafaqah is a gift; once given, it cannot be reclaimed even if divorce or death occurs.

This lesson addresses a common question: if a wife receives advance maintenance for a future period, and then the marriage ends, can the husband (or his father) reclaim it? The Hanafi school, relying on the view of Abu Yusuf, rules that it cannot be reclaimed. We will examine the reasoning and the scope of this ruling, including the effect of 'iddah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
Who gave what to whom? Here, a father gives a hundred dirhams as advance nafaqah for his son's wife, then the son divorces her.
2
Extract the hukm
Can the father reclaim it? According to Abu Yusuf (and the fatwa), no. The father cannot reclaim because if the husband had given it, he could not reclaim it.
The text states 'upon this is the fatwa' (وعليه الفتوى).
3
Understand the reasoning
The advance is a gift (silah) to the wife. The marriage at the time of giving prevents reclamation. The father’s payment is analogous to the son’s payment.
The underlying principle is that a gift to a spouse cannot be reclaimed.
4
Apply to other scenarios
The same ruling applies whether the marriage ends by divorce or death. Even if the wife dies, the advance is not reclaimed. The ‘iddah (waiting period) does not change the gift status.
In case of death, the ‘iddah continues, showing some marital bond remains.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
There is a disagreement: some say that if a divorced woman’s husband dies, her advance nafaqah should be returned. But the relied-upon view is that it is not returned, because the gift was given while marriage existed.
The text from al-Aqdiyyah mentions this disagreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق باب النفقة مائة ثم طلقها الزوج ليس للأب أن يسترد ما دفع لأنه لو أعطاها الزوج والمسألة بحالها لم يكن له ذلك عند أبي يوسف وعليه الفتوى، فكذا إذا أعطاها أبو الزوج اهـ. وشمل الموت والطلاق لما ذكرناه، وكذا في الخانية: ولو عجل لها ثم طلقها لم يكن له أن يسترد، وفي فتح القدير : والموت والطلاق قبل الدخول سواء، وفي نفقة المطلقة إذا مات زوجها اختلفوا؛ قيل ترد، وقيل لا تسترد بالاتفاق لأن العدة قائمة في موته ؛ كذا في الأقضية. فعلى هذا لا ينبغي أن يقيد كلام المصنف بموت أحدهما كما فعله الزيلعي بل تجعل مستقلة، ووجهه أنها صلة لزوجته ولا رجوع فيما يهبه لزوجته والعبرة لوقت الهبة لا لوقت الرجوع فالزوجية من الموانع من الرجوع كالموت ودفع الأب كدفع ابنه فلا إشكال.
Book of Divorce, Chapter of Maintenance: A hundred (dirhams) [given as advance nafaqah], then the husband divorces her; it is not permissible for the father to reclaim what he paid, because if the husband had given it to her while the case was the same, he would not have the right to do so according to Abu Yusuf, and upon this is the fatwa. So likewise if the husband's father gave it. [End of quote]. And it includes death and divorce due to what we mentioned. Similarly in al-Khaniyyah: And if he advanced [nafaqah] to her and then divorced her, he may not reclaim it. And in Fath al-Qadir: Death and divorce before consummation are the same. Regarding the nafaqah of a divorced woman if her husband dies, they differed: some say it is returned, and some say it is not returned by agreement because the 'iddah continues in his death; as in al-Aqdiyyah. On this basis, one should not restrict the author's words to the death of one of them as al-Zayla'i did, but rather treat it as independent. And its reasoning is that it is a gift to his wife, and there is no reclaming what he gives to his wife; consideration is given to the time of the gift, not the time of reclaming. So the marital relationship is among the impediments to reclaming, like death; and the father's payment is like the son's payment, so there is no difficulty.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on whether advance maintenance (nafaqah) paid to a wife can be reclaimed if the husband divorces her or either dies before the period ends. The author begins by discussing a case where a husband's father gives a hundred dirhams as advance nafaqah and the husband subsequently divorces the wife. The ruling, according to Abu Yusuf (and this is the position relied upon for fatwa), is that the father cannot reclaim the payment. The reason is that if the husband himself had given it directly, he could not reclaim it; thus the father, as his substitute, is in the same position. This ruling applies to both divorce and death, as stated in al-Khaniyyah and Fath al-Qadir. The author further addresses a disagreement regarding the nafaqah of a divorced woman when her husband dies: some say the advance must be returned, while others say it is not returned because the 'iddah is still in effect (as in the case of death, the 'iddah continues). The author endorses the view that the ruling should not be restricted to death of one spouse, as al-Zayla'i did, but rather is general. The underlying principle is that the advance payment is a gift (hibah) to the wife, and as long as the marriage was valid at the time of giving, the marital relationship prevents reclaming it. The father's payment is analogous to the son's (husband's) payment. Thus, no reclaiming is possible.

Key Terms
النفقة المعجلة (al-nafaqah al-mu'ajjalah): Advance payment of maintenance for a future period, given to the wife before it is due.
العدة (al-'iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of her husband, during which she cannot remarry.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Abu Yusuf), can a father-in-law reclaim advance nafaqah given to his son's wife if the son later divorces her?
A) Yes, because the divorce ends the marriage.
B) No, because the payment was a gift and the marriage was valid at the time of giving.
C) Yes, but only if the divorce occurs before consummation.
D) No, only the husband can reclaim it, not the father.

Key Takeaway
Advance nafaqah is treated as a gift; once given, it cannot be reclaimed due to divorce or death, as per the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Obligation or Commendation: Taking a Surety from the Woman for Absent Husband's Maintenance
Intra-Hanafi dispute on taking surety from wife for absent husband's maintenance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi disagreement on whether the judge must take a surety from the woman when granting maintenance for the absent husband, and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Taking a surety is precautionary, not obligatory; the judge may exercise discretion.

When a judge grants maintenance to a wife whose husband is absent, should he also take a surety (kafil) from her to protect the husband's rights in case he later proves he already paid? Hanafi scholars disagree: al-Sarakhsi said it is obligatory, while al-Khassaf said it is commendable. This lesson unpacks that dispute, the evidence, and the operative ruling for judges today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on surety
Locate in the passage where the text discusses whether taking a surety is obligatory (wajib) or commendable (hasan). Note the scholars involved: al-Sarakhsi and al-Khassaf.
The text states: 'واختلف في أخذ الكفيل هل هو واجب على القاضي أو حسن؟'
2
Trace the evidence for each view
Al-Sarakhsi argues that the judge is appointed as a supervisor for the incapable (the absent husband) and must take precautions. Al-Khassaf counters that the judge can give maintenance without a surety, indicating it is not necessary. Find the supporting references from Kitab al-Aqdiya and al-Dhakhira.
The text says: 'ذهب السرخسي إلى الأول والخصاف إلى الثاني... وفي كتاب الأقضية أن القاضي لو لم يأخذ منها كفيلاً دفع إليها النفقة...'
3
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
See which view is upheld by later authorities like al-Sadr al-Shahid and which is actually practiced. Note the nuance: al-Sadr al-Shahid upheld al-Sarakhsi's view, but the text from al-Dhakhira indicates that judges do not always take a surety.
The mufta bihi is that it is commendable (hasan), not obligatory.
4
Apply to a practical scenario
Imagine a modern case: a wife with children, husband abroad, no contact. She asks the judge for maintenance. Should the judge demand a surety? Discuss the discretion based on the preponderant view.
The judge may require a surety if he deems it necessary, but it is not a legal obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عند قسمة التركة بين الورثة فإنه ليس بحسن لجهالة المكفول له كما سيأتي. واختلف في أخذ الكفيل هل هو واجب على القاضي أو حسن؟ ذهب السرخسي إلى الأول والخصاف إلى الثاني، وصحح الصدر الشهيد الأول لأنه نصب ناظراً للعاجز فيجب عليه النظر إليه وهو في أخذ الكفيل. وفي كتاب الأقضية أن القاضي لو لم يأخذ منها كفيلاً دفع إليها النفقة، فهذا إشارة إلى أن أخذ الكفيل نوع احتياط لا أن يكون لازماً؛ كذا في الذخيرة. وذكر في المستصفى قوله ويؤخذ منها أي من المرأة وفي بعض النسخ، ويؤخذ منه أي من آخذ النفقة أو من كل واحد من الأصناف المذكورين اهـ. وهذا يدل على أنه يؤخذ الكفيل من الوالدين أيضاً وهو الظاهر لأنه أنظر للغائب. وقد يقال إنه إنما يؤخذ منها لما تقدم، وأما من الوالدين فإنما هو لاحتمال التعجيل، وقدمنا أن النفقة المعجلة للقريب إذا هلكت أو سرقت فإنه يقضى له بأخرى بخلاف الزوجة فليس في أخذ الكفيل احتياط للغائب لأنه لو كان عجل ثم ادعى الوالد هلاكها قبل منه . وقيد بكون المال عند شخص لأنه لو كان له مال في بيته فطلبت من القاضي فرض النفقة ؛ فإن علم بالنكاح بينهما فرض لها في ذلك المال لأنه إيفاء لحق المرأة وليس بقضاء على الزوج بالنفقة كما لو أقر بدين ثم غاب وله مال حاضر من جنس الدين وطلب صاحب الدين من ذلك قضى له به، أصله حديث هند كما عرف وينبغي للقاضي أن يحلفها أنه لم يعطها النفقة ويأخذ منها كفيلاً كما قدمناه ؛ كذا في الذخيرة ولو لم يكن له مال أصلاً فطلبت من القاضي فرض النفقة فعندنا يسمع البينة لأنه قضاء على الغائب، وعند زفر يسمع القاضي البينة ولا يقضي بالنكاح ويعطيها النفقة من مال الزوج وإن لم يكن له مال أمرها القاضي بالاستدانة، فإن حضر الزوج وأقر بالنكاح أمره بقضاء الدين وإن أنكر ذلك كلفها القاضي إعادة البينة، فإن لم تعدها أمرها القاضي برد ما أخذت وما يفعله القضاة في زماننا من قبول البينة من المرأة وفرض النفقة على الغائب إنما ينفذ لا لأنه قول علمائنا الثلاثة في ظاهر الرواية وإنما ينفذ لكونه مختلفاً فيه، إما مع زفر أو مع أبي يوسف كما ذكره الخصاف وهو أرفق بالناس. ثم على قول من يقول تفرض النفقة في هذه المسألة لا تحتاج المرأة إقامة البيئة على أنه لم يخلف نفقة؛ كذا في الذخيرة والخانية والحاصل أن القاضي إذا لم يعلم النكاح فليس له فرض النفقة على الغائب ولو أقامت المرأة البينة على ظاهر الرواية لكن لو سمع البينة وفرضها لا النفقة لهؤلاء من مال الغائب إذا استوثق بكفيل من أحد فحسن قوله: (فليس في أخذ الكفيل احتياط للغائب الخ) أقول : قد يدعي القريب عدم الدفع إليه دون الهلاك تأمل قوله: (ويعطيها من مال الزوج) قال الرملي : لا يلائم قوله المتقدم فلو لم يكن له مال أصلا وحق العبارة أن يقول بدل قوله ويعطيها النفقة» يأمرها القاضي بالاستدانة قوله : (وهو أرفق بالناس) قال الرملي : النفقة وأمرها بالاستدانة جاز ونفذ كما هو قول زفر وأبي يوسف وعلينه العمل وهي من إحدى المسائل الست التي يفتى فيها بقول زفر لحاجة الناس. وفي فتح القدير: ونقل مثل قول زفر عن أبي يوسف فقوي عمل القضاة لحاجة الناس إلى ذلك. وإذا كان للمرأة أولاد صغار وغاب الأب ولم يترك لهم نفقة تجبر الأم على الإنفاق إن كان لها مال ثم ترجع بذلك على الأب ؛ كذا في الخانية. وبهذا علم أن الرجل إذا غاب وله زوجة وأولاد صغار ولم يترك شيئاً فإن القاضي يسمع البينة منها على النكاح إن لم يكن عالماً به على ما عليه العمل ثم يفرض لها ولأولادها نفقة ثم يأمرها بالاستدانة، فإذا جاء رجعت عليه بالمفروض لها ولأولادها. وأشار بقوله «فرض» إلى أن المودع والمديون لو أنفقا بغير أمر القاضي فإن المودع ضامن ولا يبرأ المديون، ولا رجوع للمنفق على من أنفق عليه كما في الذخيرة وجعله في الخانية نظير المودع لو قضى بالوديعة دين المودع بغير أمر القاضي فإنه يكون ضامناً .اهـ. مع أنه في هذه المسألة لا فرق بين أمر القاضي وعدمه فإنه ليس للقاضي أن يقضي دين الغائب من وديعته كما قدمناه، ولم يذكر المصنف الحكم بعد حضور الزوج. قال في الذخيرة فإن حضر الزوج وقال كنت أوفيت النفقة أو أرسلت إليها النفقة فالقاضي يقول له أقم ،البينة فإن أقامها أمرها القاضي برد ما أخذت لأنه ظهر عند القاضي أنها أخذت بغير حق وللزوج الخيار إن شاء أخذها بذلك وإن شاء آخذ الكفيل فإن لم يكن للزوج بينة وحلفت المرأة على ذلك فلا شيء على الكفيل، وإن نكلت عن اليمين ونكل الكفيل لزمهما المال وللزوج الخيار فقد ذكر في هذه المسألة نكولهما ونكول المرأة أمر لازم، وأما نكول الكفيل فليس بلازم بل إذا نكلت المرأة فذلك يكفي لثبوت الخيار للزوج وإن لم ينكل الكفيل لأن النكول إقرار والأصيل إذا أقر بالمال لزم الكفيل وإن جحد الكفيل ولا ضمان على المودع لأن أمر القاضي بالدفع إليها قد صح فصار كأمره بنفسه .اهـ. ويخالفه ما في المبسوط وشرح الطحاوي من أنها لو أقرت أنها وفي ملتقى الأبحر وهو المختار وفي غيره وبه يفتى ؛ ذكره في النهر. وفي منح الغفار: وعمل القضاة اليوم على هذا للحاجة فيفتى به قال في الشرح كما في شرح المجمع لابن ملك ونص عبارته والقضاة في زماننا يعملون على قوله لاحتياج الناس إليه واستحسنه أكثر المشايخ فيفتي به اهـ. وشرطه أن يكون حضوره غير متيسر بأن كانت غيبته مدة سفر وإلا لا ذلك تأمل. وتقدم في الأول أنه يصح يشترط لوجوب الفرض على القاضي وجوازه منه شرطان: أحدهما طلب المرأة والثاني حضرة الزوج اهـ قوله : (وهي إحدى المسائل الست الخ سيذكرها المؤلف في كتاب الكفالة قوله : (فإن القاضي يسمع البينة على النكاح) أي لا ليقضي بالنكاح بل يقضي بالنفقة وإذا سمع بينتها عليه لذلك تضمن كون الأولاد له لقيام الفراش فيقضي بالنفقة لهم أيضاً وإن لم يحكم بالنسب .
At the division of the estate among the heirs, it is not good due to the ignorance of the person for whom the guarantee is taken, as will come. And there is disagreement about taking the surety: is it obligatory upon the judge or commendable? Al-Sarakhsi went to the first, and al-Khassaf to the second, and al-Sadr al-Shahid corrected the first because he is appointed as a supervisor for the incapable, so he must look after him, and that is in taking the surety. And in Kitab al-Aqdiya, if the judge did not take a surety from her, he gives her the maintenance, so this indicates that taking a surety is a type of precaution, not necessary. Similarly in al-Dhakhira. And it is mentioned in al-Mustasfa: "And it is taken from her" i.e. from the woman, and in some copies, "And it is taken from him" i.e. from the one taking the maintenance, or from each of the mentioned categories. This indicates that a surety is taken from the parents as well, and it is apparent because it is more considerate for the absent one. And it may be said that it is only taken from her due to what preceded, but from the parents it is due to the possibility of delay. And we have mentioned that expedited maintenance for a relative, if it perishes or is stolen, then another is decreed for him, unlike the wife, so there is no precaution for the absent in taking a surety because if he expedited and then the father claimed its destruction, it is accepted from him. And it is restricted to the wealth being with a person because if he has wealth in his house and she asks the judge to prescribe maintenance; if he knows of the marriage between them, he prescribes it from that wealth because it is fulfilling the woman's right and not a judgment against the husband for maintenance, just as if he confessed a debt then became absent and has present wealth of that type and the creditor demands from it, it is given to him. Its origin is the hadith of Hind as known. And it is appropriate for the judge to make her swear that he did not give her the maintenance and take a surety from her as we have mentioned; similarly in al-Dhakhirah. And if he has no wealth at all, and she asks the judge to prescribe maintenance, then according to us he hears the evidence because it is a judgment against the absent. According to Zufar, the judge hears the evidence but does not rule on the marriage and gives her maintenance from the husband's wealth. And if he has no wealth, the judge orders her to borrow. Then if the husband comes and acknowledges the marriage, he orders him to repay the debt. If he denies it, the judge requires her to re-establish the evidence. If she does not re-establish it, the judge orders her to return what she took. And what the judges in our time do—accepting the woman's evidence and prescribing maintenance against the absent—only takes effect not because it is the saying of our three scholars in the apparent narration, but rather it takes effect because it is a matter of dispute, either with Zufar or with Abu Yusuf, as al-Khassaf mentioned, and it is more convenient for the people. Then according to the one who says that maintenance is prescribed in this issue, the woman does not need to establish evidence that he did not leave maintenance; similarly in al-Dhakhira and al-Khaniyya. The conclusion is that if the judge does not know of the marriage, he has no right to prescribe maintenance against the absent even if the woman establishes evidence, according to the apparent narration. But if he hears the evidence and prescribes it for these from the absent's wealth when he secures a surety from someone, that is good. His statement: (There is no precaution for the absent in taking the surety, etc.) I say: The relative may claim non-payment without destruction, contemplate. His statement: (And he gives her from the husband's wealth) Al-Ramli said: It does not harmonize with his previous statement: "If he has no wealth at all," and the correct expression is that instead of his saying "and he gives her the maintenance," he should say "the judge orders her to borrow." His statement: (And it is more convenient for the people) Al-Ramli said: The maintenance and her being ordered to borrow is permissible and executable, as it is the saying of Zufar and Abu Yusuf, and upon it is practice, and it is one of the six issues in which fatwa is given by Zufar's saying due to the need of the people. And in Fath al-Qadir: The like of Zufar's saying was transmitted from Abu Yusuf, so the judges' practice was strengthened due to the need of the people for that. And if the woman has young children and the father is absent and did not leave maintenance for them, the mother is compelled to spend if she has wealth, then she recovers that from the father; similarly in al-Khaniyya. And by this it is known that if a man is absent and has a wife and young children and leaves nothing, then the judge hears the evidence from her about the marriage, if he is not aware of it, according to what practice is upon, then prescribes maintenance for her and her children, then orders her to borrow. So when he comes, she recovers from him the prescribed amount for her and her children. And he indicated by his saying "prescribes" that if the depositee and debtor spend without the judge's order, then the depositee is liable and the debtor is not absolved, and the spender has no recourse against the one on whom he spent, as in al-Dhakhira. And in al-Khaniyya he made it analogous to the depositee who pays the depositor's debt with the deposit without the judge's order, then he is liable. Even though in this issue there is no difference between the judge's order and its absence, because the judge does not have the right to pay the absent's debt from his deposit as we have mentioned. And the author did not mention the ruling after the husband's arrival. He said in al-Dhakhira: If the husband comes and says, "I had paid the maintenance" or "I had sent maintenance to her," the judge tells him, "Establish evidence." If he establishes it, the judge orders her to return what she took because it becomes clear to the judge that she took it without right. And the husband has the choice: if he wishes, he takes her with that, or if he wishes, he takes the surety. If the husband has no evidence and the woman swears about that, then there is nothing on the surety. If she refuses to swear and the surety refuses, then both of them are liable for the wealth, and the husband has the choice. So he mentioned in this issue their refusal. The woman's refusal is binding, but the surety's refusal is not binding. Rather, if the woman refuses, that is sufficient to establish the choice for the husband, even if the surety does not refuse, because refusal is an admission. And if the principal admits to the wealth, the surety is bound even if the surety denies. And there is no liability on the depositee because the judge's order to pay to her is valid, so it becomes like his own order. Something contrary is in al-Mabsut and Sharh al-Tahawi: that if she confessed that... and in Multaqa al-Abhar this is the chosen view, and in others and by it fatwa is given; mentioned in al-Nahr. And in Manh al-Ghaffar: The judges today act upon this due to need, so fatwa is given by it. He said in al-Sharh as in Sharh al-Majma' by Ibn Malik: "The judges in our time act upon his saying due to the need of the people, and most mashayikh considered it good, so fatwa is given by it." And its condition is that his presence be not attainable, such that his absence is of travel duration; otherwise, no. Contemplate. And it preceded in the first that it is valid; two conditions are required for the obligation of prescribing upon the judge and its permissibility from him: one is the woman's request, and the second is the presence of the husband. His statement: (And it is one of the six issues... the author will mention them in the book of Suretyship. His statement: (So the judge hears the evidence on the marriage) i.e., not to rule on the marriage but to rule on maintenance. And if he hears her evidence on it, that implies that the children are his due to the establishment of the marriage bed, so he rules on maintenance for them as well, even if he does not rule on lineage.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary (sharh) on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, discussing the rulings on maintenance (nafaqah) for the wife and children when the husband is absent. The passage covers several interconnected issues. First, it addresses whether a judge is obliged to take a surety (kafil) from the woman when granting maintenance from the absent husband's property. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: al-Sarakhsi considers it obligatory, while al-Khassaf considers it commendable (hasan). The preferred view, as upheld by al-Sadr al-Shahid, is that it is obligatory because the judge is appointed to protect the rights of the incapable. However, other texts indicate that taking a surety is precautionary rather than necessary. The passage also discusses whether a surety should be taken from parents as well, concluding that it is advisable for their case too, though for different reasons (to avoid neglect of the absent). The author then explains the scenario where the husband has property at home: the judge can directly assign maintenance from that property without a surety, citing the hadith of Hind. When the husband has no property, the majority view (our scholars) holds that the judge hears evidence of the marriage but does not give maintenance from absent property; instead, the woman is ordered to borrow. In contrast, Zufar (and Abu Yusuf in one narration) allows the judge to give maintenance directly from the husband's wealth if present, or order borrowing if not, and this is the practice adopted today for public convenience, being one of the six issues where Zufar's opinion is followed. The passage further details the procedure after the husband returns: if he proves he already paid maintenance, the woman must return what she took, and the husband has options against her and the surety. The issue of refusal to swear (nukul) is also discussed. Finally, it mentions conditions for the judge to prescribe maintenance: the woman's request and the husband's presence (or inability to be present). The commentary emphasizes that the judge's acceptance of evidence without proof of the husband's absence is a practical concession.

Key Terms
كفيل (kafil): A surety or guarantor who is taken from the woman or others to ensure repayment if the husband later proves he paid maintenance.
نفقة (nafaqah): Maintenance, including food, clothing, and shelter, for the wife and children which the husband is obligated to provide.
غائب (gha'ib): An absent person, specifically the husband who is away and cannot be present for the legal proceedings about maintenance.
بينة (bayyinah): Evidence, typically witness testimony, that the woman must present to prove the marriage and the husband's absence without leaving maintenance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best describes the mufta bihi (operative) Hanafi view on taking a surety from the woman for maintenance of an absent husband?
A) It is obligatory on the judge to take a surety.
B) It is commendable but not obligatory; the judge may use discretion.
C) It is prohibited because it discourages women from seeking maintenance.
D) It is required only if the husband has no property.

Key Takeaway
Taking a surety from the wife for absent husband's maintenance is commendable, not obligatory, giving the judge discretion to ease hardship.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
10 min
Judgment Against the Absent: Granting Maintenance When the Husband Has No Present Wealth
Dispute between majority and Zufar on granting maintenance for absent husband with no wealth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi judges often follow Zufar's ruling on maintenance for absent husbands when the husband has no present wealth, and identify the procedure prescribed.

Core Idea
For public necessity, Zufar's opinion prevails: the judge may order the woman to borrow, and she recovers from the husband later.

When a husband is absent and has no known property, can the judge grant maintenance to the wife based on her evidence alone? The majority Hanafi view restricts this, but Zufar (and Abu Yusuf in one narration) allows it for the sake of public need. This passage explains why modern practice follows Zufar's view, making it one of the six celebrated issues where fatwa is given by his saying.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Locate in the text: 'وعند زفر يسمع القاضي البينة ولا يقضي بالنكاح ويعطيها النفقة من مال الزوج وإن لم يكن له مال أمرها القاضي بالاستدانة'. Contrast this with the majority view: 'فعندنا يسمع البينة لأنه قضاء على الغائب'.
The majority (our scholars) say the judge hears evidence but does not give maintenance from absent property.
2
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
Under the majority, the woman must borrow without a court order and later seek repayment. Under Zufar, the judge orders her to borrow, making the debt enforceable.
The practical difference: court-ordered borrowing gives the woman stronger grounds to reclaim from the husband.
3
Analyze the reason for adopting Zufar's view
The text states: 'وهي من إحدى المسائل الست التي يفتى فيها بقول زفر لحاجة الناس'. Also 'عمل القضاة اليوم على هذا للحاجة'.
Public necessity (hajat al-nas) overrides the stricter majority rule.
4
Trace the procedure after husband's return
If the husband returns and admits the marriage, he must repay the debt. If he denies, the woman must re-prove the marriage or return what she took.
The judge also takes a surety (kafil) as precaution, as discussed in the previous lesson.

عند قسمة التركة بين الورثة فإنه ليس بحسن لجهالة المكفول له كما سيأتي. واختلف في أخذ الكفيل هل هو واجب على القاضي أو حسن؟ ذهب السرخسي إلى الأول والخصاف إلى الثاني، وصحح الصدر الشهيد الأول لأنه نصب وذكر في المستصفى قوله ويؤخذ منها أي من المرأة وفي بعض النسخ، ويؤخذ منه أي من آخذ النفقة أو من كل واحد من الأصناف المذكورين اهـ. وهذا يدل على أنه يؤخذ الكفيل من الوالدين أيضاً وهو الظاهر لأنه أنظر وليس بقضاء على الزوج بالنفقة كما لو أقر بدين ثم غاب وله مال حاضر من جنس الدين وطلب صاحب الدين من ذلك قضى له به، أصله حديث هند كما عرف وينبغي للقاضي أن يحلفها أنه لم يعطها النفقة ويأخذ منها كفيلاً كما قدمناه ؛ كذا في الذخيرة ولو لم يكن له مال أصلاً فطلبت من القاضي فرض النفقة فعندنا يسمع البينة لأنه قضاء على الغائب، وعند زفر يسمع القاضي البينة ولا يقضي بالنكاح ويعطيها النفقة من مال الزوج وإن لم يكن له مال أمرها القاضي بالاستدانة، فإن حضر الزوج وأقر بالنكاح أمره بقضاء الدين وإن أنكر ذلك كلفها القاضي إعادة البينة، فإن لم تعدها أمرها القاضي برد ما أخذت وما يفعله القضاة في زماننا من قبول البينة من المرأة وفرض النفقة على الغائب إنما ينفذ لا لأنه قول علمائنا الثلاثة في ظاهر الرواية وإنما ينفذ لكونه مختلفاً فيه، إما مع زفر أو مع أبي يوسف كما ذكره الخصاف وهو أرفق بالناس. ثم على قول من يقول تفرض النفقة في هذه المسألة لا تحتاج المرأة إقامة البيئة على أنه لم يخلف نفقة؛ كذا في الذخيرة والخانية والحاصل أن القاضي إذا لم يعلم النكاح فليس له فرض النفقة على الغائب ولو أقامت المرأة البينة على ظاهر الرواية لكن لو سمع البينة وفرضها لا النفقة لهؤلاء من مال الغائب إذا استوثق بكفيل من أحد فحسن قوله: (فليس في أخذ الكفيل احتياط للغائب الخ) أقول : قد يدعي القريب عدم الدفع إليه دون الهلاك تأمل قوله: (ويعطيها من مال الزوج) قال الرملي : لا يلائم قوله المتقدم فلو لم يكن له مال أصلا وحق العبارة أن يقول بدل قوله ويعطيها النفقة» يأمرها القاضي بالاستدانة قوله : (وهو أرفق بالناس) قال الرملي : النفقة وأمرها بالاستدانة جاز ونفذ كما هو قول زفر وأبي يوسف وعلينه العمل وهي من إحدى المسائل الست التي يفتى فيها بقول زفر لحاجة الناس. وفي فتح القدير: ونقل مثل قول زفر عن أبي يوسف فقوي عمل القضاة لحاجة الناس إلى ذلك. وإذا كان للمرأة أولاد صغار وغاب الأب ولم يترك لهم نفقة تجبر الأم على الإنفاق إن كان لها مال ثم ترجع بذلك على الأب ؛ كذا في الخانية. وبهذا علم أن الرجل إذا غاب وله زوجة وأولاد صغار ولم يترك شيئاً فإن القاضي يسمع البينة منها على النكاح إن لم يكن عالماً به على ما عليه العمل ثم يفرض لها ولأولادها نفقة ثم يأمرها بالاستدانة، فإذا جاء رجعت عليه بالمفروض لها ولأولادها. وأشار بقوله «فرض» إلى أن المودع والمديون لو أنفقا بغير أمر القاضي فإن المودع ضامن ولا يبرأ المديون، ولا رجوع للمنفق على من أنفق عليه كما في الذخيرة وجعله في الخانية نظير المودع لو قضى بالوديعة دين المودع بغير أمر القاضي فإنه يكون ضامناً .اهـ. مع أنه في هذه المسألة لا فرق بين أمر القاضي وعدمه فإنه ليس للقاضي أن يقضي دين الغائب من وديعته كما قدمناه، ولم يذكر المصنف الحكم بعد حضور الزوج. قال في الذخيرة فإن حضر الزوج وقال كنت أوفيت النفقة أو أرسلت إليها النفقة فالقاضي يقول له أقم ،البينة فإن أقامها أمرها القاضي برد ما أخذت لأنه ظهر عند القاضي أنها أخذت بغير حق وللزوج الخيار إن شاء أخذها بذلك وإن شاء آخذ الكفيل فإن لم يكن للزوج بينة وحلفت المرأة على ذلك فلا شيء على الكفيل، وإن نكلت عن اليمين ونكل الكفيل لزمهما المال وللزوج الخيار فقد ذكر في هذه المسألة نكولهما ونكول المرأة أمر لازم، وأما نكول الكفيل فليس بلازم بل إذا نكلت المرأة فذلك يكفي لثبوت الخيار للزوج وإن لم ينكل الكفيل لأن النكول إقرار والأصيل إذا أقر بالمال لزم الكفيل وإن جحد الكفيل ولا ضمان على المودع لأن أمر القاضي بالدفع إليها قد صح فصار كأمره بنفسه .اهـ. ويخالفه ما في المبسوط وشرح الطحاوي من أنها لو أقرت أنها وفي ملتقى الأبحر وهو المختار وفي غيره وبه يفتى ؛ ذكره في النهر. وفي منح الغفار: وعمل القضاة اليوم على هذا للحاجة فيفتى به قال في الشرح كما في شرح المجمع لابن ملك ونص عبارته والقضاة في زماننا يعملون على قوله لاحتياج الناس إليه واستحسنه أكثر المشايخ فيفتي به اهـ. وشرطه أن يكون حضوره غير متيسر بأن كانت غيبته مدة سفر وإلا لا ذلك تأمل. وتقدم في الأول أنه يصح يشترط لوجوب الفرض على القاضي وجوازه منه شرطان: أحدهما طلب المرأة والثاني حضرة الزوج اهـ قوله : (وهي إحدى المسائل الست الخ سيذكرها المؤلف في كتاب الكفالة قوله : (فإن القاضي يسمع البينة على النكاح) أي لا ليقضي بالنكاح بل يقضي بالنفقة وإذا سمع بينتها عليه لذلك تضمن كون الأولاد له لقيام الفراش فيقضي بالنفقة لهم أيضاً وإن لم يحكم بالنسب .
At the division of the estate among the heirs, it is not good due to the ignorance of the person for whom the guarantee is taken, as will come. And there is disagreement about taking the surety: is it obligatory upon the judge or commendable? Al-Sarakhsi went to the first, and al-Khassaf to the second, and al-Sadr al-Shahid corrected the first because he is appointed as a supervisor for the incapable, so he must look after him, and that is in taking the surety. And in Kitab al-Aqdiya, if the judge did not take a surety from her, he gives her the maintenance, so this indicates that taking a surety is a type of precaution, not necessary. Similarly in al-Dhakhira. And it is mentioned in al-Mustasfa: "And it is taken from her" i.e. from the woman, and in some copies, "And it is taken from him" i.e. from the one taking the maintenance, or from each of the mentioned categories. This indicates that a surety is taken from the parents as well, and it is apparent because it is more considerate for the absent one. And it may be said that it is only taken from her due to what preceded, but from the parents it is due to the possibility of delay. And we have mentioned that expedited maintenance for a relative, if it perishes or is stolen, then another is decreed for him, unlike the wife, so there is no precaution for the absent in taking a surety because if he expedited and then the father claimed its destruction, it is accepted from him. And it is restricted to the wealth being with a person because if he has wealth in his house and she asks the judge to prescribe maintenance; if he knows of the marriage between them, he prescribes it from that wealth because it is fulfilling the woman's right and not a judgment against the husband for maintenance, just as if he confessed a debt then became absent and has present wealth of that type and the creditor demands from it, it is given to him. Its origin is the hadith of Hind as known. And it is appropriate for the judge to make her swear that he did not give her the maintenance and take a surety from her as we have mentioned; similarly in al-Dhakhirah. And if he has no wealth at all, and she asks the judge to prescribe maintenance, then according to us he hears the evidence because it is a judgment against the absent. According to Zufar, the judge hears the evidence but does not rule on the marriage and gives her maintenance from the husband's wealth. And if he has no wealth, the judge orders her to borrow. Then if the husband comes and acknowledges the marriage, he orders him to repay the debt. If he denies it, the judge requires her to re-establish the evidence. If she does not re-establish it, the judge orders her to return what she took. And what the judges in our time do—accepting the woman's evidence and prescribing maintenance against the absent—only takes effect not because it is the saying of our three scholars in the apparent narration, but rather it takes effect because it is a matter of dispute, either with Zufar or with Abu Yusuf, as al-Khassaf mentioned, and it is more convenient for the people. Then according to the one who says that maintenance is prescribed in this issue, the woman does not need to establish evidence that he did not leave maintenance; similarly in al-Dhakhira and al-Khaniyya. The conclusion is that if the judge does not know of the marriage, he has no right to prescribe maintenance against the absent even if the woman establishes evidence, according to the apparent narration. But if he hears the evidence and prescribes it for these from the absent's wealth when he secures a surety from someone, that is good. His statement: (There is no precaution for the absent in taking the surety, etc.) I say: The relative may claim non-payment without destruction, contemplate. His statement: (And he gives her from the husband's wealth) Al-Ramli said: It does not harmonize with his previous statement: "If he has no wealth at all," and the correct expression is that instead of his saying "and he gives her the maintenance," he should say "the judge orders her to borrow." His statement: (And it is more convenient for the people) Al-Ramli said: The maintenance and her being ordered to borrow is permissible and executable, as it is the saying of Zufar and Abu Yusuf, and upon it is practice, and it is one of the six issues in which fatwa is given by Zufar's saying due to the need of the people. And in Fath al-Qadir: The like of Zufar's saying was transmitted from Abu Yusuf, so the judges' practice was strengthened due to the need of the people for that. And if the woman has young children and the father is absent and did not leave maintenance for them, the mother is compelled to spend if she has wealth, then she recovers that from the father; similarly in al-Khaniyya. And by this it is known that if a man is absent and has a wife and young children and leaves nothing, then the judge hears the evidence from her about the marriage, if he is not aware of it, according to what practice is upon, then prescribes maintenance for her and her children, then orders her to borrow. So when he comes, she recovers from him the prescribed amount for her and her children. And he indicated by his saying "prescribes" that if the depositee and debtor spend without the judge's order, then the depositee is liable and the debtor is not absolved, and the spender has no recourse against the one on whom he spent, as in al-Dhakhira. And in al-Khaniyya he made it analogous to the depositee who pays the depositor's debt with the deposit without the judge's order, then he is liable. Even though in this issue there is no difference between the judge's order and its absence, because the judge does not have the right to pay the absent's debt from his deposit as we have mentioned. And the author did not mention the ruling after the husband's arrival. He said in al-Dhakhira: If the husband comes and says, "I had paid the maintenance" or "I had sent maintenance to her," the judge tells him, "Establish evidence." If he establishes it, the judge orders her to return what she took because it becomes clear to the judge that she took it without right. And the husband has the choice: if he wishes, he takes her with that, or if he wishes, he takes the surety. If the husband has no evidence and the woman swears about that, then there is nothing on the surety. If she refuses to swear and the surety refuses, then both of them are liable for the wealth, and the husband has the choice. So he mentioned in this issue their refusal. The woman's refusal is binding, but the surety's refusal is not binding. Rather, if the woman refuses, that is sufficient to establish the choice for the husband, even if the surety does not refuse, because refusal is an admission. And if the principal admits to the wealth, the surety is bound even if the surety denies. And there is no liability on the depositee because the judge's order to pay to her is valid, so it becomes like his own order. Something contrary is in al-Mabsut and Sharh al-Tahawi: that if she confessed that... and in Multaqa al-Abhar this is the chosen view, and in others and by it fatwa is given; mentioned in al-Nahr. And in Manh al-Ghaffar: The judges today act upon this due to need, so fatwa is given by it. He said in al-Sharh as in Sharh al-Majma' by Ibn Malik: "The judges in our time act upon his saying due to the need of the people, and most mashayikh considered it good, so fatwa is given by it." And its condition is that his presence be not attainable, such that his absence is of travel duration; otherwise, no. Contemplate. And it preceded in the first that it is valid; two conditions are required for the obligation of prescribing upon the judge and its permissibility from him: one is the woman's request, and the second is the presence of the husband. His statement: (And it is one of the six issues... the author will mention them in the book of Suretyship. His statement: (So the judge hears the evidence on the marriage) i.e., not to rule on the marriage but to rule on maintenance. And if he hears her evidence on it, that implies that the children are his due to the establishment of the marriage bed, so he rules on maintenance for them as well, even if he does not rule on lineage.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary (sharh) on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, discussing the rulings on maintenance (nafaqah) for the wife and children when the husband is absent. The passage covers several interconnected issues. First, it addresses whether a judge is obliged to take a surety (kafil) from the woman when granting maintenance from the absent husband's property. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: al-Sarakhsi considers it obligatory, while al-Khassaf considers it commendable (hasan). The preferred view, as upheld by al-Sadr al-Shahid, is that it is obligatory because the judge is appointed to protect the rights of the incapable. However, other texts indicate that taking a surety is precautionary rather than necessary. The passage also discusses whether a surety should be taken from parents as well, concluding that it is advisable for their case too, though for different reasons (to avoid neglect of the absent). The author then explains the scenario where the husband has property at home: the judge can directly assign maintenance from that property without a surety, citing the hadith of Hind. When the husband has no property, the majority view (our scholars) holds that the judge hears evidence of the marriage but does not give maintenance from absent property; instead, the woman is ordered to borrow. In contrast, Zufar (and Abu Yusuf in one narration) allows the judge to give maintenance directly from the husband's wealth if present, or order borrowing if not, and this is the practice adopted today for public convenience, being one of the six issues where Zufar's opinion is followed. The passage further details the procedure after the husband returns: if he proves he already paid maintenance, the woman must return what she took, and the husband has options against her and the surety. The issue of refusal to swear (nukul) is also discussed. Finally, it mentions conditions for the judge to prescribe maintenance: the woman's request and the husband's presence (or inability to be present). The commentary emphasizes that the judge's acceptance of evidence without proof of the husband's absence is a practical concession.

Key Terms
كفيل (kafil): A surety taken from the woman or her relatives to ensure repayment if the husband later proves he paid maintenance.
نفقة (nafaqah): Maintenance, including food, clothing, and shelter, for the wife and children which the husband is obligated to provide.
غائب (gha'ib): An absent person, specifically the husband who is away and cannot be present for the legal proceedings about maintenance.
بينة (bayyinah): Evidence, typically witness testimony, that the woman must present to prove the marriage and the husband's absence without leaving maintenance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do judges today follow Zufar's opinion regarding maintenance for an absent husband's wife when the husband has no present wealth?
A) Because it is the strongest opinion in the Hanafi madhhab based on the Quran.
B) Because it is one of the six issues where Zufar's saying is followed due to public need and convenience.
C) Because Abu Hanifa himself changed his opinion to that of Zufar.
D) Because the woman has a guaranteed right to maintenance regardless of the husband's absence.

Key Takeaway
For absent husbands with no wealth, judges follow Zufar's view: prescribe maintenance and order borrowing, due to public necessity.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
The Obligation of Maintenance During 'Iddah and Its Legal Proof
Ruling and proof for maintenance during 'iddah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that maintenance (nafaqah, kiswah, sukna) is wajib for every woman in 'iddah of divorce and explain the qiyas proof using the 'illa of confinement for lineage preservation.

Core Idea
Maintenance during 'iddah is wajib because she is confined for the sake of lineage.

This lesson examines the foundational ruling on maintenance during the 'iddah period. We will see that the Hanafi school obligates food, clothing, and housing for any divorced woman in 'iddah, whether revocable or irrevocable. The key proof is a qiyas (analogical reasoning) based on the purpose of 'iddah: preserving lineage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the opening of the passage: it states that maintenance, clothing, and housing are obligatory for a woman in 'iddah of divorce. Note that this applies to all types of divorce (revocable and irrevocable).
The phrase 'أطلق الطلاق فشمل البائن والرجعي' explicitly includes both types.
2
Locate the legal cause ('illa) for the obligation
The text says: 'لأنها جراء الاحتباس وهي محبوسة فيهما في حق حكم مقصود وهو الولد' – the woman is confined for a intended ruling, which is the child. This confinement is the effective cause.
'Jira' likely means 'because of' (correct form 'لأجل'). The confinement is for determining paternity.
3
Understand the qiyas proof
The confinement during 'iddah is analogous to confinement during marriage. In marriage, the husband must provide maintenance because the wife is confined for his benefit. Here, she is confined for the benefit of determining lineage, so maintenance is wajib by analogy.
This is a qiyas jali (clear analogy) with the 'illa of confinement for a legitimate purpose.
4
Note the epistemological status
The ruling is wajib, not fard, because the evidence is qiyas (zanni al-thubut) rather than a definitive text. The text clarifies that the obligation is based on the maqsad (purpose) of 'iddah.
Hanafi usul: qiyas yields wujub, not fard.

His saying: (And for the woman in 'iddah of divorce i.e., maintenance, clothing, and housing are obligatory for the woman in 'iddah of divorce. This is the apparent meaning of the Mukhtasar. Al-Zayla'i mentioned maintenance and housing but did not mention clothing. It is transmitted in al-Dhakhira, al-Khaniyya, al-'Inaya, and al-Mujtaba that the woman in 'iddah is entitled to clothing. They said: Muhammad only did not mention it in the book because the 'iddah is usually not long, so she is independent of it, unless she needs it, then it is prescribed for her. End. So it appears that the clothing of the woman in 'iddah is detailed: if she is independent of it due to the shortness of the period, as when her 'iddah is by menstruation and she menstruates, or by months, then no clothing for her. If she needs it due to the length of the period, as when she has an extended period of purity and does not menstruate, then the judge prescribes it for her. This is what al-Tarsusi refined in Anfa' al-Wasa'il, and it is a good refinement understood from their statements. He made divorce general, so it includes irrevocable and revocable because she is for confinement and she is confined in both regarding a intended ruling, which is the child, since 'iddah is obligatory to preserve the child, so maintenance is obligatory. In al-Mujtaba: Maintenance of 'iddah is like maintenance in marriage, and it falls with the passage of the period except by prescription or settlement. If she borrows against him while he is absent, then if it was by a judge's order, she can claim it back; without a judge's order, there is difference in narrations and shaykhs. End. In al-Dhakhira: Maintenance is obligatory for the woman in 'iddah whether the period is long or short, and her statement regarding its non-expiry is accepted with her oath. If the husband brings evidence of her admission of expiry, he is free from it. If she claims pregnancy, he spends on her between her and two years from the day he divorced her. If she says 'I thought I was pregnant and did not menstruate, and I have an extended period of purity until now, and I think what I have is wind, and I want maintenance until my 'iddah expires,' and the husband says 'you claimed pregnancy and its maximum is two years,' the judge does not pay attention to his statement and maintenance is obligatory on him as long as the 'iddah has not expired, either by three menstruations or by her entering the age of menopause and three months passing after that. If she menstruates during these three months, she starts a new 'iddah by menstruation and maintenance is obligatory for her all that unless a judgment of expiry of 'iddah is made. Similarly in al-Khulasa. An incident occurred in our time where she claimed pregnancy and he did not believe her, so maintenance was prescribed for her on condition that if she is not pregnant she returns it. It is obvious that this condition is invalid. In al-Khulasa: If the woman in 'iddah does not take maintenance until her 'iddah expires, her maintenance falls. This is when it is not prescribed. As for when it is prescribed, al-Sadr al-Qadi mentioned... Maintenance of the absentee from the city, whether there is travel duration between them or not, as in al-Munya. It is appropriate that... of the hidden one in the city and includes the missing person. End. I said: And Fatawa Ahu (al-Sayrafi) ... His saying: (And al-Sarakhsi indicated that it does not fall) In most copies it is thus; in some copies 'it falls' without 'la'. The correct is... So on this, the texts must be corrected. He said: And in al-Nahr: The general statements of the texts indicate what al-Halwani chose. Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq vol. 4 p. 22. 338 Book of Divorce Chapter of Maintenance. The martyr in al-Fatawa al-Sughra from Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said: In my selected view, it does not fall. End. The dispute is also mentioned in al-Khaniyya. In al-Dhakhira: If the judge ordered her to borrow and she borrowed, she can claim reimbursement from the husband because it is as if he borrowed himself. If the judge did not order her to borrow, then there is dispute. Al-Sarakhsi indicated that it falls where he reasoned: The entitlement to this maintenance is the 'iddah, and the entitled by this cause is like a cause, so the cause must exist for entitlement of claim. Do you not see that if a dhimmi becomes Muslim and has jizya on his head, he is not demanded for any part of it? So here too. This is the correct view. End. So on this, the texts must be corrected because they state that it becomes due by judgment or consent and becomes a debt, but here it does not become a debt by judgment unless the 'iddah has not expired... In al-Dhakhira: The husband is responsible for the housing expense of the woman in 'iddah. If he does not own a house, he rents a house for her and the rent is on him. If he is poor, the woman is ordered to borrow the rent and then claim from him when he becomes wealthy, as is the ruling in maintenance during marriage. If the divorce is irrevocable, if the house is owned by the husband, the husband should leave the house and move away from her, leaving her in that house until her 'iddah expires. Similarly, if the house is rented. If he rents another house for her, it is permissible, but it is better to leave her in the house they were living in before divorce. If the divorce is revocable, al-Khassaf mentioned that he houses her in the house they were living in before divorce, but the husband leaves or moves away from her in a corner of it. End. Also in it: If the woman in 'iddah leaves the house of 'iddah, her maintenance falls as long as she persists in nushuz. If she returns to the husband's house, she has maintenance and housing. Then, leaving the house of 'iddah continuously is not a condition for her maintenance to fall: if she leaves for a time and stays for a time, she does not deserve maintenance. In Fatawa al-Nasafi: The woman in 'iddah from an irrevocable divorce who marries during 'iddah, consummates, and they are separated, and 'iddah is obligatory from both: no maintenance on the second husband due to its invalidity, and she has maintenance on the first if she does not leave the house of 'iddah. If she leaves, then she has none, and she is not described as being nashiz by preventing herself from him here because the divorce is irrevocable and the permission is gone. End. In al-Dhakhira also: If a man settles with his wife regarding her maintenance during 'iddah for a specified dirhams, not increasing it until the 'iddah expires, we see: if her 'iddah is by menstruation, the settlement is not valid due to ignorance; if by months, it is valid due to its absence. If he divorces her or irrevocably separates and then settles with her for housing for dirhams, it is not valid because it leads to nullifying Allah's right regarding housing. In al-Muhit: He divorced her with khul' on condition that she has no maintenance and no housing, so she has housing without maintenance because maintenance is her right, so it is valid to release from it, unlike housing. In al-Walwaljiyya: His nikah... His saying: (The settlement is not valid due to ignorance) In it there is that ignorance of what is settled for does not harm, so ponder. His saying: (Unless it is)
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the maintenance of a woman in 'iddah (waiting period) after divorce. The author first clarifies the ruling: a woman in 'iddah of divorce is entitled to maintenance (nafaqah), clothing (kiswah), and housing (sukna). This is general for both revocable and irrevocable divorce. The reason given is that she is confined for the sake of preserving lineage (al-walad), as the 'iddah is prescribed to determine paternity. The discussion then focuses on clothing: some Hanafi scholars (like Zayla'i) omit it, but majority (Dhakhira, Khaniyya, etc.) consider it obligatory. However, al-Marghinani (author of Hidayah) and others specify that clothing is only due if needed due to a long 'iddah (e.g., extended purity without menstruation); if the 'iddah is short (by menstrual cycles or months), clothing is not required. This is the refined position of Tarsusi. Next, the passage addresses when maintenance falls: it falls with the end of 'iddah unless it was fixed by a judge (farad) or settlement (sulh). If the wife borrowed money without a judge's order, there is disagreement among the mashayikh. The text details the case of a woman claiming pregnancy: the husband must pay maintenance for up to two years from divorce, and her word is accepted regarding non-expiry of 'iddah. An incident is mentioned where a judge prescribed maintenance conditionally—this condition is invalid. The passage then discusses the difference between prescribed and unprescribed maintenance: if prescribed, it does not fall even if 'iddah ends; if not prescribed, it falls. There is a dispute between Sarakhsi (who says it falls) and Halwani (who says it does not) regarding maintenance for an absent husband. The correct view is stated to be that of Sarakhsi—the cause (the 'iddah itself) must exist for the entitlement, analogized to the dhimmi's jizya not being demanded after Islam. The housing expense is the husband's duty; if the house is owned by him, he must vacate and leave it for her during 'iddah (especially in irrevocable divorce). For revocable divorce, he moves away within the same house. Leaving the house of 'iddah for a short time does not cancel maintenance if she returns, but continuous departure cancels it. If she marries during 'iddah and consummates, she has no maintenance from the second husband (invalid marriage), and the first husband's maintenance is conditional on her not leaving the house. Settlement for maintenance during 'iddah is only valid if the 'iddah is by months (known duration), not by menstruation (unknown). Settlement for housing is invalid because housing is a right of Allah (related to the 'iddah itself, not purely financial). In khul', she can waive maintenance but not housing. The passage ends with a comment on the principle that ignorance of the subject matter in settlement (sulh) generally invalidates it, but here ignorance does not harm—so the text requires reflection.

Key Terms
نفقة (nafaqah): Maintenance including food, clothing, and lodging for a woman during 'iddah
عدة ('iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death before remarrying
كسوة (kiswah): Clothing that the husband must provide for the woman during 'iddah if needed
سكنى (sukna): Housing that must be provided for the woman during 'iddah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary proof for making maintenance (nafaqah) during 'iddah wajib?
A) A direct Quranic verse
B) A hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him)
C) Qiyas (analogy) based on confinement for preserving lineage
D) Ijma' (consensus) of the Companions

Key Takeaway
Maintenance during 'iddah (food, clothing when needed, housing) is wajib on the husband for all types of divorce, proven by qiyas on the basis of confinement for lineage preservation.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
6 min
The Detailed Ruling on Clothing (Kiswah) During 'Iddah
Dispute and refinement on clothing during 'iddah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on clothing for the woman in 'iddah and state when it is obligatory based on the length of the 'iddah.

Core Idea
Clothing is wajib only if the 'iddah is long; if short, she is independent.

While the general obligation of maintenance includes clothing, the Hanafi school specifies that clothing is not automatically due. This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi discussion on kiswah and the refined position that clothing is only prescribed when the 'iddah is extended, such as when the woman has an extended period of purity without menstruation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling on clothing
The passage begins by stating that the apparent meaning of the Mukhtasar is that clothing is obligatory. But then it notes that al-Zayla'i omitted clothing from his list. This signals a dispute.
The omission by Zayla'i is significant because he is a major Hanafi commentator.
2
Understand the majority position
The passage cites al-Dhakhira, al-Khaniyya, al-'Inaya, and al-Mujtaba that the woman is entitled to clothing. They explain that Muhammad (al-Shaybani) did not mention it because the 'iddah is usually short, but if needed, it is prescribed.
This shows that the obligation is conditional on need.
3
Learn Tarsusi's refinement
Al-Tarsusi in Anfa' al-Wasa'il refined the position: if the 'iddah is short (by menstruation or months), no clothing; if it is long (extended purity), the judge prescribes it. This is presented as a good refinement.
Tarsusi's view is considered the preferred one by the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.
4
Apply to examples
Apply: A woman whose 'iddah is by three menstrual cycles typically lasts about three months – short, so no clothing. A woman who has delayed menstruation and her 'iddah could be a year or more – she needs clothing.
The key is whether she is independent (تستغني) due to short duration.
