Apostasy and Maintenance after Final Divorce: The Role of Imprisonment
Commentary on the effect of apostasy and allowing access on post-divorce maintenance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on maintenance of an apostate woman after a final divorce and identify the operative legal cause (imprisonment) that determines the ruling.

Core Idea
Maintenance during 'iddah depends on confinement in the marital home; apostasy drops maintenance only because it leads to imprisonment.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: why does apostasy after a final divorce drop maintenance, but allowing the husband's son access does not? The key is not the sin itself but the consequence — imprisonment prevents confinement in the 'iddah home. We will unpack the commentator's reasoning and see how this principle applies across cases like the nashizah and the woman who joins dar al-harb.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text compares a woman who apostatizes after a final divorce (bainunah) with one who allows the husband's son access (tamkin). Both involve separation by divorce, but only apostasy drops maintenance.
Apostasy leads to imprisonment; tamkin does not.
2
Find the hidden cause
The commentator argues that the operative cause ('illah) is not apostasy or tamkin per se, but whether the woman is confined (muhtabisa) in the house of 'iddah. The apostate is imprisoned, so she cannot be confined; the one who allows access is free, so confinement is possible.
Imprisonment (habs) prevents ihtibas.
3
Apply the general principle
The text quotes al-Muhit: every woman who has no maintenance on the day of divorce has no maintenance ever, except the nashizah. For the apostate, maintenance was already wajib on the day of divorce; it drops only because imprisonment prevents confinement. If she repents and returns to confinement, maintenance resumes.
Nashizah regains maintenance by returning to obedience; apostate can regain by returning to confinement after repentance.
4
Distinguish the irrevocable drop
If apostasy itself ends the marriage (e.g., apostasy before divorce), then maintenance never becomes wajib and cannot be restored. This is different from apostasy after bainunah, where maintenance was initially wajib.
Compare 'mubānah bi al-riddah' vs 'murtaddah after bainunah'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وردتها بعد البت تسقط نفقتها لا تمكين ابنه يعني لو طلقها بائناً ثم ارتدت سقطت نفقتها، ولو مكنت ابن زوجها بعد البينونة لا تسقط مع أن الفرقة فيهما بالطلاق لا من جهتها بمعصية لأن المرتدة تحبس حتى تتوب ولا نفقة للمحبوسة والممكنة لا تحبس فلهذا تقع الفرقة وفي الحقيقة لا فرق بين المسئلتين لأن المرتدة بعد البينونة لو لم تحبس تجب لها النفقة كما في غاية البيان والمحيط كالممكنة والممكنة إذا لم تلزم بيت العدة لا نفقة لها، فليس للردة أو التمكين دخل في الإسقاط وعدمه، بل إن وجد الاحتباس في بيت العدة وجبت وإلا فلا. ولو حبست المعتدة للردة ثم تابت ورجعت تجب النفقة لعود الاحتباس كالناشزة إذا عادت لزوال المانع بخلاف المبانة بالردة إذا أسلمت لا تعود نفقتها لسقوط نفقتها أصلاً بمعصيتها والساقط لا يعود ولو لحقت بدار الحرب ثم عادت وتابت فلا نفقة لها لسقوط العدة بالالتحاق حكماً لتباين الدارين لأنه بمنزلة الموت فانعدم السبب الموجب، قيد بالطلاق البائن لأن المعتدة عن رجعي إذا طاوعت ابن زوجها أو قبلها بشهوة فلا نفقة لها لأن الفرقة لم تقع بالطلاق وإنما وقعت بسبب وجد منها وهو معصيتها. وأطلقه فشمل البائن بالواحدة أو بالثلاث وما في الهداية من تقييده بالثلاث اتفاقي وفي المحيط : الأصل أن كل امرأة لا نفقة لها يوم الطلاق فليس لها النفقة أبداً إلا الناشزة كالمعتدة عن النكاح الفاسد والأمة المزوجة إذا لم يبوئها المولى بيتاً .اهـ. ثم قال بعده ولو طلقها وهي مبوأة فلها النفقة، فإن أخرجها المولى بطلت فإن أعادها عادت النفقة فلو بوأها بعد الطلاق الرجعي وجبت النفقة لأنها منكوحة بخلاف المبانة .
His statement: (And her apostasy after a final divorce drops her maintenance, not her allowing her son [access]). Meaning: If he divorced her irrevocably then she apostatized, her maintenance drops. But if she allowed her husband’s son access after final divorce, it does not drop, although the separation in both cases is due to divorce, not from her side by sin. Because the apostate is imprisoned until she repents, and there is no maintenance for the imprisoned woman. The one who allows access is not imprisoned, so for this reason the separation occurs. In reality, there is no difference between the two cases, because if the apostate after final divorce had not been imprisoned, she would be entitled to maintenance, as in Ghayat al-Bayan and al-Muhit, like the one who allows access. And the one who allows access, if she does not confine herself to the house of 'iddah, she has no maintenance. So apostasy or tamkin has no influence on the dropping or non-dropping. Rather, if confinement in the house of 'iddah exists, maintenance is obligatory; otherwise not. And if the woman in 'iddah is imprisoned for apostasy, then repents and returns, maintenance becomes obligatory due to the return of confinement, like the nashizah when she returns due to removal of the impediment. Unlike the one separated by apostasy when she becomes Muslim, her maintenance does not return because her maintenance was dropped entirely by her sin, and what has dropped does not return. And if she joins the abode of war then returns and repents, there is no maintenance for her because the 'iddah is legally dropped by joining due to the difference of the two abodes, as it is like death, so the cause of obligation is absent. It is restricted to final divorce because the woman in 'iddah from a revocable divorce, if she allows her husband’s son access or kisses him with desire, there is no maintenance for her because the separation did not occur by divorce but by a cause from her side, which is her sin. And he released it, so it includes final divorce by one or three. What is in al-Hidayah restricting it to three is coincidental. In al-Muhit: The principle is that every woman who has no maintenance on the day of divorce has no maintenance ever, except the nashizah, like the woman in 'iddah from an invalid marriage, and the married slave woman when the master does not provide a house for her. End. Then he said after that: If he divorces her while she is housed, she has maintenance; if the master removes her, it becomes void; if he returns her, maintenance returns. If he houses her after revocable divorce, maintenance becomes obligatory because she is a wife, unlike the irrevocably divorced woman.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the maintenance of a divorced woman. It examines two scenarios: apostasy (riddah) after a final divorce (bainunah) and allowing the husband's son to have access (tamkin). The key insight is that the determining factor is whether the woman is imprisoned (habs) in the marital home during her 'iddah. The apostate woman is imprisoned until she repents, so she loses maintenance because she cannot remain in the home. The woman who allows access is not imprisoned, so her maintenance remains. The text then clarifies that apostasy or tamkin themselves are not the cause; rather, the presence or absence of confinement (ihtibas) in the house of 'iddah determines the right to maintenance. If she returns to Islam and resumes confinement, maintenance returns, unlike the case where she joins the abode of war, which nullifies the 'iddah entirely. The passage also quotes al-Muhit establishing the general principle: any woman who lacks maintenance on the day of divorce will never have maintenance, except the nashizah (disobedient wife) who can regain it by returning to obedience. Examples are given of the woman in 'iddah from an invalid marriage and the married slave woman without a house from her master.

Key Terms
الردة (ar-riddah): Apostasy from Islam, which in this context leads to imprisonment (habs) until repentance.
البائن (al-bā'in): A final, irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately; the wife must observe 'iddah but is not a wife.
المحبوسة (al-maḥbūsah): The imprisoned woman, here referring to the apostate who is detained until she repents.
النشوز (an-nushūz): Disobedience of the wife, which can be rectified; the nashizah loses maintenance but regains it upon return to obedience.
العدة (al-'iddah): The waiting period after divorce or death; during this period, the woman is entitled to maintenance under certain conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does maintenance drop for a woman who apostatizes after a final divorce?
A) Because apostasy is a major sin.
B) Because she is imprisoned until she repents.
C) Because her 'iddah ends.
D) Because she is no longer Muslim.

Key Takeaway
Maintenance during 'iddah after final divorce is conditional on the wife's confinement in the marital home; apostasy drops maintenance only because it leads to imprisonment, not because of the sin itself.

The Mother's Prohibition of Accepting Wages for Nursing
Commentary on the prohibition of hiring a mother as wet nurse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mother accepting payment for nursing her own child and explain the Quranic proof and the concept of diyanatan.

Core Idea
A mother is religiously obliged to nurse; accepting wages for it is haram because the obligation makes the act wajib upon her.

This lesson examines a key ruling from Kanz al-Daqaiq: a mother (whether wife or in 'iddah) cannot be hired to nurse her own child. The Quranic verse (2:233) establishes her religious duty, and accepting payment would contradict that obligation. We will unpack the proof and the Hanafi distinction between legal and religious enforceability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The passage states: a woman who is a wife or in 'iddah cannot be hired to nurse her own child. Identify the act (istijar) and the ruling (haram).
2
Locate the Quranic proof
The author cites Surah al-Baqarah 2:233. Understand that the verse is a command, which in Hanafi usul indicates wujub.
The verse: 'And mothers shall nurse their children for two complete years.'
3
Apply the concept of diyanatan
The obligation is diyanatan (religious), not qada'an (enforceable). This means the mother is morally bound, but if she refuses, the court cannot force her (though she may be compelled by other means).
4
Trace the reasoning for prohibition
If she accepts payment, her ability to nurse is established, so the act becomes wajib and she cannot take wages for a wajib act. That is why it is haram.
5
Note the scope: wife and mu'taddah
The ruling covers both a wife and a woman in 'iddah (revocable and irrevocable). For irrevocable, there is a difference of opinion, which will be covered later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو معتدة وهي أحق بعدها ما لم تطلب زيادة ولأبويه وأجداده وجداته لو فقراء ولا الخلاف عند قدرة الأب بالمال. وفي غاية البيان معزياً إلى التتمة عن إجارة العيون عن محمد فيمن استأجر ظئر الصبي شهراً فلما انقضى الشهر أبت أن ترضعه والصبي لا يقبل ثدي غيرها قال: أجبرها أن ترضع قوله: (ويستأجر من يرضعه عندها) أي ويستأجر الأب من يرضع الطفل عند الأم لأن الحضانة لها والنفقة عليه أطلقه هنا وقيده في الهداية بإرادة الأم للحضانة وهو مبني على ما صححه من أن الأم لا تجبر عليها لأنها حقها، وعلى ما اختاره الفقهاء الثلاثة من الجبر فليس معلقاً بإرادتها لأنها حق الصبي عليها. وفي الذخيرة: لا يجب على الظئر أن تمكث في بيت الأم إذا لم يشترط عليها ذلك وقت العقد وكان الولد يستغني عن الظئر في تلك الحالة، بل لها أن ترضع وتعود إلى منزلها كما لها أن تحمل الصبي إلى منزلها أو تقول أخرجوه فترضعه عند فناء الدار ثم تدخل الولد على الوالدة إلا أن يشرط عند العقد أن الظئر تكون عند الأم فحينئذ يلزمها الوفاء بذلك الشرط اهـ. وفي الخزانة عن التفاريق: لا تجب في الحضانة أجرة المسكن الذي يحضن فيه الصبي. وقال آخرون: تجب إن كان للصبي مال وإلا فعلى من يجب عليه نفقته اهـ. قوله: (لا أمة لو منكوحة أو معتدة) أي لا يستأجر أمه لو منكوحته أو معتدته لأن الإرضاع مستحق عليها ديانة قال الله تعالى: {والوالدات يرضعن أولادهن حولين كاملين} [البقرة: 233] إلا أنها عذرت لاحتمال عجزها، فإذا أقدمت عليه بالأجر ظهرت قدرتها فكان الفعل واجباً عليها فلا يجوز أخذ الأجر عليه أطلق نفي المعتدة فشمل المعتدة عن رجعي وبائن وهو في الرجعي رواية واحدة، وفي البائن في رواية وفي رواية أخرى جاز استئجارها لأن النكاح قد زال وجه الأول أنه باق في حق بعض الأحكام؛ كذا في الهداية. قوله: (تجبر الأم على الإرضاع عند الكل) قال الرملي: نقل الزيلعي ذلك عن الخصاف وزاد عليه قوله وتجعل الأجرة ديناً عليه اهـ. قلت: ومثله في المجمع قوله: (قال أجبرها أن ترضع) عبارة الفتاوى الهندية عن الوجيز تجبر على إبقاء الإجارة بالإرضاع قوله: (وفي الخزانة عن التفاريق لا تجب في الحضانة أجرة المسكن) قال الغزي: وأما لزوم مسكن الحاضنة فاختلف فيه من غير ترجيح صريح، وإن كان تأخير وجه المنع يدل على أنه المختار عنده كما وصحح في الجوهرة الجواز فكان الأولى للمصنف أن يقيد المعتدة بالرجعي وذكر في فتح القدير عن بعضهم أن ظاهر الرواية الجواز. وقيد بالأم لأنه لو استأجر منكوحته لترضع ولده من غيرها جاز لأنه لم يجب عليها إرضاعه بخلاف الأم لأنه وجب عليها إرضاعه ديانة كما قدمناه عن الهداية، وظاهره أنه لا يجوز لها أخذ الأجر من مال الصغير لو كان له مال لكن في الذخيرة: هذا إذا لم يكن للصغير مال، أما إذا كان له مال هل يجوز أن يفرض أجرة الرضاع في ماله؟ ذكر الصدر الشهيد أنه روي عن محمد أنه يفرض في مال الصبي. وهكذا ذكر في إجارات القدوري وليس فيه اختلاف الروايتين ولكن ما روي عن محمد أنه يفرض في مال الصبي تأويله إذا لم يكن للأب مال، وما ذكر أن الزوج إذا استأجرها لا يجوز تأويله إذا فرض أجرة الرضاع من مال نفسه فلا تستحق ذلك كيلا يؤدي إلى اجتماع أجر الرضاع مع النكاح في مال واحد وهذا المعنى لا يتحقق إذا فرض لها في مال الصغير فقلنا إنها تستحق ذلك اهـ. فالحاصل أن على تعليل صاحب الهداية لا تأخذ شيئاً في مقابلة الإرضاع من الزوج ولا من مال الصغير لوجوبه عليها وعلى ما علل به في الذخيرة من أن المنع إنما هو لاجتماع واجبين في مال وفي المجتبى لو استأجر زوجته من مال الصبي لإرضاعه جاز وفي ماله لا يجوز حتى لا يجتمع عليه نفقة النكاح والإرضاع اهـ. والأظهر لزوم ذلك كما في بعض المعتبرات .اهـ. أقول وهذا يعلم من قولهم إذا احتاج الصغير إلى خادم يلزم الأب به فإن احتياجه إلى المسكن مقرر؛ كذا في حاشية الرملي قوله: (وصحح في الجوهرة الجواز) وفي الفتاوى الهندية: المعتدة عن طلاق بائن أو طلقات ثلاث في رواية ابن زياد تستحق أجر الرضاعة وعليه الفتوى؛ هكذا في جواهر الأخلاطي اهـ قوله: (تأويله إذا لم يكن للأب مال) لعل المراد أنه إذا لم يكن للأب مال دفعه إليها بل دفع من مال الصبي. وإنما قلنا ذلك به في الذخيرة أيضاً وسيأتي نحوه عن المجتبى أن إرضاع الصغير إذا كان يوجد من يرضعه إنما تجب على الأب إذا لم يكن للصغير مال، أما إذا كان له مال بأن ماتت أمه فورث مالاً أو استفاده بسبب آخر يكون مؤنة الرضاع في مال الصغير، وكذلك نفقة الصبي بعد الفطام إذا كان له مال في ماله .اهـ. فليس فرضه في مال الصبي متوقفاً على أن لا يكون للأب مال، ولعل الأظهر أن يقال: تأويله إذا كان للابن مال تأمل قوله: فالحاصل أن على تعليل صاحب الهداية لا تأخذ شيئاً الخ قال في النهر والأوجه عندي عدم الجواز ويدل على ذلك ما قالوه من أنه لو استأجر منكوحته لإرضاع ولده من غيرها جاز من غير ذكر خلاف لأنه غير واجب عليها مع أن فيه اجتماع أجرة الرضاع والنفقة في مال واحد، ولو صلح مانعاً لما جاز هنا فتدبره اهـ. وحاصله أن التعليل باجتماع واجبين لا مفهوم له لأنه غير مؤثر في المنع بدليل المسألة المذكورة فلا يقال إذا لم يجتمع الواجبان يجوز فيتعين تعليل صاحب الهداية المفيد عدم الجواز فمبنى الاستدلال على عدم
Or a woman in waiting period, and she is more entitled after her as long as she does not ask for an increase, and to his parents and grandparents and grandmothers if they are poor, and no dispute when father is capable with wealth. And in Ghayat al-Bayan citing from al-Tatimma about hiring of wet nurses, from Muhammad concerning one who hired a wet nurse for a child for a month, then when the month ended she refused to nurse him and the child would not accept the breast of anyone else: he said, 'I compel her to nurse.' His statement: (And one hires someone to nurse him at her [the mother's] place) meaning the father hires someone to nurse the child at the mother's because custody belongs to her and maintenance is on him. He made it absolute here and restricted it in al-Hidayah to the mother's desire for custody, which is based on what he adopted that the mother is not compelled to [nurse] because it is her right, and on what the three jurists chose of compulsion, so it is not dependent on her desire because it is the child's right upon her. In al-Dhakhira: It is not obligatory on the wet nurse to stay in the mother's house if that was not stipulated at the time of the contract and the child is independent of the wet nurse in that situation; rather she may nurse and return to her home, just as she may carry the child to her home or say 'take him out' and nurse him at the door of the house then bring the child in to the mother, unless it was stipulated at the contract that the wet nurse be with the mother, then she is bound to fulfill that condition. In al-Khizanah from al-Tafariq: The rent of the dwelling where the child is raised is not obligatory in custody. And others said: It is obligatory if the child has wealth, otherwise on the one who is obliged to spend on him. His statement: (Not an enslaved woman if married or in waiting period) meaning one does not hire his mother [the child's mother] if she is his wife or in waiting period, because nursing is due upon her diyanatan [religiously], Allah Almighty said: 'And mothers shall nurse their children for two complete years' [2:233], except that she is excused due to the possibility of her inability; if she undertakes it for payment, her ability becomes apparent, so the act becomes obligatory upon her, so it is not permissible to take payment for it. He made the prohibition of the woman in waiting period absolute, so it includes the woman in waiting period from a revocable and irrevocable divorce, and concerning the revocable it is one narration, and concerning the irrevocable there is one narration and in another narration it is permissible to hire her because the marriage has ended; the first view is based on its remaining in some rulings; as in al-Hidayah. His statement: (The mother is compelled to nurse according to all) al-Ramli said: al-Zayla'i transmitted that from al-Khassaf and added to it his statement 'and the payment is made a debt upon him.' I say: and similar is in al-Majma'. His statement: (He said: I compel her to nurse) the expression of al-Fatawa al-Hindiyyah from al-Wajiz: she is compelled to fulfill the lease by nursing. His statement: (And in al-Khizanah from al-Tafariq, the rent of the dwelling is not obligatory in custody) al-Ghazzi said: As for the obligation of the dwelling for the custodian, there is disagreement without clear preference, though delaying the ground of prohibition indicates it is his choice, and as was adopted in al-Jawharah permissibility, so it would have been better for the author to restrict the woman in waiting period to the revocable, and it was mentioned in Fath al-Qadir from some that the apparent of the narration is permissibility. He restricted it to the mother because if he hired his married wife to nurse his child from another woman, it is permissible because it was not obligatory upon her to nurse him, unlike the mother because it was obligatory upon her to nurse him diyanatan as we presented from al-Hidayah. And its apparent is that it is not permissible for her to take payment from the child's wealth if he has wealth, but in al-Dhakhira: this is if the child has no wealth; if he has wealth, is it permissible to stipulate the nursing fee from his wealth? al-Sadr al-Shahid mentioned that it is narrated from Muhammad that he stipulates it from the child's wealth. And thus it was mentioned in Ijarat al-Quduri, and there is no difference between the two narrations, but what is narrated from Muhammad that he stipulates it from the child's wealth is interpreted as when the father has no wealth; and what is mentioned that if the husband hires her it is not permissible is interpreted as when he stipulates the nursing fee from his own wealth, so she does not deserve it, so as not to lead to combining the nursing fee and maintenance with marriage in one wealth, and this meaning does not materialize if he stipulates for her from the child's wealth, so we say she deserves it. So the conclusion is that according to the reasoning of the author of al-Hidayah, she does not take anything in exchange for nursing from the husband nor from the child's wealth due to its being obligatory upon her, and according to what was reasoned in al-Dhakhira, the prohibition is only due to the combination of two obligations in one wealth. In al-Mujtaba: if he hired his wife from the child's wealth to nurse him, it is permissible, and from his own wealth it is not permissible, so as not to combine the maintenance of marriage and nursing on him. And the more apparent is its necessity as in some reliable works. I say: and this is known from their statement: if the child needs a servant, the father is obliged to provide it, for his need for the dwelling is established; as in Hashiyat al-Ramli. His statement: (And it was adopted in al-Jawharah permissibility) and in al-Fatawa al-Hindiyyah: the woman in waiting period from an irrevocable divorce or three divorces, in the narration of Ibn Ziyad, she deserves the nursing fee, and upon it is the fatwa; thus in Jawahir al-Akhlati. His statement: (Interpreted as when the father has no wealth) perhaps meaning that when the father has no wealth, he pays it to her but pays from the child's wealth. And we only said that in al-Dhakhira also, and similar will come from al-Mujtaba that nursing of the child, if someone is available to nurse him, is only obligatory on the father if the child has no wealth; if he has wealth, such as if his mother died and he inherited wealth or acquired it through another means, the expense of nursing is from the child's wealth. And likewise the maintenance of the child after weaning, if he has wealth, from his wealth. So stipulating from the child's wealth is not conditional on the father having no wealth; perhaps the more apparent is to say: its interpretation is when the child has wealth. Contemplate his statement: 'So the conclusion is that according to the reasoning of the author of al-Hidayah, she does not take anything...' He said in al-Nahr: the more correct in my view is non-permissibility, and it is indicated by what they said: if he hired his married wife to nurse his child from another woman, it is permissible without mention of disagreement, because it is not obligatory upon her, despite the combination of nursing fee and maintenance in one wealth; if it were a valid impediment, it would not be permissible here, so reflect. And its summary is that the reasoning by combination of two obligations has no meaning, because it is not effective in the prohibition, as evidenced by the mentioned case; so it cannot be said that if the two obligations do not combine, it is permissible. Thus the reasoning of the author of al-Hidayah indicates non-permissibility, so the basis of inference is on non-
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq deals with rulings on hiring a wet nurse (istijar al-dharr) for a child, focusing on two main issues: (1) whether the mother can be forced to nurse her own child, and (2) whether a wife or woman in 'iddah can be hired to nurse her child. The commentary expands on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq, providing evidence, intra-Hanafi differences, and later fatwa positions.

The first part discusses hiring a wet nurse to nurse the child at the mother's house. The father is obligated to pay for the wet nurse, but the wet nurse is not required to stay at the mother's house unless stipulated. The mother's right to custody is acknowledged, but the child's right to nursing overrides.

The second part addresses the prohibition of hiring an enslaved woman (أمة) who is either the father's wife or a woman in 'iddah. The Quranic verse (2:233) establishes that mothers are religiously obligated to nurse their own children; accepting payment would indicate ability and thus make the act wajib without compensation. For the wife in 'iddah, there is a riwaya difference: according to one, hiring her is prohibited; according to another, it is permissible if the iddah is bain (irrevocable). The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that an irrevocably divorced woman may be hired, as stated in Fatawa Hindiyya.

The third part addresses whether mothers are compelled to nurse. The three jurists (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree on compulsion, though some earlier texts differ. The child's right is emphasized.

The final part discusses paying the nursing fee from the child's own wealth. If the child has wealth, it can be used; otherwise, the father must pay. The reasoning of al-Hidayah (prohibition) is contrasted with al-Dhakhira (permitted from child's wealth to avoid combining two obligations in one wealth). Al-Nahr prefers non-permissibility for the wife, but the majority allow it from the child's wealth.

Key Terms
الظئر (al-dharr): A wet nurse hired to nurse a child; also called مرضعة.
معتدة (mu'taddah): A woman in the waiting period ('iddah) after divorce or death of husband.
ديانة (diyanatan): Religiously obligatory, but not enforceable in court; as opposed to قضاء.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this lesson, why is it haram for a wife to accept wages for nursing her own child?
A) Because it is not permitted in the contract of marriage.
B) Because the Quran commands nursing without compensation.
C) Because nursing is wajib upon her diyanatan, and accepting wages for a wajib act is invalid.
D) Because the father cannot pay for nursing as maintenance.

Key Takeaway
A mother's nursing is a religious duty; she cannot charge for it, but she is excused if unable, and the father must provide for the child's care.

Hiring a Divorced Wife for Breastfeeding During 'Iddah
Intra-Hanafi dispute with reasoning analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the different Hanafi positions on hiring a divorced wife for breastfeeding during 'iddah and identify the relied-upon view.

Core Idea
The permissibility depends on the type of divorce and source of payment.

The Hanafi school has a nuanced dispute on whether a woman in 'iddah can be hired to breastfeed her own child. Al-Hidayah prohibits it, al-Jawhara permits it, and later authorities like al-Fatawa al-Hindiyyah adopt the permissive view for irrevocable divorces. Understanding the reasoning behind these positions is essential for issuing correct fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position in al-Hidayah
State the prohibition view and its basis: the mother is obliged to breastfeed, so she cannot demand wages.
Obligation is diyanah (religious duty).
2
Identify the opposing position in al-Jawhara
State the permissive view and its support from Ibn Ziyad's riwayah and later texts.
Fatawa al-Hindiyyah adopts this as mufta bihi.
3
Analyze the reasoning based on combination of obligations
Understand the argument that prohibition arises from combining wage and maintenance in one wealth, and its refutation using the case of hiring a non-marital relative.
The combination argument is deemed ineffective.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a woman in bāʾin ʿiddah may demand wages; a woman in rajʿī may not, according to some.
The source of payment (child's wealth vs. husband's wealth) also matters.
5
Apply the tarjih mechanism
Trace how later Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Fatawa al-Hindiyyah) weighed the evidence and established the mufta bihi.
The permissive view is relied upon.

Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage addresses the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a woman can be hired to breastfeed her own child during her 'iddah period. The central issue is whether the obligation of breastfeeding upon her prevents her from receiving wages. The commentary expands on the differences among Hanafi authorities. Al-Hidāyah takes the position that she may not take wages from the husband because it is obligatory upon her. However, al-Jawhara corrects that it is permissible, and this is supported by the riwāyah of Ibn Ziyād. The dispute is further nuanced by whether the child has his own wealth. If the child has wealth, some narrations from Imam Muhammad allow setting wages from that wealth. The author reconciles the different views by explaining that the prohibition is only when the husband pays from his own wealth, as it would combine the wage and maintenance obligation. When the child has wealth, there is no combination. The commentary then criticizes the reasoning that combines two obligations, pointing out that in the case of hiring a non-marriageable relative, there is also a combination of wage and maintenance, yet it is permissible. Therefore, the true reason is the obligation itself, not the combination. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to al-Fatāwā al-Hindiyyah is that a woman in an irrevocable divorce (bā'in) deserves the wage.

Key Terms
معتدة (muʿtaddah): A woman observing the waiting period (ʿiddah) after divorce or death.
إرضاع (irḍāʿ): Breastfeeding a child by a woman.
أجرة الرضاع (ujrat al-riḍāʿ): Wage paid for breastfeeding, distinct from maintenance (nafaqah).
مال الصغير (māl al-ṣaghīr): Wealth belonging to the minor child, e.g., from inheritance or gift.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of hiring a divorced wife for breastfeeding during ʿiddah depends on the type of divorce and the source of payment; the relied-upon view allows it for bāʾin divorce from the child's wealth if the father is unable.

Mother's Right to Breastfeed After 'Iddah: Priority and Compensation
Ruling with proof: mother's breastfeeding priority and ujrah nature

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the mother's entitlement to breastfeed after 'iddah and explain why the payment is ujrah, not nafaqah.

Core Idea
After 'iddah, the mother is entitled to a fair wage for breastfeeding; the payment is a debt, not maintenance.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the mother's priority to breastfeed after her 'iddah expires. It addresses when she loses that priority, the nature of the compensation, and related issues like compromise and inheritance. Understanding this distinction between ujrah and nafaqah is crucial for family law.

Guided Path
1
Understand the basic ruling
The mother is more entitled to breastfeed after 'iddah unless she demands a wage higher than the market rate for a wet nurse. In that case, she loses priority and the father may hire a stranger.
The mother's priority is based on compassion, not obligation.
2
Identify the rationale for wage entitlement
After 'iddah, the marriage ends completely, so the mother is no longer entitled to maintenance (nafaqah) from the father. Therefore, her breastfeeding becomes a service compensated by a wage (ujrah).
The obligation of breastfeeding was tied to the father's obligation of maintenance during marriage/iddah.
3
Analyze the proof from Quran
The verse 2:233 establishes the father's obligation to provide for the mother during marriage and 'iddah. After 'iddah, this obligation ceases, so the wage replaces maintenance.
The proof is dalil naqli; the verse is qati' al-thubut but zanni al-dalalah regarding the post-iddah period.
4
Examine the rules of compromise (sulh)
Compromise on breastfeeding fees is impermissible during marriage or 'iddah of revocable divorce (according to one riwaya), but permissible after irrevocable divorce or after 'iddah. Conditions must avoid riba and debt-for-debt sales.
The debate reflects whether the payment is ujrah or nafaqah.
5
Distinguish ujrah from nafaqah
Ujrah is a wage for a service; it does not abate with the death of the father and is a debt on his estate. Nafaqah is maintenance arising from marriage or kinship; it abates with death (unless already due by court order).
This distinction has practical implications for inheritance and creditor rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وهي أحق بعدها بعدها ما لم تطلب زيادة أي الأم أحق بإرضاع ولدها من الأجنبية بعد انقضاء العدة ما لم تطلب أجرة زائدة على أجرة الأجنبية للإرضاع فحينئذ لا : تكون أحق. وإنما جاز لها أخذ الأجرة بعد انقضاء عدتها لأن النكاح قد زال بالكلية وصارت كالأجنبية. فإن قلت: إن وجوب الإرضاع عليها هو المانع من أخذ الأجرة وهو بعينه موجود بعد انقضائها فليست كالأجنبية . قلت : إن الوجوب عليها مقيد بإيجاب رزقها على الأب بقوله تعالى وعلى المولود له رزقهن وكسوتهن ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٣٣] ففي حال الزوجية والعدة هو قائم برزقها وفيما بعد العدة لا يقوم بشيء فتقوم الأجرة مقامة كما في فتح القدير. وإنما كانت أحق لأنها أشفق فكان نظراً للصبي في الدفع إليها، وإن التمست زيادة لم يجبر الزوج عليها دفعاً للضرر عنه وإليه الإشارة بقوله تعالى لا تضار والدة بولدها ولا مولود له بولده ﴾ [البقرة : ۲۳۳] أي بإلزامه لها أكثر من أجرة الأجنبية. وفي الذخيرة: لو صالحت المرأة زوجها عن أجر الرضاع على شيء إن كان الصلح حال قيام النكاح أو في العدة لا يجوز، وإن كان عن طلاق بائن واحدة أو ثلاثاً عن طلاق رجعي جاز على إحدى الروايتين لأن الصلح على أن يعطيها شيئاً لترضع ولدها استئجار لها، وإذا جاز الصلح فهو كما لو استأجرها على عمل آخر من الأعمال على دراهم وصالحها عن تلك الداهم على شيء بعينه جاز، وإن صالح عنها على شيء بغير عينه لا يجوز إلا أن يدفع ذلك في المجلس حتى لا يكون بيع دين بدين، وفي كل موضع جاز الاستئجار ووجبت النفقة لا تسقط بموت الزوج لأنها أجرة وليست بنفقة اهـ. وكذا ذكر في الولوالجية لا تسقط هذه الأجرة بموته بل تكون أسوة الغرماء .اهـ. فالحاصل أنه أجرة فلذا لا تتوقف على القضاء، وظاهر المتون أن الأم لو طلبت الأجرة أي أجرة المثل والأجنبية الجواز بطلان تعليل الذخيرة، وبه اندفع ما توهم من أن لفظة «عدم) في كلام النهر لعلها زائدة من النساخ قوله : (قلت إن الوجوب الخ) مقتضى هذا أنه لو وجب عليها إرضاعه بعد العدة لعدم أخذه ثدي غيرها أنه لا تستحق أجرة وهي خلاف إطلاق المصنف من أنها أحق إلا في حال طلب الزيادة فإنه يدل على أنها أحق في كل حالة إلا في حال طلب الزيادة، ويدل عليه ما مر عن غاية البيان من إجبار الظئر على الإرضاع فإنه ظاهر في أن الإجبار بالأجرة وقدمنا التصريح به عن الهندية قوله : (وفي كل موضع جاز الاستئجار أي كما إذا كان بعد انقضاء العدة أو كان في عدة البائن على إحدى الروايتين. وقوله ووجبت النفقة الظاهر أنه عطف مرادف والمراد به نفقة المرضعة بالأجرة التي تأخذها بقرينة التعليل أي أن ما تأخذه من والد الرضيع لتنفقه على نفسها بمقابلة الإرضاع هو أجرة لا نفقة فإذا مات لا تسقط هذه الأجرة بموته ولو كان نفقه لسقط كما تسقط بالموت نفقة الزوجة والقريب ولو بعد القضاء ما لم تكن مستدانة بأمر القاضي.
His statement: (And she is more entitled after her 'iddah as long as she does not demand extra) i.e., the mother is more entitled to breastfeed her child than a stranger after the expiry of the 'iddah, as long as she does not demand a wage higher than the wage of the stranger for breastfeeding; then she is not more entitled. It is permissible for her to take the wage after her 'iddah because the marriage has completely ended and she becomes like a stranger. If you say: The obligation of breastfeeding upon her is what prevents taking the wage, and it is exactly present after its expiration, so she is not like a stranger. I say: The obligation upon her is restricted to the obligation of her sustenance upon the father by His statement: {And upon the father is their provision and clothing} (2:233). So during the marriage and the 'iddah, he is responsible for her sustenance, but after the 'iddah he is not responsible for anything, so the wage replaces it as in Fath al-Qadīr. She is more entitled only because she is more compassionate, so it is in the interest of the child to give to her. If she demands extra, the husband is not compelled to agree, to prevent harm to him, and to that is reference in His statement: {A mother shall not be harmed on account of her child, nor a father on account of his child} (2:233), i.e., by compelling him to pay more than the wage of a stranger. In al-Dhakhīrah: If the woman makes a compromise with the husband concerning the wage of breastfeeding for something, if the compromise is during the marriage or during the 'iddah, it is not permissible. If it is after an irrevocable divorce (bā'in) or three divorces, or after a revocable divorce (raj'ī), it is permissible according to one of the two riwāyas, because the compromise is that he gives her something for her to breastfeed her child, which is a hiring of her. If the compromise is permissible, then it is like hiring her for any other work for dirhams and then compromising with her for those dirhams for a specific thing; it is permissible. If he compromises with her for a non-specified thing, it is not permissible unless it is paid in the session to avoid a sale of debt for debt. And in every case where hiring is permissible and the maintenance is due, it does not abate with the death of the husband because it is a wage, not maintenance. End. Likewise it is mentioned in al-Walwālijiyyah: This wage does not abate with his death; rather, she is like the rest of the creditors. End. So the conclusion is that it is a wage, hence it is not dependent on a court order. The apparent of the texts is that if the mother demands the wage (i.e., the fair wage) and the stranger... the permissibility nullifies the reasoning of al-Dhakhīrah, and with that is repelled what was suspected that the word 'عدم' in the statement of al-Nahr is perhaps an addition from the copyists. His statement: (I say: The obligation, etc.) The implication of this is that if breastfeeding were obligatory upon her after the 'iddah because she does not accept another's breast, she would not deserve a wage, and that contradicts the absolute statement of the author that she is more entitled except in the case of demanding extra. That indicates that she is more entitled in every case except in the case of demanding extra. Evidence for it is what passed from Ghāyat al-Bayān concerning compelling the wet nurse to breastfeed, for it is apparent that the compulsion is with a wage. And we have already stated this from al-Hindiyyah. His statement: (And in every place where hiring becomes permissible), i.e., as when after the expiry of the 'iddah or during the 'iddah of a bā'in divorce according to one of the two riwāyas. And his statement: 'and the maintenance is due' apparently is a synonymous conjunction, and by it is meant the maintenance of the wet nurse with the wage she takes, as indicated by the reasoning: that what she takes from the father of the infant to spend on herself in return for breastfeeding is a wage, not maintenance. So if he dies, this wage does not abate with his death. If it were maintenance, it would abate, just as the maintenance of a wife or a relative abates upon death, even after a court order, unless it was borrowed by order of the judge.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling that after the 'iddah period expires, the mother is more entitled to breastfeed her child than a stranger, but if she demands a wage higher than the market rate for a wet nurse, she loses this priority. The reason she can take wages after 'iddah is that the marriage has ended, and she is no longer entitled to maintenance from the father, so the wage compensates. The obligation of breastfeeding is linked to maintenance; once maintenance ends, the obligation is replaced by a wage. The mother's priority is due to her compassion. However, if she demands an excessive wage, the father is not compelled to pay it, to prevent harm. The passage also discusses compromise (sulh) on breastfeeding fees, stating that it is permissible only after divorce and under conditions. Finally, it emphasizes that the payment is a wage (ujrah), not maintenance (nafaqah), so it does not abate with the death of the father; it is a debt to be paid from the estate.

Key Terms
أحق (ahaqq): More entitled or more deserving, specifically of the right to breastfeed the child.
أجرة المثل (ujrat al-mithl): The fair market wage for breastfeeding, not an arbitrary amount.
صلح (ṣulḥ): Compromise or settlement, here concerning breastfeeding fees.
نفقة (nafaqah): Maintenance or financial support.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to the breastfeeding payment if the father dies?
A) It abates because it is nafaqah
B) It remains due as a debt from the estate because it is ujrah
C) It is nullified because the marriage ended
D) Only if the mother received a court order

Key Takeaway
After iddah, the mother is entitled to a fair wage for breastfeeding; this wage is a debt that does not abate with death, unlike maintenance.

Talaq — Divorce

Mother's Custody Priority When Fee Is Demanded vs. Free Offer from Aunt or Stranger
Intra-Hanafi dispute on custody fee demand vs. free offer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mother's custody priority when she demands a fee versus a paternal aunt or foreign woman offering free care, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf between the positions of al-Tabyeen and al-Walwalijiyya.

Core Idea
Mother's right to custody is primary unless she demands more than the like wage; only relatives like the paternal aunt can displace her, not strangers.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq examines a recurring modern custody dispute: when a mother demands payment for custody, but a paternal aunt or even a stranger offers to care for the child for free. Hanafi texts appear contradictory, but the author resolves by distinguishing breastfeeding from custody and by limiting the stranger's priority. This lesson unpacks the intra-madhhab dispute and the operative fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling from the matn
The matn states that the mother is more entitled in all cases except when she demands more than the wage of a foreign woman. This establishes the default: mother keeps the child unless she asks for an excessive fee.
The wage here refers to breastfeeding, not custody, as clarified later.
2
Note the explicit contrary view from al-Tabyeen
Al-Tabyeen says: if a foreign woman offers to breastfeed for free, she takes priority over the mother even if the mother asks for the like wage. This contradicts the matn's implication.
This view is limited to breastfeeding, not custody.
3
Examine the correct view from al-Walwalijiyya
The correct view is that the mother is more entitled unless she demands more than the like wage. If she demands the like wage, she keeps the child. She is told: either keep the child without fee or give him to the paternal aunt.
This view is preferred by the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq.
4
Analyze the extension to foreign women
The author argues that a foreign woman is not like a paternal aunt; the aunt has a special status as a relative. A foreign woman cannot displace the mother even if she offers free custody, because custody is a right that remains with the mother.
This distinguishes between breastfeeding (where a stranger can take over) and custody (where only relatives can).
5
Determine the practical consequence
In practice, if the mother demands the like wage, she retains custody. If she demands more, she loses to the paternal aunt (if aunt offers free), but not to a foreign woman. The father cannot force the child to a stranger.
This is the mufta bihi position according to al-Bahr al-Raiq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق باب النفقة صبي متبرعة بالإرضاع فالأم أولى لأنهم جعلوا الأم أحق في سائر الأحوال إلا في حالة طلب الزيادة على أجرة الأجنبية. والمصرح به بخلافه كما في التبيين وغيره أن الأجنبية أولى لكن هي أولى في الإرضاع، أما في الحضانة ففي الولوالجية وغيرها رجل طلق امرأته وبينهما وللصبي عمة أرادت أن تربيه وتمسكه من غير أجر من غير أن تمنع الأم عنه والأم تأبى ذلك وتطالب الأب بالأجر ونفقة الولد فالأم أحق كما يقال لو تبرعت العمة، وظاهر المتون أن الأم تأخذه بأجر المثل ولا تكون الأجنبية أولى بخلاف العمة على الصحيح إلا أن نقل صريح في أن الأجنبية كالعمة والظاهر أن العمة ليست قيداً بل كل حاضنة كذلك بل الخالة كذلك بالأولى لأنها من قرابة الأم. قوله : (والمصرح به بخلافه كما في التبيين وغيره) أي بخلاف ما هو ظاهر المتون. قال في التبيين : وإن رضيت الأجنبية أن ترضعه بغير أجر أو بدون أجر المثل والأم بأجر المثل فالأجنبية أولى وقال في البدائع : وأما إذا انقضت عدتها فالتمست أجرة الرضاع وقال الأب أجد من ترضع من غير أجر أو بأقل من ذلك فذلك له لقوله تعالى وإن تعاسرتم فسترضع له أخرى) [الطلاق: ٦] ولأن في الزام الأب ما تلتمسه ضرراً بالأب وقد قال الله تعالى ولا مولود له بولده﴾ [البقرة: ٢٣٣] أي لا يضار الأب بإلزام الزيادة على ما تلتسمه الأجنبية ؛ كذا ذكر في بعض التأويلات. ولكن توضع عند الأم ولا يفرق بينهما لما فيه من إلحاق الضرر بالأم ا هـ قوله : (وتطالب الأب بالأجر ونفقة الولد أراد بالأجرة أجرة الرضاع سواء أرضعته بنفسها أو أرضعته غيرها. وأراد بالنفقة ما يكون بعد الفطام والظاهر أن وضع المسألة في مطلقة مضت عدتها فإن طلب الأجرة من الأب من جهة أم الصبي إنما هو في هذه الصورة كما سبق آنفاً وإنما قلنا أراد بالأجرة أجرة الرضاع إذ لا يجب على الأب أجرة على الحضانة زائدة على هذه الأجرة حتى تطالبه المرأة به كما صرح به في جواهر الفتاوى نقلاً عن قاضيخان، وتحقيقه أن أجرة الرضاع بمنزلة الرضاع والرضاع من النفقة كما صرحوا به والنفقة إنما تجب على الأب بخلاف الحضانة فإنها ليست عليه على ما قرره بعض العلماء ؛ كذا في زاده على الدرر والغرر والظاهر أن المراد أجرة الحضانة كما فهمه المؤلف بدليل قوله وإما أن تدفعيه إلى العمة إذ لو كان المراد أجرة الرضاع لم تؤمر بالدفع إلى العمة حاشية عزمي
Book of Divorce, Chapter of Maintenance. A child [and] a woman offering to breastfeed for free: the mother is more entitled because they made the mother more entitled in all circumstances except in the case of demanding an increase over the wage of a foreign woman. And what is explicitly stated is contrary to this, as in al-Tabyeen and others: the foreign woman is more entitled, but she is more entitled in breastfeeding. As for custody, in al-Walwalijiyya and others: A man divorced his wife and between them there is a child, and the child has a paternal aunt who wants to raise him and keep him without wage without preventing the mother from him, and the mother refuses that and demands from the father the wage and maintenance of the child: the mother is more entitled to the child. And the mother's right is only invalidated if the mother imposes a wage for breastfeeding more than her like. And the correct view is that the mother is told: either keep the child without wage or give him to the paternal aunt. End. And I have not seen anyone explicitly state that a foreign woman is like a paternal aunt in that the child is given to her if she offers for free while the mother wants the wage for custody, and she is not measured against the paternal aunt because she is a custodian in general. And the question about this issue has become frequent in our time: the father brings a foreign woman offering custody for free; is the mother told as she would be told if the paternal aunt offered? And the apparent meaning of the texts is that the mother takes him for the like wage and the foreign woman is not more entitled, contrary to the paternal aunt according to the correct view, except that there is an explicit narration that the foreign woman is like the paternal aunt, and the apparent meaning is that the paternal aunt is not a restriction, rather every custodian is like that, even the maternal aunt a fortiori because she is from the mother's relatives. His statement: (And what is explicitly stated is contrary to it as in al-Tabyeen and others) i.e., contrary to the apparent meaning of the texts. He said in al-Tabyeen: If a foreign woman agrees to breastfeed him without wage or less than the like wage, and the mother asks for the like wage, then the foreign woman is more entitled. And he said in al-Bada'i: And if her waiting period has ended and she demands the wage for breastfeeding, and the father says 'I find someone to breastfeed without wage or for less,' then that is permissible for him because of the Almighty's statement: 'And if you disagree, then another woman will breastfeed for him' [al-Talaq: 6], and because imposing on the father what she demands harms the father, and Allah Almighty said: 'And no parent shall be made to suffer for their child' [al-Baqarah: 233], i.e., the father should not be harmed by imposing an increase over what the foreign woman demands; thus mentioned in some interpretations. But the child is placed with the mother and no distinction is made between them because of the harm to the mother. End. His statement: (And she demands from the father the wage and maintenance of the child) He meant by wage the wage for breastfeeding, whether she breastfeeds him herself or someone else breastfeeds him. And he meant by maintenance what is after weaning. And the apparent meaning is that the scenario is about a divorced woman whose waiting period has passed, because her demand for wage from the father from the side of the child's mother is only in this situation as previously. And we only said he meant by wage the wage for breastfeeding because the father is not obligated for a wage for custody in addition to this wage so that the woman may demand it from him, as stated in Jawaher al-Fatawa transmitted from Qadikhan. And its verification is that the wage for breastfeeding is in the position of breastfeeding, and breastfeeding is from maintenance as they stated, and maintenance is only obligatory on the father, unlike custody, for it is not upon him according to what some scholars established. Thus in Zadeh on al-Durar wa al-Ghurar. And the apparent meaning is that what is meant is the wage for custody, as the author understood by the evidence of his statement 'or give him to the paternal aunt'; because if what was meant was the wage for breastfeeding, she would not be ordered to give him to the paternal aunt. Hashiyat 'Azmi.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on who has priority for custody when the mother demands a fee and a relative (paternal aunt) or a stranger offers to do it for free. The matn states that the mother is more entitled in all circumstances except when she demands more than the stranger's fee; then the stranger is given priority for breastfeeding, but custody remains with the mother. The commentary cites conflicting rulings: al-Tabyeen gives the foreign woman priority even if the mother demands the like wage, while al-Bada'i holds that the father can give the child to a stranger offering free breastfeeding. The correct view (as per al-Walwalijiyya) is that the mother is more entitled unless she demands an excessive fee; if she demands the like wage, she keeps the child. The passage then addresses the question of whether a foreign woman is like a paternal aunt; the author concludes that a paternal aunt has a special status as a relative, so she takes priority over a stranger, but a maternal aunt is even more entitled. The commentary also clarifies that the wage in question is for breastfeeding, not custody, because custody is not a paid service for the father. However, some later authorities interpret the wage as for custody, arguing that otherwise the mother would not be told to give the child to the aunt.

Key Terms
أجرة الرضاع (ujrat al-rida'): Wage for breastfeeding; an obligation on the father owed to the mother or any wet nurse.
أجرة الحضانة (ujrat al-hadana): Wage for custody; disputed whether father owes it. The text says some scholars hold it is not obligatory on father.
مثلها (mithluha): The like wage; a fair market rate for a service (breastfeeding or custody) based on what similar women would charge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the correct view in this passage, when can a paternal aunt take custody of a child over the mother?
A) Always, because she is a relative.
B) Only when the mother demands a wage higher than the like wage.
C) Only when the mother is deceased.
D) Never, because the mother is always more entitled.

Key Takeaway
The mother's right to custody is only lost if she demands more than the fair wage; a paternal aunt has special priority over a foreign woman.

Breastfeeding Fee Duration for the Divorced Woman: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Exposition of breastfeeding fee duration with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the maximum duration for which a divorced woman (mubannah) can claim breastfeeding fees, and explain the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The breastfeeding fee for a divorced woman is limited to two years by consensus, despite Abu Hanifa's view of two and a half.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq elucidates the duration for which a divorced woman can claim compensation for breastfeeding her child. It resolves an intra-Hanafi dispute by relying on the consensus of later scholars, establishing two years as the operative limit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is breastfeeding by a divorced mother; the father is obligated to pay a fee (ujrah) for it. Determine the hukm level: wajib, as it is a financial obligation.
The fee is distinct from maintenance (nafaqa) and does not lapse upon death.
2
Locate the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Abu Hanifa holds that the divorced woman can claim the fee up to two and a half years. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) restrict it to two years. Identify the precise point of disagreement: the duration, not the obligation itself.
Khalaf ibn Ayyub dissents on permissibility of breastfeeding beyond two years.
3
Trace the Tarjih (Preference)
The majority of later scholars (mutakhkhirin) adopt the two-year limit, citing consensus (ijma') during the two years and beyond it. This becomes the mufta bihi (operative opinion).
The passage states 'most scholars' and 'by consensus' for the two-year period.
4
Note the Thamarah al-Khilaf (Practical Consequences)
If a divorced woman breastfeeds beyond two years, according to Abu Hanifa she can claim the fee for the extra period; according to the mufta bihi, she cannot. The practical difference affects the father's liability.
5
Apply the Mufta Bihi in Fatwa
In contemporary Hanafi fatwa, the two-year limit is relied upon. A divorced woman can only claim breastfeeding fees for the first two years of the child's life, regardless of the opinion of Abu Hanifa.
This is the position of the majority and the Sahibayn, supported by later authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حول ونصف حل بالإجماع ولا تأثم، ولو لم يستغن بحولين حل لها أن ترضعه بعدهما عند عامة المشايخ إلا عند خلف بن أيوب وأما الكلام في استحقاق الأجرة فمنهم من قال إنه على الخلاف حتى إن المبانة تستحق إلى الحولين ونصف عنده وعندهما إلى حولين فقط، وأكثر المشايخ على أن مدة الرضاع في حق الأجرة حولان عند الكل حتى لا تستحق بعد الحولين إجماعاً وتستحق في الحولين إجماعاً. وظاهر كلامهم أن وجوب أجرة الرضاع لا تتوقف على عقد إجارة مع الأم بل تستحقه بالإرضاع مطلقاً في المدة المذكورة، وقد قدمنا أنه ليس بفقه . وفي الظهيرية : وإذا أقرت المعتدة أنها قبضت نفقة أولادها الصغار لخمسة أشهر ثم قالت إنها قبضت عشرين درهماً ونفقة خمسة أشهر مائة درهم لم تصدق على ذلك وإن قالت ضاعت النفقة فإنها ترجع على أبيهم بنفقتهم دون حصتها اهـ . قوله : (وقد قدمنا أنه ليس بفقه الظاهر أن النسخة ليس بنفقة لأنه الذي قدمه عن الذخيرة في هذه القولة حيث قال : لا تسقط بموت الزوج لأنها أجرة وليست بنفقة
A year and a half is permissible by consensus and she does not sin. If the child does not become self-sufficient in two years, it is permissible for her to breastfeed him after that according to the general body of scholars except Khalaf ibn Ayyub. As for the discussion of entitlement to the fee, some said it is based on the disagreement, such that a divorced woman is entitled up to two and a half years according to him, and according to them up to only two years. Most scholars say that the duration of breastfeeding regarding the fee is two years according to everyone, so that nothing is entitled after two years by consensus, and it is entitled during the two years by consensus. The apparent meaning of their words is that the obligation of the breastfeeding fee does not depend on a contract of hire with the mother, rather she is entitled to it by breastfeeding absolutely within the mentioned period, and we have previously stated that this is not a fiqh. In al-Zahiriyyah: If a woman in her waiting period (iddah) acknowledges that she received maintenance for her young children for five months, then says she received twenty dirhams while the maintenance for five months is one hundred dirhams, she is not believed in that. If she says the maintenance was lost, then she may claim from their father for their maintenance without her share. His statement: 'And we have previously stated that it is not a fiqh' — the apparent reading is that the manuscript has 'not a maintenance (nafaqa)' because that is what he previously transmitted from al-Dhakhirah in this statement where he said: 'It does not lapse upon the death of the husband because it is a fee and not maintenance.'
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the duration of breastfeeding and the entitlement to payment for it, particularly for a divorced woman (mubannah). It begins by stating that breastfeeding for a year and a half (around eighteen months) is permissible by consensus, and the mother is not sinful for breastfeeding beyond two years if the child needs it, though the majority of scholars (excluding Khalaf ibn Ayyub) permit it. The main issue is the period for which a divorced woman can claim a fee for breastfeeding. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that the divorced woman is entitled to the fee up to two and a half years, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) restrict it to two years. The majority of later scholars resolve this by stating that the period for the fee is two years for all women, based on consensus. The text also notes that the obligation to pay the breastfeeding fee does not require a formal contract (ijarah); it is owed simply by the act of breastfeeding. However, the author remarks that this is not a matter of fiqh (jurisprudence) but rather a financial entitlement (ujrah), meaning it is not like maintenance (nafaqa) that lapses on death. Then, a ruling from al-Zahiriyyah is cited: if a woman in iddah acknowledges receiving maintenance for her children, then later claims she received less, she is not believed; but if she claims the money was lost, she can reclaim it from the father. This is a separate evidentiary rule about claims of maintenance receipt.

Key Terms
مبانة (mubannah): A woman who has been irrevocably divorced (ba'in talaq) and is therefore in her iddah period.
أجرة الرضاع (ujrat al-rada'): The compensation/fee owed to the mother for breastfeeding the child, distinct from maintenance (nafaqa).
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The transmitted position from the six core books of Imam Muhammad; here, the two-year limit for breastfeeding fee is the relied-upon position.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of later Hanafi scholars (mutakhkhirin), what is the maximum duration for which a divorced woman (mubannah) can claim the breastfeeding fee?
A) One and a half years
B) Two years
C) Two and a half years
D) Until the child is weaned

Key Takeaway
The operative Hanafi position is that a divorced woman can claim the breastfeeding fee for a maximum of two years, based on the majority and consensus.

Exclusive Maintenance Obligation: Father and Child
Expansion of the exclusivity rule and its exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule of exclusive maintenance obligation between father and child, and apply the exceptions when the father is poor or absent, including the grandfather's liability.

Core Idea
No one shares the father's or child's maintenance duty – only poverty shifts it to the grandfather.

Maintenance is a unique obligation: the father must support his children, and the child must support his parents. No other relative shares this burden unless the father is destitute or absent. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the rule, its scope, and the critical intra-Hanafi dispute over the grandfather's role when the father cannot provide.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Find the statement that no one shares with the father or son in maintenance. Understand that it covers both minors and disabled adults.
The author includes grandfather under 'father' and grandson under 'son'.
2
Analyze the scenario when the father has means but refuses
The judge orders the mother to borrow and spend on the child, allowing her to reclaim from the father later.
This is a temporary measure; the father remains ultimately liable.
3
Examine the poor father scenario
When the father is poor, the correct madhhab treats him as dead, making the grandfather directly obligated to maintain the grandchildren without reclaim.
This is the mufta bihi, supported by al-Dhakhira and al-Sadr al-Shahid.
4
Contrast the opposing view (al-Quduri / al-Hasan ibn Salih)
They hold that the mother should borrow and the grandfather is not obligated. The tarjih favors the grandfather's immediate duty.
The thamarah al-khilaf: who bears the burden in practice.
5
Apply the ruling to a modern scenario
A father with chronic illness (zaman) is treated like one who cannot earn; the grandfather must support the grandchildren and cannot reclaim.
This protects the children from destitution.

Source Text

التتارخانية. والمسألة في كثير من الكتب كالبزازية وغيرها. حتى قوله : (وقد ذكرنا أول هذا الفصل قال الرملي : هو من كلام صاحب الذخيرة. وقوله «إن الأب الخ لا خفاء أن الأم المعسرة كذلك واعلم أنه إنما يلحق بالميت عند القائل به في حق الجد لا يرجع، وأما في حق الزوجة فلا، وبه يفهم كلامهم في هذا المحل فتأمل . ا هـ يعني أنه في حق الزوجة لا يلحق الأب المعسر بالميت إذا لو ألحق بالميت في حقها لزم أن لا ترجع He made it general for the child, so it includes the minor and those whose maintenance is wajib due to these descriptions, so ponder. His statement: '(And no one) shares with the father and the son in the maintenance of his child and his parents.' Al-Ramli said: He made it general, so it includes the adult child, and this is the answer in al-Mabsut, and it is apparent, as he will mention at the end of the statement. As for what al-Khassaf mentioned, it is wajib on the father and mother for adults in thirds! End. I say: The author means by 'father' what includes the grandfather, and by 'son' what includes the son's son. So in al-Bada'i': No one shares with the son in the maintenance of his parents, and likewise in the maintenance of his grandfather and grandmother when the parents are absent, and no one shares with the father in the maintenance of his child. Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, vol. 4, p. 23. [Page 354] Book of Divorce, Chapter of Maintenance: The child. And if the father has the means but refuses maintenance for the child, so the judge imposes maintenance on the father, then he refuses to pay, the judge orders her (the mother) to borrow on his behalf and spend on the child, so that she may reclaim from the father. Similarly, if the father is absent after the imposition of maintenance for the children, leaving them without maintenance, and she borrows with the judge's order and spends on them, she reclaims from him. And this ruling applies to the cost of breastfeeding if the father is poor; the judge orders the mother to borrow. When he becomes wealthy, she reclaims from him the amount the judge ordered her to borrow. But if she did not borrow after the imposition, and they were eating from begging, there is no reclaim because of sufficiency. If they were given half of sufficiency, half of the maintenance is dropped from the father for the remaining half, and analogically. And similarly for the maintenance of maharim, and its completion will come. And if a poor person has young children and a wealthy grandfather, maintenance is not imposed on the grandfather, but the grandfather is ordered to spend to preserve the son's son, and it becomes a debt on the father of the children. This is what al-Quduri mentioned, so he did not place maintenance on the grandfather in the case of the father's poverty. And we mentioned at the beginning of this chapter that the poor father is attached to the deceased in deserving maintenance from the grandfather, and this is the correct view of the madhhab. What al-Quduri mentioned is the saying of al-Hasan ibn Salih; thus mentioned al-Sadr al-Shahid in Adab al-Qadi to al-Khassaf. And if the father is chronically disabled (zaman), he judges maintenance of the children on the grandfather, and he does not reclaim from anyone for the spending, because the father's maintenance in this case is on the grandfather. Similarly, no one shares with the grandfather in the maintenance of his son's son in the absence of his guardian, because he stands in his place in his absence. End. His statement: 'Then he made the mother more deserving of bearing than other relatives...' Al-Ramli said: It will come that the poor father is like the deceased, and that if the child has no father, and has a mother and a paternal grandfather, the maintenance is on both. The summary: When the father is poor, there is a dispute: the texts say it is on the father and the mother borrows; according to what the author of al-Dhakhira corrected, it is on the grandfather. And whether the borrowing is on the father and reclaiming, there is also a dispute. As for the mother, she borrows and reclaims, so ponder. And in al-Sughra: A woman has a minor son with no property and no property for her, she borrowed and spent on the child with the judge's order, then he grew up; she does not reclaim from him; thus in al-Tatar Khaniyya. And the issue is in many books like al-Bazzaziyya and others. Until his statement: 'We mentioned at the beginning of this chapter...' Al-Ramli said: This is from the speech of the author of al-Dhakhira. And his statement: 'Indeed the father...' There is no doubt that the poor mother is similar. And know that he is attached to the deceased according to the one who holds it, regarding the grandfather, he does not reclaim. But regarding the wife, no. And by this, their speech in this place is understood, so ponder. End. It means that regarding the wife, the poor father is not attached to the deceased, because if he were attached to the deceased in her right, it would entail that she does not reclaim, because it is wajib on her and on the grandfather in thirds according to inheritance, originally not deputizing for the father. His statement: (A) (H) i.e., the speech of al-Dhakhira. His statement: 'And the obligation on others...' The meaning of 'others' is the grandfather when the children have no mother, and the grandfather or others if the father is zaman i.e., poor, so someone other than the father has shared in spending on his child. This contradicts the absolute statement of the texts. And al-Maqdisi answered in his commentary that the speech of the texts is restricted to wealth, because the principle regarding the one obligated for maintenance is that he be wealthy, so ponder.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling that no one shares with the father or son in the obligation of maintenance. It explains that the rule covers both minors and adults (the father must maintain the adult child if the child is unable to earn). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: al-Khassaf holds that for adults, maintenance is wajib on both parents in thirds, but the relied-upon view is that the father alone is responsible. The commentary then details situations when the father is poor or absent: the mother can borrow with the judge's permission and reclaim from the father later. If the father is poor, the correct madhhab is that he is treated like dead, so the grandfather must maintain the grandchildren and cannot reclaim. This is supported by al-Dhakhira and al-Sadr al-Shahid. The passage also discusses the mother's priority over other relatives in bearing temporary maintenance, and the ruling that if the mother borrows and spends, she reclaims from the father (with some exceptions like the child growing up).

Key Terms
لا يشارك (la yusharik): No one shares; the obligation is exclusive to the father or son.
الاستدانة (al-istidanah): Borrowing, permitted with the judge's order, to be reclaimed from the obligated person later.
الزم (al-zaman): Chronic illness or disability preventing earning; such a person is treated as incapable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the correct madhhab position regarding the grandfather's obligation when the father is poor?
A) The grandfather is not obligated
B) The grandfather is obligated and can reclaim from the father
C) The grandfather is obligated and cannot reclaim, as the poor father is like dead
D) The mother is always obligated first

Key Takeaway
The father (or child) is exclusively liable for maintenance; only poverty equivalent to death shifts the burden to the grandfather without reclaim.

Effect of Intoxication on Manumission
Clarifies when intoxication invalidates manumission and legal acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between permissible and impermissible causes of intoxication in Hanafi fiqh and state the ruling on the validity of legal acts (such as manumission and divorce) performed in each state.

Core Idea
Intoxication that results from permissible causes is treated like unconsciousness — all legal acts are invalid.

Intoxication (sukr) can arise from various substances and situations. In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of legal acts performed while intoxicated hinges on the cause of that intoxication. This lesson examines the passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq that classifies intoxicants into two categories: those that invalidate acts due to being impermissible or intentionally consumed for intoxication, and those where the intoxication is incidental and results from a permissible means, rendering the person like unconsciousness (ighma').

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage addresses manumission, divorce, and any legal transaction (tasarruf). The ruling is that these acts are invalid (batil) when performed in a state of intoxication from permissible causes.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is analogical reasoning (qiyas): permissible intoxication is likened to unconsciousness (ighma'), where legal acts are universally invalid due to loss of intellect.
The asl is unconsciousness; the far' is permissible intoxication.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The common factor (illa) is the loss of intellect and intention. In both states, the person lacks the capacity to form valid intention required for legal acts.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars may differentiate based on degree of intoxication, but Hanafis treat all cases of complete loss of intellect equally.
The passage does not elaborate on opposing views.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that acts performed in this state are invalid. This is based on the authoritative text al-Tahrir and consistent with rulings in divorce.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب العتق مثلث بقصد السكر، وأما ما كان طريقه مباحاً كسكر المضطر إلى شرب الخمر والحاصل من الأدوية والأغذية المتخذة من غير العنب والمثلث لا بقصد السكر بل بقصد الاستمراء والتقوى ونقيع الزبيب بلا طبخ فإنه كالإغماء لا يصح معه تصرف ولا طلاق ولا عتاق؛ كذا التحرير، وقدمناه في الطلاق.
Book of Manumission. The muthallath (concentrated grape juice) intended for intoxication, and as for that whose method is permissible like the intoxication of one compelled to drink wine, and that resulting from medicines and foods made from non-grapes, and the muthallath not intended for intoxication but for nutrition and strength, and raisin infusion without cooking, then it is like unconsciousness: no legal act is valid with it, nor divorce, nor manumission. Thus in al-Tahrir, and we have presented it in the Book of Divorce.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the ruling on intoxication in relation to manumission. It begins by distinguishing between types of intoxication. The author states that if a person becomes intoxicated by a substance that is inherently impure (like wine) or by a substance that is permissible but consumed with the intent of intoxication (like muthallath), then that intoxication invalidates legal acts. However, if the intoxication results from a permissible cause—such as a person forced to drink wine to save his life, or from medicines or foods not made from grapes, or from muthallath taken for nutrition rather than intoxication, or from raisin infusion that has not been cooked—then such intoxication is treated like unconsciousness (ighma'). In that state, no legal transaction (tasarruf), divorce (talaq), or manumission ('itaq) is valid. The author references al-Tahrir and notes that this ruling was already presented in the chapter on divorce. The key legal principle here is that acts performed in a state of complete loss of intellect are invalid, whether due to unconsciousness or permissible intoxication, because the agent lacks the requisite intention and comprehension.

Key Terms
سكر (sukr): Intoxication caused by any substance that overcomes the intellect.
إغماء (ighma'): Unconsciousness; a state where a person has no awareness or control.
مثلث (muthallath): A concentrated grape juice boiled down to one-third; can be intoxicating if intended for that purpose.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on manumission pronounced by a person who becomes intoxicated from raisin infusion (naqi' al-zabib) taken for nutrition without cooking?
A) The manumission is valid because the raisin infusion is permissible.
B) The manumission is invalid because the person is in a state like unconsciousness.
C) The manumission is valid if the person had intention to free the slave before intoxication.
D) The manumission is suspended until he regains sobriety.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, intoxication from a permissible cause (like medication or forced consumption) invalidates legal acts because it is analogous to unconsciousness, regardless of the permissibility of the cause.
