Manumission of a Pregnant Slave: Mother and Fetus
Rulings on freeing a pregnant slave and fetus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on manumission of a pregnant slave, distinguish between Abu Yusuf's exception and the majority view, and apply the rules of tab'iyyah to determine the child's freedom and wala'.

Core Idea
Freeing a pregnant slave frees the child via tab'iyyah, but timing affects wala' and independent manumission.

This lesson delves into a nuanced area of Hanafi fiqh: the manumission of a pregnant slave. The core principle is that freeing the mother also frees her fetus by attachment (tab'iyyah). However, Imam Abu Yusuf introduces an exception when most of the child has emerged, and the timing of birth determines whether the child is freed primarily or by following, impacting the wala' (patronage) rights. We will explore these details using the commentary of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Main Ruling
First, state the general rule: if a master frees a pregnant slave, both mother and child become free. The child follows the mother (tab'iyyah) because it is attached to her like a part.
This is the default position of the Hanafi school.
2
Note Abu Yusuf's Exception
Abu Yusuf holds that if most of the child has emerged at the time of freeing, the child is not freed because it is considered separate in legal rulings (e.g., 'idda ends, inheritance applies). Recognize that this is an intra-Hanafi difference.
The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) do not make this distinction.
3
Analyze the Timing Distinction
Determine how the timing of birth after manumission affects the ruling. If the child is born less than six months after freeing, it is freed independently (asalah). If born six months or more, it is freed by following (tab'iyyah).
This distinction affects wala' and whether the child was considered to exist at the time of freeing.
4
Apply the Wala' Rule
Understand the consequence for wala'. If the child is freed by tab'iyyah, his wala' goes to the father's master (if the father was a slave). If freed independently, wala' goes to the mother's patron.
The father's ownership at conception is key.
5
Consider Freeing the Fetus Only
Examine the ruling when the master frees only the fetus without the mother. This is valid, but the mother remains a slave. However, selling or gifting the fetus is invalid because delivery is impossible.
This contrasts with freeing the mother, which automatically frees the fetus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو حرر حاملاً عتقاً) أي الأم والحمل تبعاً لها إذ هو متصل بها فهو كسائر أجزائها ولو استثناه لا يصح كاستثناء جزء منها. وقال أبو يوسف : إذا خرج أكثر الولد فأعتق الأم لا يعتق الولد لأنه كالمنفصل في حق الأحكام ألا ترى أنه تنقضي به العدة ولو مات في هذه الحالة يرث بخلاف ما إذا مات قبل خروج الأكثر ; هكذا ذكره الشارحون وظاهره أن نسبة هذا التفصيل لأبي يوسف لكونه نقل عنه وحده لا لأن الصاحبين يخالفانه فإنه موافق للقاعدة. وفي الخانية: رجل أعتق جارية إنسان الملك الثابت هنا إنما هو في ضمن ثبوت العتق المحكوم بثبوته شرعاً لضرورة دفع الذل عن القريب قرابة قوية ويغتفر في الضمنيات ما لا يغتفر في القصديات بخلاف قوله كل مملوك لي حر فإنه قصدي. حاملاً عتقا وإن حرره عتق فقط والولد يتبع أمه في الملك والحرية والرق والتدبير والأستيلاد والكتابة وولد الأمة من سيدها حر. فأجاز المولى إعتاقه بعد ما ولدت يعتق الولد .اهـ. وأطلق المصنف في عتق الحمل فشمل ما إذا ولدته بعد عتقها لستة أشهر أو أقل أو أكثر لكن إن ولدته لأقل من ستة أشهر بعد عتقها فإنه يعتق مقصوداً لا بطريق التبعية حتى لا ينجر ولاؤه إلى مولى الأب وإن ولدته لستة أشهر فأكثر فإنه يعتق بطريق التبعية فحينئذ ينجر الولاء إلى مولى الأب كما في شرح الوقاية . وعلى هذا فينبغي أن يحمل قوله هنا على ما إذا ولدته لأقل من ستة أشهر ليكون عتقه بطريق الأصالة لئلا يلزم التكرار ولأنه سيذكر أن الولد يتبع الأم في الحرية والتبعية إنما تكون إذا ولدته لستة أشهر فأكثر فيحمل عليه اللهم إلا أن يريد بالحرية الحرية الأصلية فلا إشكال ولا تکرار . قوله : (وإن حرره عتق فقط) أي إن حرر الحمل وحده عتق هو دون أمه لأنه لا وجه إلى إعتاقها مقصود العدم الإضافة إليها ولا إليه تبعاً لما فيه من قلب الموضوع. ثم إعتاق الحمل صحيح ولا يصح بيعه ولا هبته لأن التسليم نفسه شرط في الهبة والقدرة عليه في البيع ولم يوجد بالإضافة إلى الجنين وشيء من ذلك ليس شرطاً في الإعتاق فافترقا . وأفاد بقوله «حرره» أنه كان موجوداً وقت التحرير ولن يتحقق وجوده إلا إذا ولدته لأقل من ستة أشهر، وإن ولدته لستة أشهر فأكثر فإنه لا يعتق ولا يكون قوله ما في بطنك حر إقراراً بوجوده لعدم التيقن بوجوده وقته لجواز حدوثه إلا في مسألتين: أحدهما ما إذا كانت الأمة معتدة عن طلاق أو وفاة فتلده لأقل من سنتين من وقت الفراق، وإن كان لأكثر من ستة أشهر من وقت الإعتاق فحينئذ يعتق لأنه كان موجوداً حين أعتقه بدليل ثبوت نسبه . ثانيهما إذا كان حملها توأمين فجاءت بأولهما لأقل من ستة أشهر ثم جاءت بالثاني لستة أشهر أو أكثر فإنه يعتق لأنه كان محكوماً بوجوده حين أعتقه حتى ثبت نسبه. وتفرع على التفصيل السابق مسألتان : إحداهما لو قال المولى ما في بطنك حر ثم قال إن حملت فسالم حر فولدت بعده لستة أشهر فالقول له إن أقر أنها كانت حاملاً يومئذ عتق الولد وإن أقر أنه حمل مستقبل عتق لأنا تيقنا بعتق أحدهما وشككنا في الآخر لأنه لا يخلوا إما أن يكون العلوق والحمل كان موجوداً وقت الإعتاق أو كان حادثاً بعده فرجع في البيان إليه. وإن جاءت به لأكثر من سنتين يعتق سالم دون الولد لأنا تيقنا أنه لم يكن موجوداً وقت الإعتاق، وإن جاءت لأقل مطلق فيقتضي صفة الكمال فاحتاج إلى الملك المطلق ولم يكن فيه مطلق الملك، ألا ترى أنه لا يدخل فيه البعض المملوك ويدخل في ملك القريب فيعتق والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم. قوله: (وينبغي أن يقال إن ولدته الخ لأنه قد يكون الضرب بعد العتق لأقل من ستة أشهر سالم به
His statement: (And if he frees a pregnant one, she is free) i.e., the mother and the fetus as a follower of her, because it is attached to her, so it is like the rest of her parts. And if he excludes it, it is not valid, like excluding a part of her. Abu Yusuf said: If most of the child has emerged and he frees the mother, the child is not freed because it is like separated in rulings. Do you not see that the 'idda ends with it, and if it dies in this state it inherits, unlike if it died before the emergence of most. Thus the explainers mentioned, and it appears that this detail is attributed solely to Abu Yusuf, not because the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) oppose it, but it agrees with the principle. In al-Khaniyya: A man freed a slave girl of someone else; the ownership established here is only within the establishment of the manumission ruled to be established legally due to the necessity of removing humiliation from a strong relative, and in implicit matters what is not forgiven in explicit matters is forgiven, unlike his statement 'Every slave of mine is free' which is explicit. (A pregnant one is free), and if he frees only it, it is free, and the child follows its mother in ownership, freedom, slavery, tadbir, istilad, and kitaba. And the child of an owned slave girl from her master is free. So if the master permitted his manumission after she gave birth, the child is freed. End. The author (al-Kanz) was absolute in the manumission of the fetus, so it includes whether she gives birth after her manumission within six months, or less, or more. But if she gives birth in less than six months after her manumission, then it is freed intentionally (maqsudan) not by way of following, so his wala' does not transfer to the father's master. And if she gives birth after six months or more, then it is freed by way of following, so then the wala' transfers to the father's master, as in Sharh al-Wiqaya. Upon this, his statement here should be interpreted as when she gives birth in less than six months, so that his manumission is by way of originality to avoid repetition, and because he will mention that the child follows the mother in freedom, and following only occurs when she gives birth after six months or more, so it should be interpreted accordingly, unless he means freedom in the original sense, then there is no problem or repetition. His statement: (And if he frees only it, it is free) i.e., if he frees the fetus alone, it is free without its mother, because there is no way to free her intentionally with no addition to her, nor to him by following because that would invert the subject. Then freeing the fetus is valid, and selling it or gifting it is not valid because delivery itself is a condition in gift and ability to deliver is a condition in sale, and that does not exist with respect to the fetus, and none of that is a condition in freeing, so they differ. And his word 'frees it' indicates that it existed at the time of freeing, and its existence is only verified if she gives birth in less than six months. If she gives birth after six months or more, then it is not freed, and his statement 'What is in your belly is free' is not an acknowledgment of its existence due to lack of certainty of its existence at that time because it could have occurred later, except in two cases: First, if the slave girl is in 'idda from divorce or death and she gives birth within less than two years from the separation, even if more than six months from the time of freeing, then it is freed because it existed when he freed it, proven by the establishment of lineage. Second, if her pregnancy is of twins and she delivers the first in less than six months and the second in six months or more, then it is freed because it was ruled to have existed when he freed it, so its lineage is established. Two issues branch from the previous detail: One of them: If the master said, 'What is in your belly is free,' then said, 'If you become pregnant, Salim is free,' and she gave birth after six months, then the word is his: if he acknowledges that she was pregnant at that time, the child is freed; if he acknowledges that it is a later pregnancy, Salim is freed, because we are certain that one of them is freed and we are uncertain about the other, since it is either that conception and pregnancy existed at the time of freeing or occurred afterwards, so the explanation is referred to him. If she gives birth after more than two years, Salim is freed and not the child, because we are certain that it did not exist at the time of freeing. And if she gives birth in absolutely less (than six months?), then it requires the attribute of perfection, so it needed absolute ownership, and it did not have absolute ownership. Do you not see that it does not include a partially owned part, and it enters into the ownership of a relative, so it becomes free. And Allah, the Exalted, knows best. His statement: (It should be said that if she gives birth to him... because it might be that the conception after freeing is less than six months) Salim by it.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This lesson from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq covers the rulings on manumission of a pregnant slave. The matn states: 'If he frees a pregnant one, she is free' meaning both mother and child are freed because the fetus is attached to her like a part of her body. However, Abu Yusuf makes a distinction: if most of the child has emerged at the time of freeing the mother, the child is not freed because it is now considered separate for legal purposes (e.g., 'idda ends, inheritance applies). The majority view (Imam Muhammad and Abu Hanifa) seems to agree with the principle that the child follows the mother, but the detail is attributed to Abu Yusuf. Next, the matn says: 'And if he frees only it (the fetus), it is free, and the child follows its mother in ownership, freedom, slavery, tadbir, istilad, and kitaba. And the child of a slave girl from her master is free.' The commentary then discusses when the child is freed as a primary intention or by way of following. If the woman gives birth within six months of manumission, the child is freed primarily (maqsudan) and his wala' goes to his father's master only if the father was a free man? Actually, the text says: 'then he is freed intentionally not by way of following, so his wala' does not transfer to the father's master.' If she gives birth after six months, he is freed by following and his wala' transfers to the father's master. The commentator reconciles the apparent contradiction by saying that the author's general statement refers to the case of less than six months to avoid redundancy. Then the commentary explains the second part of the matn: if the master frees only the fetus, it is valid and the mother remains a slave. However, selling or gifting the fetus is invalid because delivery and capacity are conditions for those transactions, but not for manumission. The existence of the fetus at the time of freeing is only certain if born within six months; otherwise, it is usually considered not existing, except in two cases: when the mother is in 'idda and gives birth within two years, or when there are twins and the first is born within six months. In these cases, lineage proves prior existence. Two further branches are given: if the master makes two conditional statements, one about the current pregnancy and one about future pregnancy, and the woman gives birth after six months, the determination of which child is freed depends on the master's acknowledgment of whether the pregnancy existed at that time. Finally, a note on a missing detail: the window ends with a cut-off comment.

Key Terms
تبعية (tab'iyyah): The child follows the mother in the ruling of manumission when born after the mother's manumission, typically if born after six months.
ولاء (wala'): The right of inheritance and loyalty that transfers to the freed slave's patron; if a child is freed by following the mother, the wala' goes to the father's patron if the child was conceived in the father's ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A master says to his pregnant slave, 'You are free,' and she gives birth to a child seven months later. According to the passage, how is the child freed?
A) The child is not freed because it was born after six months.
B) The child is freed by way of following (tab'iyyah) and his wala' goes to the father's master if the father is a slave.
C) The child is freed independently (asalah) and wala' goes to the mother's patron.
D) The child is freed only if the master explicitly includes it.

Key Takeaway
The manumission of a pregnant slave frees the child by way of following (tab'iyyah) unless the child is born less than six months after, in which case it is freed independently with different wala' consequences.

Talaq — Divorce
advanced
12 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Partial Tadbir and Itq of a Slave
Commentary on rulings when one part-owner does tadbir and another does itq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the divisibility of tadbir and apply the ruling for the silent partner and the mudabbar in a co-ownership scenario.

Core Idea
Tadbir is divisible per Imam Abu Hanifa; the silent partner can claim damages from the mudabbar, not the manumitter.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on a complex scenario in Kanz al-Daqa'iq: a slave owned by three persons, where one owner performs tadbir (suspensive emancipation upon death), another performs immediate manumission (itq), and the third remains silent. The commentary explains the options available to each partner, revealing a fundamental intra-Hanafi dispute on whether tadbir is divisible. Understanding this ikhtilaf is essential for correctly applying the rulings in co-ownership cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their actions
There are three co-owners: one does tadbir (mudabbar), one does itq (manumitter), and one does nothing (silent partner). Note that the slave is owned by financially capable (musir) partners.
The passage assumes the partners are musir (affluent) for certain options.
2
Analyze the silent partner's options
The silent partner can claim damages (daman) from the mudabbar (not from the manumitter) for his share. He can also seek istis'a' from the slave if the mudabbar is poor.
This is based on Imam Abu Hanifa's view that tadbir is divisible.
3
Analyze the mudabbar's options
The mudabbar can claim damages from the manumitter for one-third of the slave's value as mudabbar (i.e., the share affected by the manumitter's action). If the manumitter is poor, the mudabbar can seek istis'a' from the slave.
The mudabbar's claim is limited to the portion of his share that was spoiled.
4
Compare with Sahibayn's view
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold tadbir indivisible: the first mudabbar owns the entire slave and must compensate the partner with two-thirds of the slave's value, regardless of affluence.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is which partner has precedence and the calculation of compensation.

كتاب العتق باب العبد يعتق بعضه
عبد الموسرين دبره واحد وحرره آخر ضمن الساكت المدبر والمدبر المعتق ثلثه مدبر إلا ابنه لأنه لو اشترى نصف ابنه من أحد الشريكين وهو موسر فإنه يلزم المشتري الضمان بالإجماع للشريك الذي لم يبع، ولا يضمن للبائع شيئاً لأن الشريك الذي لم يبع لم يشاركه في العلة فلا يبطل حقه بفعل غيره، ولا يخفى أن في مسألة الكتاب إذا لم يضمن المشتري للبائع كان له الخيار إن شاء أعتق نصيبه وإن شاء استسعى وفي البدائع: رجل قال إن اشتريت فلاناً أو بعضه فهو حر فادعى رجل آخر أنه ابنه ثم اشترياه عتق عليهما ونصف، ولائه للذي أعتقه وهو ابن للذي ادعاه لأن النسب ههنا لم يسبق اليمين فيعتق نصيب كل واحد منهما عليه، وولاؤه بينهما لأنه عتق عليهما والولاء للمعتق .اهـ. مع أنهم قالوا : إن المعتق آخر العصبات فينبغي أن يكون ميراثه كله لأبيه مع وجوده ولا شيء للمعتق إلا أن يفرق بين ثبوت النسب قبل العتق وبينه بعده.
قوله : (عبد الموسرين دبره واحد وحرره آخر ضمن الساكت المدبر والمدبر المعتق ثلثه مدبر إلا ما ضمن) أي لو كان عبد بين ثلاثة دبره أحدهم ثم أعتقه آخر فللساكت وهو الذي لم يدبر ولم يحرر أن يضمن المدبر وليس له أن يضمن المعتق وللمدبر أن يضمن المعتق ثلث العبد مدبراً وليس له أن يضمنه الثلث الذي ضمنه للساكت وإنما يضمن الساكت المدبر ثلث قيمته قناً لأن التدبير يتجزئ عند الإمام لأنه شعبة من شعبه فيكون معتبراً به فاقتصر على نصيبه، وقد أفسد بالتدبير نصيب الآخرين فكان لكل واحد منهما أن يدبر نصيبه أو يعتق أو يكاتب أو يضمن المدبر أو يستسعي العبد أو يتركه على حاله، فلما حرره الآخر تعين حقه فيه وسقط اختياره غيره فتوجه للشريك الساكت سبباً ضمان تدبير المدبر وإعتاق المعتق فله تضمين المدبر ليكون الضمان ضمان معاوضة إذ هو الأصل حتى جعل الغصب ضمان معاوضة على أصلنا وأمكن ذلك في التدبير لكونه قابلاً للنقل من ملك إلى أول الباب إلى آخره .

Book of Emancipation, Chapter on the slave who is partially freed. A slave of two prosperous persons: one executed tadbir and another manumitted him, the silent partner holds the mudabbar liable, and the mudabbar holds the manumitter liable for one-third of him as mudabbar except his son... [continues]
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage is an expansion by al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It discusses the case where a slave is owned by three persons: one performs tadbir (suspensive emancipation upon death), another performs immediate manumission (itq), and the third remains silent. The silent partner has the option to claim damages from the mudabbar (the one who did tadbir) but not from the manumitter. The mudabbar can claim damages from the manumitter for one-third of the slave's value as a mudabbar, provided the manumitter is affluent. This is based on Imam Abu Hanifa's view that tadbir is divisible, as it is a branch of ownership, so each partner can dispose of his share. The manumitter's action spoils the mudabbar's interest. If the manumitter is not affluent, the mudabbar can seek earning (istis'a') from the slave. Abu Hanifa's students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that tadbir is indivisible, so the entire slave belongs to the first one who performed tadbir, and he must compensate his partner with two-thirds of the slave's value, regardless of the partner's affluence. The commentary then discusses valuation, the options of istis'a', and the wala' (patronage) distribution. The relied-upon position is that of Imam Abu Hanifa, with fatwa on the valuation method mentioned in al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
تدبير (tadbir): Suspensive emancipation of a slave upon the master's death.
ساكت (saakit): The partner who neither executed tadbir nor manumission.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who is subject to tadbir (suspensive emancipation). Also the owner who performed tadbir.
موسر (mawsir): Affluent, financially capable of paying compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when a slave is co-owned and one partner performs tadbir and another performs itq, what option does the silent partner have?
A) Claim damages from the manumitter
B) Claim damages from the partner who did tadbir
C) Seek istis'a' from the slave for full value
D) Automatically free the slave

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that tadbir is divisible (Imam Abu Hanifa), allowing co-owners to claim damages or istis'a' based on their shares; the contrary view of Sahibayn is recognized but not operative for fatwa.

Types of Ambiguity in Emancipation and the Analogy with Divorce
Analogy with divorce and introduction of ambiguity types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between original and incidental ambiguity in emancipation and explain the Hanafi mechanism of ta‘līq bi’l-bayān.

Core Idea
When a master's statement is originally ambiguous, emancipation is suspended on specification because the condition attaches to the ruling, not the cause.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā’iq first draws an analogy with divorce to demonstrate how fractions of mahr reduction apply when a husband dies without specifying which non-consummated wife was divorced. Then it introduces a crucial distinction in emancipatory statements: ambiguity can be original (present from the start) or incidental (arising later). For original ambiguity, the Hanafi school employs a special suspension called ta‘līq bi’l-bayān, where the condition is on the ruling (the transfer of ownership) not the cause (the act of emancipation). This nuance is vital for correctly applying the rules of 'itq.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the analogy with divorce
Review the fractions of mahr reduction when a husband says 'one of you is divorced' twice to three non-consummated wives and dies before specification. This parallels the emancipation case where fractions of damage are involved.
The fractions: external wife loses 1/4, fixed wife loses 3/8, internal wife loses 1/8 according to Muhammad; the two say 1/4 reduction.
2
Identify the two types of ambiguity
Original ambiguity (jahāla aṣliyya) means the wording from the start is ambiguous, e.g., 'one of you is free'. Incidental ambiguity (jahāla ṭāri‘a) arises after a clear statement. Focus on original ambiguity as the text develops.
The text only introduces the types; original ambiguity is the primary subject.
3
Analyze the mechanism of ta‘līq bi’l-bayān
In original ambiguity, the emancipation is suspended on specification. The condition (specification) attaches to the ruling (the transfer of ownership) not to the cause (the act of emancipation). This is a unique Hanafi concept, unlike ordinary ta‘līq where condition is on the cause.
Compare to tadbīr (suspension on death) and sale with option (khiyār al-sharṭ).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لو كان هذا في الطلاق فالحكم كذلك قال في الهداية : ولو كان هذا في الطلاق وهن غير مدخول بهن ومات الزوج قبل البيان سقط من مهر الخارجة ربعه، ومن مهر الثابتة ثلاثة أثمان ومن مهر الداخلة ثمنه . قيل : هذا قول محمد. وعندهما يسقط ربعه . وقيل : هو قولهما أيضاً. وقد ذكرنا الفرق وتمام تفريعها في الزيادات وقد أوضحه في فتح القدير ثم اعلم أن جهالة المعتق لا تخلو إما أن تكون أصلية وإما أن تكون طارئة ؛ فإن كانت أصلية وهي أن تكون الصيغة من الابتداء مضافة إلى أحد المذكورين غير عين فصاحبه المزاحم لا يخلو إما أن يكون محتملاً للإعتاق وهو ممن ينفذ إعتاقه فيه كقوله لعبديه أحدكما خر فالكلام فيه في موضعين الأول في كيفية هذا التصرف، والثاني في أحكامه . اه. أما كيفيته فقيل إن العتق معلق بالبيان ولا يثبت العتق قبل الاختيار إلا أنه ها هنا يدخل الشرط على الحكم لا على السبب كالتدبير والبيع بخيار الشرط بخلاف التعليق بسائر اهـ. ومثله في المعراج والتتارخانية وغرر الأفكار والعناية وهذا ظاهر ثم راجعت البدائع فوجدت ما ذكره المؤلف هو عبارتها بحروفها وهو مشكل فإن الموت بيان فموت الداخل يقتضي تعين الثابت بالإيجاب الثاني، ومن العجب ما كتبه الرملي حيث قال: قوله فيؤمر بالبيان وذلك لأن موت الداخل بيان للإيجاب الثاني فقط فبقي الأول منهما على حاله اهـ. فإنه غير ملاقٍ لما كتب عليه، نعم هو ظاهر على ما نقلناه عن الفتح وغيره ولعل نسخته موافقة لذلك.
And the author indicated that if this were in divorce, the ruling is likewise. He said in al-Hidayah: If this were in divorce, and they are non-consummated, and the husband died before specification, then from the mahr of the external woman, a quarter is reduced; from the mahr of the fixed woman, three-eighths; from the mahr of the internal woman, one-eighth. It is said: This is the statement of Muhammad. According to the two, a quarter is reduced. And it is said: It is also their statement. We have mentioned the difference and its complete branching in al-Ziyadat, and he clarified it in Fath al-Qadir. Then know that the ambiguity of the slave to be freed is either original or incidental. If original, it means the formulation from the beginning is added to one of the mentioned persons without specification, so the competing party is either possibly subject to emancipation (the one who can have his emancipation executed, like saying to his two slaves 'one of you is free'). So the discussion is in two places: first on how this disposal, second on its rulings. As for its nature, it is said that emancipation is suspended on specification, and freedom does not occur before choice, except that here the condition enters on the ruling, not on the cause, like tadbir and sale with option of condition, unlike suspension with other things. The same is in al-Mi'raj, al-Tatarkhaniyya, Ghurar al-Afkar, and al-'Inaya, and this is apparent. Then I checked al-Bada'i' and found that what the author mentioned is its exact wording, and it is problematic because death is a specification, so the death of the internal slave necessitates the specification of the fixed one by the second statement. And astonishing is what al-Ramli wrote: his statement 'he is ordered to specify' because the death of the internal slave is a specification only for the second statement, so the first remains pending. This does not match what was written; yes, it is apparent according to what we reported from al-Fath and others, and perhaps his copy agrees with that.
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage first draws an analogy between the emancipation case and divorce (talaq). If a husband says 'one of you is divorced' twice to three non-consummated wives and dies before specifying, the reduction of mahr (dower) follows a similar pattern: the external wife's mahr is reduced by a quarter, the fixed wife's by three-eighths, and the internal wife's by an eighth. There is disagreement on the exact fractions between Muhammad and the Sahibayn. The author then introduces a new topic: the types of ambiguity (jihāla) in the slave intended for emancipation. The ambiguity can be original (aṣliyya), where the wording from the start is ambiguous (e.g., 'one of you is free'), or incidental (ṭāri'a), which arises later. The text begins to discuss the original type, noting that the emancipation is suspended on specification and does not take effect before choice, but here the condition is on the ruling (the transfer of property) rather than the cause (the act of emancipation), similar to tadbir (conditional emancipation upon death) and sale with option. The author then critiques a passage from al-Bada'i', noting that death itself is a specification, and discusses a comment by al-Ramli. This sets the stage for a deeper discussion of how ambiguity and specification work in Hanafi law.

Key Terms
جهالة أصلية (jahāla aṣliyya): Original ambiguity in the emancipation statement from the beginning, e.g., 'one of you is free'
جهالة طارئة (jahāla ṭāri'a): Incidental ambiguity that arises after the statement
تعليق بالبيان (ta‘līq bi’l-bayān): Suspending the effect of the emancipation until the master specifies which slave he intended

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on original ambiguity (jahāla aṣliyya) in emancipation?
A) The emancipation is invalid.
B) The emancipation is suspended until specification.
C) The slaves are all freed.
D) The master must free all mentioned.

Key Takeaway
Original ambiguity in emancipation triggers a unique suspension (ta‘līq bi’l-bayān) where the condition is on the ruling, not the cause.

Death as a Clarifying Event in Ambiguous Manumission
Explains that death of one slave clarifies who is free in ambiguous manumission, with exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on death as clarification in ambiguous manumission and distinguish between implicit (hukmi) and explicit (sarih) clarification.

Core Idea
Death of one slave in ambiguous manumission clarifies the living slave as free.

When a master says 'One of you is free' without specifying which slave, the statement is ambiguous. The Hanafi school recognizes that certain events, like the death of one slave, serve as implicit clarification (hukmi bayan), resolving the ambiguity. This lesson explores when death clarifies, what distinguishes it from other events, and a related dispute about compensation for injuries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ambiguous manumission scenario
Understand the two contexts: immediate (e.g., 'One of you is free') and suspended (e.g., 'When Zayd comes, one of you is free'). The ruling on death's clarifying effect applies to both.
2
Distinguish insha and ikhbar
Manumission is an act of creation (insha), valid only for the living. Death ends insha, so the dead slave cannot be freed, leaving the other as the clear choice.
This is the key legal rationale.
3
Apply the ruling of death as hukmi bayan
Death of one slave frees the other, whether by natural causes or killing. If the master kills, no compensation; if a stranger kills, he pays the master.
If the master later frees the dead slave, it acts as acknowledgment, and the living remains free.
4
Contrast with amputation (qat' yad)
Amputation does not clarify because it does not remove the slave from the realm of life; freedom can still be intended for the injured slave.
This exception highlights the specificity of death as a clarifying event.
5
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on arsh
When a stranger injures one slave and the master clarifies freedom in the injured slave, al-Quduri said arsh goes to the master (qiyas of ta'liq), while al-Isbijabi said it goes to the slave (qiyas of tanjiz).
The practical difference is who receives compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من إنشاء عن شيء سابق والإخبار يصح في الحي والميت فيقف على بيانه بخلاف أحدكما [؟] والإنشاء لا يصح إلا في الحي. وأطلق في الموت فشمل القتل، سواء قتله المولى أو أجنبي، فإن كان القتل من المولى فلا شيء عليه، وإن كان من الأجنبي فعليه قيمة العبد المقتول للمولى، فإن اختار المولى عتق المقتول لا يرتفع العتق عن الحي ولكن يكون لورثة المقتول لأن المولى قد أقر بحريته فلا يستحق شيئاً من قيمته وقيد بالموت احترازاً عن قطع اليد فإنه لا يعتق الآخر، سواء كان القطع من المولى أو من الأجنبي. فإن كان أجنبي وبين المولى العتق في غير المجني عليه فالأرش للمولى بلا شك، وإن بينه في المجني عليه ذكر القدوري أن الأرش للمولى لا للمجني عليه. وذكر الأسبيجابي أن الأرش للمجني عليه وهو قياس مذهب التنجيز والأول قياس مذهب التعليق. وفي فتح القدير : وما يقع به البيان في العتق المبهم المنجز يقع به في العتق المبهم المعلق كأن قال إذا جاء زيد فأحدكما حر، فلو مات أحدهما قبل الشرط أو تصرف فيه بإزالة الملك ثم جاء زيد عتق الباقي. وفرق بين البيان الحكمي والصريح، فإن الحكمي قد رأيت أنه يصح قبل الشرط بخلاف الصريح فإنه لو قال قبل الشرط اخترت أن يعتق فلان ثم وجد الشرط لا يعتبر لأنه اختيار قبل وقته كما لو قال أنت حر إن دخلت هذه أو هذه ثم عين إحداهما للحنث لا يصح تعيينه. ولو باع أحدهما أو كلاهما ثم اشتراهما ثم جاء زيد ثبت حكم العتق المبهم فيعتق أحدهما ويؤمر بالبيان لأن زوال الملك بعد اليمين لا يبطلها ا هـ . وفي الاختيار : لو قال أحدكما حر فقيل أيهما نويت فقال لم أعن هذا عتق الآخر، فإن قال بعد ذلك لم أعن هذا عتق الأول أيضاً، وكذلك طلاق إحدى المرأتين بخلاف ما إذا قال لأحد هذين على ألف فقيل له هو هذا فقال لا يجب للآخر شيء. والفرق أن التعيين واجب عليه في الطلاق والعتاق فإذا نفاه عن أحدهما تعين الآخر إقامة للواجب، أما الإقرار لا يجب عليه البيان فيه لأن الإقرار للمجهول لا يلزم حتى لا يجبر عليه فلم يكن نفي أحدهما تعييناً للآخر.
From creation (insha) of something prior, and informing (ikhbar) is valid regarding the living and the dead, so it stops for clarification – unlike 'one of you two' [؟]. Insha is only valid for the living. He made it absolute in death, so it includes killing, whether the master kills or a stranger. If the master kills, nothing is upon him. If a stranger kills, he must pay the value of the killed slave to the master. If the master chooses to free the killed slave, the freedom does not lift from the living one, but it goes to the heirs of the killed, because the master has acknowledged his freedom, so he does not deserve anything from his value. He restricted it to death to avoid amputation of a hand, for it does not free the other, whether the cutting is by the master or a stranger. If it is a stranger and the master clarifies the freeing in the non-injured one, then the compensation (arsh) is for the master without doubt. If he clarifies it in the injured one, al-Quduri said the compensation is for the master, not the injured one. Al-Isbijabi said the compensation is for the injured one, and that is the analogy (qiyas) of the school of immediate (tanjiz), while the first is the analogy of the school of suspended (ta'liq). In Fath al-Qadir: What serves as clarification in immediate ambiguous manumission also serves in suspended ambiguous manumission – like if he said 'When Zayd comes, one of you two is free,' then if one dies before the condition or he disposes of him by removing ownership, then Zayd comes, the remaining one is freed. He distinguished between implicit (hukmi) and explicit (sarih) clarification. For the implicit, you have seen that it is valid before the condition, unlike the explicit: if he said before the condition 'I choose that so-and-so be freed,' then the condition occurs, it is not considered, because it is a choice before its time – like if he said 'You are free if you enter this or this,' then specified one of them for the oath (hanth), his specification is not valid. If he sold one or both, then bought them back, then Zayd came, the ruling of ambiguous manumission is established, so one is freed and he is ordered to clarify, because removal of ownership after the oath does not invalidate it. End quote. In al-Ikhtiyar: If he said 'One of you two is free,' and it was said 'Which one did you intend?' and he said 'I did not mean this one,' then the other is freed. If he later said 'I did not mean this one,' the first is also freed – similarly with divorce of one of two women, unlike if he said 'One of these two owes me a thousand,' and it was said to him 'It is this one,' and he said 'No,' nothing is owed by the other. The difference is that specification is obligatory in divorce and manumission, so when he negates it from one, the other is specified to fulfill the obligation. As for acknowledgment (iqrar), clarification is not obligatory because acknowledgment for an unknown is not binding, so he is not forced to do it, thus negating one does not specify the other.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-explanation from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It discusses how the death of one slave in an ambiguous manumission statement clarifies who is freed. The author begins by distinguishing between 'insha' (creation) and 'ikhbar' (informing) – manumission is an insha, valid only for the living, so death ends its possibility. However, if one slave dies, the ruling of freedom does not apply to the dead, so the living one is freed. This is for 'ikhbar' type statements where the speaker informs of a pre-existing freedom. The text then narrows to the case of death implying freedom for the other, even if the death is by killing. If the master killed, no compensation; if a stranger killed, he pays the master. But if the master chooses to free the dead slave, it is effective as an acknowledgment, and the living one remains free. The author contrasts death with amputation of a hand: amputation does not free the other because it does not remove the slave from human life. Then the passage discusses compensation (arsh) when a stranger injures one slave and the master clarifies freedom in the injured or non-injured. Two views are cited: al-Quduri (arsh for master) and al-Isbijabi (arsh for the injured slave), reflecting different qiyas for immediate vs. suspended manumission. The text then moves to Fath al-Qadir, explaining that the same clarifying events apply in suspended manumission (e.g., 'When Zayd comes, one of you is free'). Death before the condition frees the survivor. However, explicit specification before the condition is invalid, unlike implicit (hukmi) clarification which is valid. Sale and repurchase do not void the oath. Finally, from al-Ikhtiyar: if the master denies intention for one, the other is freed; subsequent denial frees the first too – unlike in debt acknowledgment where denial does not specify. The key distinction: in manumission and divorce, specification is obligatory (wajib), so denial effectively specifies the other. The passage is dense with legal principles and cross-references, demonstrating the Hanafi method of analyzing ambiguous expressions.

Key Terms
بيان حكمي (bayān hukmī): Implicit clarification: an event that legally determines the intended person without explicit verbal specification (e.g., death of one slave).
بيان صريح (bayān ṣarīḥ): Explicit verbal specification of the intended person, which is invalid if done before the condition in suspended manumission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a master says 'One of you two is free' and then one slave dies, what is the ruling?
A) Both slaves remain slaves because death invalidates the statement.
B) The living slave is freed because death clarifies the intention.
C) The heirs of the dead slave receive compensation from the master.
D) The master must make a new declaration to free the living slave.

Key Takeaway
Death of one slave in an ambiguous manumission statement frees the other, serving as implicit clarification (hukmi bayan), unlike amputation or explicit premature specification.

Intercourse as Clarification in Ambiguous Manumission: Hanafi Dispute
Explains that intercourse does not clarify ambiguous manumission according to Abu Hanifa; Sahibayn disagree.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on whether intercourse clarifies ambiguous manumission and state the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
Intercourse with one slave woman does not clarify ambiguous manumission according to Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn say it does.

When a master ambiguously frees one of two slave women, does his subsequent intercourse with one of them specify who is freed? The Hanafi school is divided: Abu Hanifa holds that intercourse is not a clarification, while his two disciples argue it is. This lesson unpacks their proofs, the preferred view, and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the legal issue
Identify the scenario: a master says 'One of you is free' to his two slave women, then has intercourse with one. Does this act determine which woman is freed?
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute; no external school involvement.
2
Identify the two positions
Abu Hanifa: intercourse is not a clarification (both remain slaves until verbal specification). The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): intercourse is a clarification, so the untouched woman is freed.
The mufta bihi is the companions' view.
3
Analyze each proof
Companions: intercourse is only permissible in ownership; since one is free, intercourse with one shows she is owned, so the other must be the freed one. Abu Hanifa: the statement is indefinite but the woman is specific, so intercourse is permissible and thus not clarifying.
The reasoning uses qiyas with divorce but distinguishes based on purpose.
4
Understand the tarjih
The text states the preferred view is that of the companions, and fatwa is given accordingly, due to caution (ihtiyat). Abu Hanifa's view is not given as fatwa despite his usual caution.
Tarjih authority: Al-Hidayah and others.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
If Abu Hanifa's view is followed, both remain slaves until a verbal clarification; if the companions' view, the untouched one becomes free immediately upon intercourse.
This affects the permissibility of subsequent intercourse and ownership.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (لا الوطء) أي لا يكون وطء إحدى الأمتين بياناً للعتق المبهم إذا لم يكن معلقاً عند أبي حنيفة . وقالا : لا هو بيان فتعتق الأخرى لأن الوطء لا يحل إلا في الملك وإحداهما حرة فكان بالوطء مستبقياً الملك في الموطوءة فتعينت الأخرى لزواله بالعتق كما في الطلاق، وله أن الملك قائم في الموطوءة لأن الإيقاع في النكرة وهي معينة فكان وطؤها حلالاً فلا يجعل بياناً ولهذا حل وطؤهما على مذهبه إلا أنه لا يفتى به ثم يقال : العتق غير نازل قبل إذا ماتت واحدة منهن فإن الميتة لا تتعين للحرية لأن الحرية هناك غير نازلة في إحداهن وإنما تنزل عند وجود الشرط وهو الاختيار مقصوراً عليه والمحل ليس بقابل للحرية وقت الاختيار، وفي هذا النوع البيان اظهار وتعيين لمن نزلت فيه الحرية من الأصل فلم تكن الحياة شرطاً؛ كذا في البدائع. البيان لتعلقه به أو يقال نازل في المنكر فيظهر في حق حكم يقبله والوطء يصادف المعينة بخلاف الطلاق لأن المقصود الأصلي من النكاح الولد وقصد الولد بالوطء يدل على استبقاء الملك في الموطوءة صيانة للولد، أما الأمة فالمقصود من وطئها قضاء الشهوة دون الولد فلا يدل على الاستبقاء وفي فتح القدير: الحق أنه لا يحل طؤهما كما لا يحل بيعهما وقد وضع في الأصول مسألة يجوز أن يحرم أحد أشياء كما يجوز إيجاب أحد أشياء كما في خصال الكفارة، وحكم تحريم أحد أشياء جواز فعلها إلا واحداً لأنه لو عمها فعلاً كان فاعلاً للمحرم قطعاً ولا يعلم خلاف في ذلك، وثبوت الملك قد يمتنع معه الوطء لعارض كالرضاع والمجوسية فلا يستلزم قيامه حل الوطء وقد أطال رحمه الله تعالى إطالة حسنة. والحاصل أن الراجح قولهما وأنه لا يفتى بقول الإمام كما في الهداية وغيرها لما فيه من ترك الاحتياط مع أن الإمام رحمه الله تعالى ناظر إلى الاحتياط في أكثر المسائل قيدنا الوطء بكونه غير معلق لأنها لو علقت . به عتقت الأخرى بالاتفاق. وقيد بالعتق المبهم لأن الوطء في التدبير المبهم يكون بياناً بالإجماع لأن التدبير لا يزيل ملك المنافع بخلاف العتق. وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لو قبلها أو لمسها أو نظر إلى فرجها بشهوة لا يكون بياناً بالأولى وهو على الخلاف كما في المحيط، وإلى أنه لو استخدم أحدهما طوعاً أو كرهاً لا يكون بياناً وهو بالإجماع لأن الاستخدام لا ينافي إنشاء العتق ولا يبطله الإنشاء لأنه لا يختص بالملك لأنه قد تستخدم الحرة فلا يكون بياناً دلالة ؛ كذا في المحيط قوله: (وهو والموت بيان في الطلاق المبهم) أي الوطء بيان للطلاق المبهم فتطلق التي لم يطأها كما إذا ماتت إحداهما تعينت الأخرى للطلاق، وقد قدمنا الفرق بين الطلاق والعتق ولا بد أن يكون الطلاق بائناً، أما لو كان رجعياً لا يكون الوطء بياناً لطلاق الأخرى لحل وطء المطلقة الرجعية. وهل البيان يثبت في الطلاق بالمقدمات في الزيادات لا يثبت وقال الكرخي : يحصل بالتقبيل كما يحصل بالوطء؛ كذا في فتح القدير . قيد بالوطء والموت لأنه لو طلق إحداهما ينبغي أن لا يكون بياناً لأن المطلقة يقع الطلاق عليها ما دامت في العدة فلا يدل على أن الأخرى هي المطلقة.
His statement: '(not intercourse)' – meaning intercourse with one of the two slave women is not a clarification for ambiguous manumission when it is not suspended, according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: No, it is a clarification, and the other is freed, because intercourse is only permissible in ownership, and one of them is free, so by intercourse he is maintaining ownership in the one he had intercourse with, so the other is specified due to removal of ownership by manumission, as in divorce. According to him (Abu Hanifa), ownership remains in the one he had intercourse with because the occurrence (iqa') is on an indefinite (nakira) while she is specified (mu'ayyana), so his intercourse with her is permissible, thus it does not serve as a clarification. Therefore, intercourse with both is permissible in his madhhab, except that it is not given as a fatwa. Then it is said: Manumission does not descend before... if one of them dies, the dead one is not specified for freedom because freedom there does not descend in one of them; it only descends when the condition is met, which is choice restricted to it, and the subject is not receptive to freedom at the time of choice. In this type, clarification is a manifestation and specification of the one in whom freedom descended from the beginning, so life was not a condition; as in al-Bada'i'. The clarification is attached to it, or it is said that it descends in the indefinite and appears in a ruling it accepts. Intercourse encounters the specified, unlike divorce because the main purpose of marriage is offspring, and intending offspring through intercourse indicates maintaining ownership in the one he had intercourse with to protect the offspring. As for the slave woman, the purpose of intercourse is satisfying desire, not offspring, so it does not indicate maintenance. In Fath al-Qadir: The truth is that intercourse with both is not permissible, just as selling both is not permissible. It has been established in the principles (usul) the issue that it is permissible to prohibit one of several things, just as it is permissible to necessitate one of several things, as in the expiation of kaffara. The ruling of prohibiting one of several things is that it is permissible to do all except one, because if he did all, he would certainly do the prohibited act, and there is no disagreement on that. The existence of ownership may prevent intercourse due to an impediment like fosterage or fire-worship, so its existence does not necessitate the permissibility of intercourse. He (the commentator) has elaborated well. The summary is that the preferred view (al-rajih) is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and that the fatwa is not given on the statement of the Imam (Abu Hanifa), as in al-Hidayah and others, because it involves abandoning caution (ihtiyat), even though the Imam looks to caution in most issues. We restricted intercourse to being not suspended because if it were suspended, the other is freed by agreement. And restricted to ambiguous manumission because intercourse in ambiguous tadbir (deferred manumission) is a clarification by consensus because tadbir does not remove ownership of usufruct, unlike manumission. The author indicated that if he kissed her, touched her, or looked at her private part with desire, it is not a clarification a fortiori, and it is based on the ikhtilaf as in al-Muhit. And if he employed one willingly or unwillingly, it is not a clarification by consensus, because employment does not contradict the creation of manumission and does not invalidate it because it is not specific to ownership – a free woman may be employed, so it is not indicative. As in al-Muhit. His statement: '(And it and death are clarifications in ambiguous divorce)' – meaning intercourse is a clarification for ambiguous divorce, so the one he did not have intercourse with is divorced, just as if one dies, the other is specified for divorce. We have previously mentioned the difference between divorce and manumission. And it must be a final divorce (ba'in); if it is a revocable (raj'i), then intercourse is not a clarification for the divorce of the other because intercourse with a revocable divorced woman is permissible. Does clarification in divorce occur through preliminaries (muqaddimat)? In al-Ziyadat it is not established. Al-Karkhi said: It occurs through kissing just as it occurs through intercourse. As in Fath al-Qadir. He restricted to intercourse and death because if he divorces one, it should not be a clarification, because the divorced woman's divorce occurs as long as she is in the waiting period, so it does not indicate that the other is the one divorced.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute over whether sexual intercourse with one of two slave women in an ambiguous manumission statement (e.g., 'One of you is free') serves as a clarification specifying which one is freed. The author presents the positions: Abu Hanifa holds that intercourse is not a clarification, so both remain slaves; but the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that it is a clarification, and the other woman is freed. The reasoning for each is given: the companions argue that intercourse is only permissible in ownership, and since one is free (by the ambiguous statement), intercourse with one indicates that he considers her his property, so the other must be the one freed. Abu Hanifa argues that the ambiguous statement is indefinite (nakira) but the woman is specific, so intercourse with her is permissible, hence it does not clarify. The text notes that according to Abu Hanifa, intercourse with both is permissible, but this is not given as a fatwa. The commentary then cites a distinction between manumission and divorce: in divorce, intercourse does clarify because the purpose of marriage is offspring, so intercourse indicates intent to keep the wife; in manumission, the purpose is merely satisfaction, so it does not indicate the same. The preferred view (al-rajih) is that of the two companions, and fatwa is given accordingly, as in al-Hidayah, because it shows caution (ihtiyat). The passage also notes that if the manumission is suspended (mu'allaq), there is no dispute – intercourse frees the other. For tadbir (deferred manumission), intercourse is a clarification by consensus. Other acts like kissing, touching, or looking with desire are not clarification (by a fortiori reasoning), and employment is not clarification by consensus. The last part discusses ambiguous divorce: intercourse and death are clarifications, but only for a final (ba'in) divorce, not revocable (raj'i). Clarification through preliminaries is disputed; al-Karkhi says kissing suffices. The text emphasizes that the reasoning for divorce differs from manumission because of the purpose.

Key Terms
وطء (waṭʾ): Sexual intercourse; here, with one of two slave women in an ambiguous manumission context.
بيان (bayān): Clarification determining which of the two ambiguous parties is intended for manumission or divorce.
عتق مبهم (ʿitq mubham): Ambiguous manumission where a master frees one unnamed slave among a group.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view (mufta bihi), if a master has two slave women and says 'One of you is free' and then has intercourse with one, which woman becomes free?
A) Both remain slaves because the statement is ambiguous.
B) The one with whom he had intercourse.
C) The one with whom he did not have intercourse.
D) He must make a verbal declaration to free one.

Key Takeaway
In ambiguous manumission, the mufta bihi is that intercourse with one slave woman frees the other, based on the caution-oriented view of the two companions.

Conditional Manumission with Unknown Birth Order
Ruling on a conditional manumission with twins of unknown birth order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a conditional manumission is tied to the first child's gender and twins of unknown order are born, and identify the legal consequences for each party.

Core Idea
Uncertainty in birth order divides freedom: the mother and female become half-free, the male remains a slave.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a classic case of conditional manumission (ta'liq al-'itq) where the condition is based on the firstborn's gender. When twins arrive and the order is unknown, the Hanafi school applies a nuanced ruling that balances the master's conditional right and the slave's potential freedom. The key principle is that each possible scenario must be considered, and the outcome that preserves both parties' rights is adopted through partial manumission and compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and the birth event
The master said: 'If the first child is male, you are free.' She gave birth to twins, a boy and a girl, order unknown.
The condition is valid (ta'liq sahih).
2
Consider the two possible birth orders
Scenario 1: male first. Scenario 2: female first. Each leads to different outcomes for the mother and female child.
The male child's status is the same in both.
3
Determine the mother's status in each scenario
If male first, condition met → mother free. If female first, condition not met → mother remains slave.
Uncertainty → she is considered half-free.
4
Determine the female child's status via taba'iyya
If male first, mother free at birth → female born free (dependency). If female first, mother slave → female born slave.
Uncertainty → she is also half-free.
5
Determine the male child's status
If male first, he is born to a free mother? No: the condition frees the mother, but does not free the child. If male second, born to slave mother. So in both cases, he is a slave.
He is definitely a slave.
6
Apply the rule of uncertainty and compensation
For the mother and female, since they are free in one scenario and slave in another, they are considered half-free and must perform sa'y (work) for the other half of their value to compensate the master.
This preserves both parties' rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو قال إن كان أول ولد تلدينه ذكر أفأنت حرة فولدت ذكر وأنثى ولم يدر الأول رق الذكر وعتق نصف الأم والأنثى) لأن كل واحد منهما يعتق في حال دون حال وهو ما إذا ولدت الغلام أولاً عتقت الأم بالشرط والجارية لكونها تبعاً لها لأن الأم حرة حين ولدتها، وترق في حال وهو ما إذا ولدت الجارية أولاً لعدم الشرط فيعتق نصف كل واحدة وتسعى في النصف . أما الغلام فيرق في الحالين فلهذا يكون عبداً ، وهذا الجواب كما ترى
His statement: (And if he said 'If the first child you give birth to is a male, then you are free,' and she gave birth to a male and a female, and it is not known which was first – the male is a slave, and half of the mother and the female are freed.) Because each of them is freed in one case but not the other. The case is: if she gave birth to the boy first, the mother is freed by the condition, and the girl as a dependent because the mother was free when she gave birth to her. And in the other case: if she gave birth to the girl first, the condition is not met, so half of each is freed, and she (the mother?) must work for the half. As for the male, he is a slave in both cases, so he is a slave. And this answer is as you see.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage is a specific ruling from the chapter on partial manumission. It presents a case: a master says to his slave woman 'If the first child you give birth to is a male, then you are free.' She then gives birth to twins – a boy and a girl – but it is unknown which was born first. Since the condition is based on the first child, the uncertainty leads to a complex outcome. The ruling: the male child is a slave in all scenarios. If the boy was born first, the mother is freed, and the girl is born free as a dependent of her free mother. If the girl was born first, the condition is not met, so the mother remains a slave, and the girl is also a slave (since her mother was a slave at birth). Because we don't know which scenario occurred, we apply the worst-case to the mother and the girl – they are presumed slaves, but since there is a possibility they are free, each is half-free and must work to compensate the master for the other half. This is a typical Hanafi approach: when uncertainty exists, the rights of both parties are partially preserved through compensation (s'ay/sa'y). The boy is definitely a slave because in both scenarios he is a slave: if born first, the condition is met and mother freed, but the boy himself is not freed by the condition (only the mother is), and if born second, he is born to a slave mother. So he remains a slave entirely.

Key Terms
تبعية (tabaʿiyya): Dependency: the female child is free if the mother is free at the time of birth (follows the mother's status).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a master says to his slave woman 'If the first child is male, you are free,' and she gives birth to twins (male and female) of unknown order, what is the status of the male child?
A) He is free because he might have been born first.
B) He is a slave in both possible scenarios, so he is a slave.
C) He is half-free like the mother.
D) He is free if born first, but since unknown, he is considered free.

Key Takeaway
When a conditional manumission depends on unknown birth order, the Hanafi school resolves the uncertainty by partially freeing those whose status is uncertain and requiring them to compensate the master.

Ruling on Ambiguous Manumission with Condition of Firstborn Child
Explains the ruling when a slave-girl gives birth to twins and the order is unknown.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal ruling when a slave-girl gives birth to twins after a condition linked to the firstborn male and explain how the shares of freedom are determined.

Core Idea
When the order of birth is unknown, ambiguity in the condition yields half-freedom for the mother and female twin.

The core matn of this passage presents a specific dilemma: a master conditions his slave-girl's freedom on the first child being male. She delivers twins—a boy and a girl—and the order is unknown. The text rules that the male remains a slave, while the mother and the female become half-free. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this nuanced outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Condition and Its Trigger
The master says: 'If the first child you give birth to is a male, you are free.' The condition is the birth of a male as the firstborn.
2
Recognize the Twin Scenario and Uncertainty
She gives birth to a male and a female twin, but the order of birth is unknown. Two possibilities exist: male first (condition fulfilled) or female first (condition not fulfilled).
3
Apply the Hanafi Principle of Ambiguity
In cases of uncertainty, Hanafi law splits ownership proportionally. Each scenario is equally probable, so half of the mother is considered free and half remains a slave. The female twin's status follows the mother because her freedom is tied to the same condition.
The male twin is not freed because the condition only applies to the mother.
4
Determine the Final Shares
The male twin is fully a slave. The mother is half-free (half of her value is freed). The female twin is also half-free, by extension.
This ruling is based on the principle of fairness in ambiguous situations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب العتق باب العبد يعتق بعضه
تلدينه ذكرا فأنت حرة فولدت ذكر وأنثى ولم يدر الأول رق الذكر وعتق نصف الأم
البيان لتعلقه به أو يقال نازل في المنكر فيظهر في حق حكم يقبله والوطء يصادف المعينة بخلاف الطلاق لأن المقصود الأصلي من النكاح الولد وقصد الولد بالوطء يدل على استبقاء الملك في الموطوءة صيانة للولد، أما الأمة فالمقصود من وطئها قضاء الشهوة دون الولد فلا يدل على الاستبقاء وفي فتح القدير: الحق أنه لا يحل طؤهما كما لا يحل بيعهما وقد وضع في الأصول مسألة يجوز أن يحرم أحد أشياء كما يجوز إيجاب أحد أشياء كما في خصال الكفارة، وحكم تحريم أحد أشياء جواز فعلها إلا واحداً لأنه لو عمها فعلاً كان فاعلاً للمحرم قطعاً ولا يعلم خلاف في ذلك، وثبوت الملك قد يمتنع معه الوطء لعارض كالرضاع والمجوسية فلا يستلزم قيامه حل الوطء وقد أطال رحمه الله تعالى إطالة حسنة. والحاصل أن الراجح قولهما وأنه لا يفتى بقول الإمام كما في الهداية وغيرها لما فيه من ترك الاحتياط مع أن الإمام رحمه الله تعالى ناظر إلى الاحتياط في أكثر المسائل قيدنا الوطء بكونه غير معلق لأنها لو علقت . به عتقت الأخرى بالاتفاق. وقيد بالعتق المبهم لأن الوطء في التدبير المبهم يكون بياناً بالإجماع لأن التدبير لا يزيل ملك المنافع بخلاف العتق. وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لو قبلها أو لمسها أو نظر إلى فرجها بشهوة لا يكون بياناً بالأولى وهو على الخلاف كما في المحيط، وإلى أنه لو استخدم أحدهما طوعاً أو كرهاً لا يكون بياناً وهو بالإجماع لأن الاستخدام لا ينافي إنشاء العتق ولا يبطله الإنشاء لأنه لا يختص بالملك لأنه قد تستخدم الحرة فلا يكون بياناً دلالة؛ كذا في المحيط قوله: (وهو والموت بيان في الطلاق المبهم) أي الوطء بيان للطلاق المبهم فتطلق التي لم يطأها كما إذا ماتت إحداهما تعينت الأخرى للطلاق، وقد قدمنا الفرق بين الطلاق والعتق ولا بد أن يكون الطلاق بائناً، أما لو كان رجعياً لا يكون الوطء بياناً لطلاق الأخرى لحل وطء المطلقة الرجعية. وهل البيان يثبت في الطلاق بالمقدمات في الزيادات لا يثبت وقال الكرخي: يحصل بالتقبيل كما يحصل بالوطء؛ كذا في فتح القدير. قيد بالوطء والموت لأنه لو طلق إحداهما ينبغي أن لا يكون بياناً لأن المطلقة يقع الطلاق عليها ما دامت في العدة فلا يدل على أن الأخرى هي المطلقة.
Book of Manumission, Chapter on the Slave Who Is Partially Freed. "You give birth to a male, so you are free, then she gave birth to a male and a female and it was not known which was first, so the male is a slave and half of the mother is free." Explanation is attached to it, or it is said that it is issued regarding the denier so it appears in the right of a ruling that he accepts. Intercourse applies to the specific [slave-girl] contrary to divorce because the primary purpose of marriage is children and intending children by intercourse indicates preserving ownership over the one with whom intercourse is had to protect the child. As for the slave-girl, the purpose of intercourse is fulfilling desire, not children, so it does not indicate preservation. In Fath al-Qadir: the truth is that it is not permissible to have intercourse with both of them just as it is not permissible to sell both of them. And it has been placed in the principles the issue that it is permissible to prohibit one of two things just as it is permissible to make obligatory one of two things as in the expiation alternatives. The ruling on prohibiting one of two things is that it is permissible to do all except one because if he did all of them he would definitely be doing the prohibited, and there is no known disagreement on that. The establishment of ownership may prevent intercourse due to an impediment like fosterage or Magianism, so its existence does not entail the permissibility of intercourse. And he prolonged—may Allah have mercy on him—a good prolongation. The conclusion is that the preferred view is theirs (the two shaykhs, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and that fatwa is not given according to the Imam's (Abu Hanifa) statement as in al-Hidayah and others because it involves abandoning precaution, even though the Imam—may Allah have mercy on him—looks to precaution in most issues. We restrict intercourse to being unconditional because if it were conditional, the other would be freed by agreement. And we restrict to ambiguous manumission because intercourse in ambiguous tadbir is clarification by consensus because tadbir does not remove the right of usufruct unlike manumission. The author indicated that if he kissed her, touched her, or looked at her private part with desire, it is not clarification a fortiori, and it is subject to disagreement as in al-Muhit. And that if he used one of them voluntarily or involuntarily, it is not clarification by consensus because usage does not contradict initiating manumission nor invalidate it because it is not specific to ownership since a free woman can be used, so it is not clarification by indication. Likewise in al-Muhit. His statement: (And intercourse and death are clarification in ambiguous divorce) meaning intercourse is clarification for ambiguous divorce, so the one he did not have intercourse with is divorced, just as if one of them dies the other is determined for divorce. And we have presented the difference between divorce and manumission, and divorce must be irrevocable. As for if it were revocable, intercourse would not be clarification for divorcing the other because of the permissibility of intercourse with the revocably divorced woman. And does clarification occur in divorce by preliminary acts? In al-Ziyadat it is not established, and al-Karkhi said: it occurs by kissing as it occurs by intercourse. Likewise in Fath al-Qadir. He restricted to intercourse and death because if he divorced one of them, it should not be clarification because the divorcée is subject to divorce as long as she is in her waiting period, so it does not indicate that the other is the divorcée.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq deals with ambiguous manumission where the condition is based on the firstborn child. The matn states a scenario: a master says to his slave-girl, 'If the first child you give birth to is a male, you are free.' She then gives birth to twins, a male and a female, and it is unknown which was born first. The ruling is that the male is a slave, and half of the mother and the female are free. The commentary explains the reasoning: the mother becomes half-free because if the male was first, she is fully free; if the female was first, she remains a slave. Similarly, the female is half-free because if she was first, she is free by the condition (since the condition only mentions male, but here the condition is different? Actually the condition is only about male; if female is first, the condition is not fulfilled, so mother and female remain slaves. The matn result of half freedom for both indicates the ambiguity. The commentary then compares with ambiguous divorce, explaining that in divorce, intercourse with a particular woman clarifies who is divorced, because the primary purpose of marriage is children and intercourse indicates a desire to preserve ownership for the child's sake. In manumission, however, intercourse does not indicate preservation because the purpose is desire, not children. The preferred view (rajih) is that of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), and fatwa is given accordingly, not according to Abu Hanifa, even though Abu Hanifa often prioritizes precaution. The passage also discusses other acts like kissing, touching, looking with desire as potential clarification, but these are disputed. Using one of the two slaves as a servant does not constitute clarification by consensus.

Key Terms
العتق المبهم (al-'itq al-mubham): Manumission where the specific slave to be freed is not identified, e.g., 'one of you is free.'
البيان (al-bayan): Clarification; an act that specifies which slave is freed in an ambiguous manumission.
الطلاق المبهم (al-talaq al-mubham): Divorce where the wife is not specified, e.g., 'one of you is divorced.'

Key Takeaway

Clarification (Bayan) through Intercourse in Ambiguous Manumission
Expands on the concept of bayan in ambiguous manumission via intercourse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether intercourse with one of two ambiguous slave-girls constitutes clarification and state the preferred view.

Core Idea
The Sahibayn consider intercourse as clarification; Abu Hanifa disagrees, but the mufta bihi is the former.

The passage expands beyond the matn to discuss how a master can resolve ambiguity in manumission. Specifically, does intercourse with one of two ambiguous slave-girls indicate which one is intended to be freed? This lesson dissects the dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and the ruling that prevails in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Set the Context of Ambiguous Manumission
The master says 'one of you is free' without specifying. The ambiguity remains until clarification (bayan) occurs. The text examines whether intercourse with one slave-girl can serve as bayan.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position
Abu Hanifa holds that intercourse does NOT clarify. His reasoning: the primary purpose of intercourse with a slave-girl is gratification, not children, so it does not indicate an intention to preserve ownership or to free her.
3
State the Sahibayn's Position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that intercourse DOES clarify. They analogize to divorce, where intercourse with one wife during ambiguity determines that the other is divorced. However, they note a difference: in marriage, intercourse aims at procreation, indicating a desire to maintain the marriage. In manumission, no such indication exists, but they still consider intercourse as bayan by way of istihsan (juristic preference).
4
Identify the Preferred View (Mufta Bihi)
The text declares that the preferred view is that of the Sahibayn, and fatwa is given accordingly. This is also supported by al-Hidayah.
5
Extend to Other Acts
The text also discusses whether acts like kissing, touching, or looking with desire constitute bayan. These are disputed, but using a slave-girl as a servant is not bayan by consensus.

تلدينه ذكرا فأنت حرة فولدت ذكر وأنثى ولم يدر الأول رق الذكر وعتق نصف الأم
البيان لتعلقه به أو يقال نازل في المنكر فيظهر في حق حكم يقبله والوطء يصادف المعينة بخلاف الطلاق لأن المقصود الأصلي من النكاح الولد وقصد الولد بالوطء يدل على استبقاء الملك في الموطوءة صيانة للولد، أما الأمة فالمقصود من وطئها قضاء الشهوة دون الولد فلا يدل على الاستبقاء وفي فتح القدير: الحق أنه لا يحل طؤهما كما لا يحل بيعهما وقد وضع في الأصول مسألة يجوز أن يحرم أحد أشياء كما يجوز إيجاب أحد أشياء كما في خصال الكفارة، وحكم تحريم أحد أشياء جواز فعلها إلا واحداً لأنه لو عمها فعلاً كان فاعلاً للمحرم قطعاً ولا يعلم خلاف في ذلك، وثبوت الملك قد يمتنع معه الوطء لعارض كالرضاع والمجوسية فلا يستلزم قيامه حل الوطء وقد أطال رحمه الله تعالى إطالة حسنة. والحاصل أن الراجح قولهما وأنه لا يفتى بقول الإمام كما في الهداية وغيرها لما فيه من ترك الاحتياط مع أن الإمام رحمه الله تعالى ناظر إلى الاحتياط في أكثر المسائل قيدنا الوطء بكونه غير معلق لأنها لو علقت . به عتقت الأخرى بالاتفاق. وقيد بالعتق المبهم لأن الوطء في التدبير المبهم يكون بياناً بالإجماع لأن التدبير لا يزيل ملك المنافع بخلاف العتق. وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لو قبلها أو لمسها أو نظر إلى فرجها بشهوة لا يكون بياناً بالأولى وهو على الخلاف كما في المحيط، وإلى أنه لو استخدم أحدهما طوعاً أو كرهاً لا يكون بياناً وهو بالإجماع لأن الاستخدام لا ينافي إنشاء العتق ولا يبطله الإنشاء لأنه لا يختص بالملك لأنه قد تستخدم الحرة فلا يكون بياناً دلالة؛ كذا في المحيط قوله: (وهو والموت بيان في الطلاق المبهم) أي الوطء بيان للطلاق المبهم فتطلق التي لم يطأها كما إذا ماتت إحداهما تعينت الأخرى للطلاق، وقد قدمنا الفرق بين الطلاق والعتق ولا بد أن يكون الطلاق بائناً، أما لو كان رجعياً لا يكون الوطء بياناً لطلاق الأخرى لحل وطء المطلقة الرجعية. وهل البيان يثبت في الطلاق بالمقدمات في الزيادات لا يثبت وقال الكرخي: يحصل بالتقبيل كما يحصل بالوطء؛ كذا في فتح القدير. قيد بالوطء والموت لأنه لو طلق إحداهما ينبغي أن لا يكون بياناً لأن المطلقة يقع الطلاق عليها ما دامت في العدة فلا يدل على أن الأخرى هي المطلقة.
Book of Manumission, Chapter on the Slave Who Is Partially Freed. "You give birth to a male, so you are free, then she gave birth to a male and a female and it was not known which was first, so the male is a slave and half of the mother is free." Explanation is attached to it, or it is said that it is issued regarding the denier so it appears in the right of a ruling that he accepts. Intercourse applies to the specific [slave-girl] contrary to divorce because the primary purpose of marriage is children and intending children by intercourse indicates preserving ownership over the one with whom intercourse is had to protect the child. As for the slave-girl, the purpose of intercourse is fulfilling desire, not children, so it does not indicate preservation. In Fath al-Qadir: the truth is that it is not permissible to have intercourse with both of them just as it is not permissible to sell both of them. And it has been placed in the principles the issue that it is permissible to prohibit one of two things just as it is permissible to make obligatory one of two things as in the expiation alternatives. The ruling on prohibiting one of two things is that it is permissible to do all except one because if he did all of them he would definitely be doing the prohibited, and there is no known disagreement on that. The establishment of ownership may prevent intercourse due to an impediment like fosterage or Magianism, so its existence does not entail the permissibility of intercourse. And he prolonged—may Allah have mercy on him—a good prolongation. The conclusion is that the preferred view is theirs (the two shaykhs, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and that fatwa is not given according to the Imam's (Abu Hanifa) statement as in al-Hidayah and others because it involves abandoning precaution, even though the Imam—may Allah have mercy on him—looks to precaution in most issues. We restrict intercourse to being unconditional because if it were conditional, the other would be freed by agreement. And we restrict to ambiguous manumission because intercourse in ambiguous tadbir is clarification by consensus because tadbir does not remove the right of usufruct unlike manumission. The author indicated that if he kissed her, touched her, or looked at her private part with desire, it is not clarification a fortiori, and it is subject to disagreement as in al-Muhit. And that if he used one of them voluntarily or involuntarily, it is not clarification by consensus because usage does not contradict initiating manumission nor invalidate it because it is not specific to ownership since a free woman can be used, so it is not clarification by indication. Likewise in al-Muhit. His statement: (And intercourse and death are clarification in ambiguous divorce) meaning intercourse is clarification for ambiguous divorce, so the one he did not have intercourse with is divorced, just as if one of them dies the other is determined for divorce. And we have presented the difference between divorce and manumission, and divorce must be irrevocable. As for if it were revocable, intercourse would not be clarification for divorcing the other because of the permissibility of intercourse with the revocably divorced woman. And does clarification occur in divorce by preliminary acts? In al-Ziyadat it is not established, and al-Karkhi said: it occurs by kissing as it occurs by intercourse. Likewise in Fath al-Qadir. He restricted to intercourse and death because if he divorced one of them, it should not be clarification because the divorcée is subject to divorce as long as she is in her waiting period, so it does not indicate that the other is the divorcée.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq deals with ambiguous manumission where the condition is based on the firstborn child. The matn states a scenario: a master says to his slave-girl, 'If the first child you give birth to is a male, you are free.' She then gives birth to twins, a male and a female, and it is unknown which was born first. The ruling is that the male is a slave, and half of the mother and the female are free. The commentary explains the reasoning: the mother becomes half-free because if the male was first, she is fully free; if the female was first, she remains a slave. Similarly, the female is half-free because if she was first, she is free by the condition (since the condition only mentions male, but here the condition is different? Actually the condition is only about male; if female is first, the condition is not fulfilled, so mother and female remain slaves. The matn result of half freedom for both indicates the ambiguity. The commentary then compares with ambiguous divorce, explaining that in divorce, intercourse with a particular woman clarifies who is divorced, because the primary purpose of marriage is children and intercourse indicates a desire to preserve ownership for the child's sake. In manumission, however, intercourse does not indicate preservation because the purpose is desire, not children. The preferred view (rajih) is that of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), and fatwa is given accordingly, not according to Abu Hanifa, even though Abu Hanifa often prioritizes precaution. The passage also discusses other acts like kissing, touching, looking with desire as potential clarification, but these are disputed. Using one of the two slaves as a servant does not constitute clarification by consensus.

Key Terms
العتق المبهم (al-'itq al-mubham): Manumission where the specific slave to be freed is not identified, e.g., 'one of you is free.'
البيان (al-bayan): Clarification; an act that specifies which slave is freed in an ambiguous manumission.
الوطء (al-wat'): Sexual intercourse; in this context, considered as a potential clarifying act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi, what is the effect of intercourse with one of two ambiguous slave-girls?
A) Both slave-girls become free
B) The slave-girl with whom intercourse occurred is freed
C) The other slave-girl is freed
D) Neither is freed; ambiguity remains

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on bayan via intercourse is resolved in favor of the Sahibayn: intercourse clarifies ambiguous manumission.
